There is a liberty granted to a christian, to fast at all times, not for the superstition of keeping the fast: but for the vertue of abstinence. For how else could chasti∣ty vncorrupt be kept among them? vnlesse she were vnderpropped with the pinching staies and props of continency. How shall they ap∣ply themselues to the scriptures? How shal they employ themselues to wisdom and knowledge, but by bridling the belly & abstinence? How shall one geld himselfe for the kingdome of heauen? vnlesse he cut off abundance of meates, vnlesse hee vse abstinency, as a seruant. This therefore is the maner of christian fasting. Heere wee may see plainelie, that those daies of fasting were obserued in Cyrils age, which our church vseth, and the same endes of fasting: that is, not for superstition, as though there were any holinesse in meates, but for continencie and chastitie, to tame the bodie, to bee more apt to study the scriptures: These were the endes for which christi∣ans fasted. But there is also (saith he) another kinde of religious fa∣sting, whose praise is set forth in the writings of some of the Apostles. For we find written in a certaine booke of the Apostles: Blessed is hee that fasteth, that he may sustaine the poore. This mans fast is verie ac∣ceptable to the Lord. And indeed worthely enough; for he imitates him that gaue his life for his brethren, &c. The which kinde of fast
also our gracious prince hath commanded of late, and our church hath practised. The same ende of fasting we may reade in those which they call the Apostles Canons, If any Bishop, priest,Can. 50 or Deacon shal abstain from mariage, flesh, or wine, not for this cause, that his mind should be made more fit to serue God, but because they are abhominable, &c. let him be thrust out of the church: as also any lay man. Heere is first the cause of abstinence, to tame the flesh: and of single life, to make the minde more apt to serue God. But both these since haue béene accompted steps to heauen, meanes of saluati∣on: And mariage in a minister; as also meates eaten at times, not by the pope prescribed, is abhominable. Ferus of this supersti∣tion of meates writes thus: So many amongst vs,In Ioh. ca. 18 pa. 487. 488. trusting to the ordinances of man, hereof do promise righteousnesse to themselues: in the meane time, nothing regarding the commandements of God. Against such the 23. chap of Matth. is of no lesse force, then it was in times past against the hypocrites, among the Iewes; who woulde not haue thought but that that people had beene holy, and to haue had a iust cause against Christ, which with such care & religion, kept the constitutions of the fathers? If they would not break the commā∣dement of a godly man: how much lesse are they to bee thought to breake the lawe of God? Here wee may see hypocrisie. But Christ taught vs another righteousnesse, when hee saide: O father, sanctifie them in thy truth. That is that true sanctification, when the father himselfe possesseth our heartes, and reneweth and lighteneth them, with the true knowledge of Christ, with faith and remission of sinnes. This holinesse flesh acknowledgeth not: but imagineth a certaine carnall holinesse, whereby it abstaineth from certaine meates, and meetings, and familiarity of certaine men. And surelie this was the superstition and counterfeit holinesse in poperie. Their Imber daies, foure times by the yeare,Pontacus Bur∣degal. in chrono an. Dom. 214. were first ordai∣ned by Calixtus, who at those times decréed yt orders shold be giuē to ministers, and that the people thorow the whole church (as it should seem) should pray & fast thē, that God would send good pastors into his church. But in those Imbers, now they neuer thinke on this. The Rogation wéeke was first ordained, because there was a great earthquake at Vienna, and Wolues and wilde beastes came in and slew men. And therefore they fasted and praied. Or as some o∣ther thinke, because all things then are springing, they pray God that
he would blesse the fruits of the earth, and crowne the earth with his goodnes. But their latter Rogations, were a matter of state ra∣ther then humilitie: euerie one kéeping his order, and follow∣ing the crosse. And here somtimes a surmised contempt of one go∣ing before another (as I haue heard) hath bred more malice that weeke,Exod. 17.10 Ios. 7.6 These beads be¦gan an. Dom. 1090. a new deuise. Polidor Virgil de inuent. rr. then a whole yeere after could salue againe. Their beades Peter the Ermit, a French man, inuented (as it shoulde séeme) to teach that we shoulde continue in praier. For so no doubt Moses continued in praier all the while Iosuah fought against Amalecke. And Iosuah himself, when as God was angry with Israell for Achans offence, rent his clothes, and fell vpon his face to the earth, euen till the eeuen-tide, before the Arke of the Lorde, continuing in prayer: and Elias praied seauen times,1. King. 18.44 Mat 26.38 before he obtained raine, and our Sa∣uiour saide the same praier thrice. As no doubt all these continued begging of God still the same thing chiefelie, as also the importu∣nate widow in the gospell, had but one suite to the Iudge, which she continued: so to continue in praier, or often to say the same prai∣er, is no sinne. But they haue taught of late that the saying or repeating ouer onely,Ex opere operato. of so manie aues, so manie pater nosters, and so many creedes, not vnderstoode (of the worke done as they saie) do obtaine remission of their sinnes. What shall I speake of all their abuses? Ferus also concerning their abuses, saieth thus: How many thinges haue the saintes ordained of a good intent,In Iud. ca. 18 Pal. 426. which we now see to bee turned partly into abuse, partly into superstition: let holidaies, ceremonies, Images, masse, monasteries, bee an exam∣ple. So that by Ferus iudgement, euen the principall partes of their religion are nothing else but abuses and superstition. There∣fore wee may saie of this Romish Babilon, of this daughter of Babilon (as Dauid saieth),Psal. 137.9, Blessed is hee that taketh thy young in∣fants, that is those things which the fathers in simplicitie suffered, (which in déed were the infants of poperie) and dasheth thē against the stones, that is, against the great rocke Iesus Christ. Oh would to God our catholiques at this day would do so: these yong imp and infants (as it were of poperie) in the church concerning cere∣monies, which the fathers then suffered, nowe beguiles manie: And thus craftelie poperie came in; and by little & little, al their su∣perstitions grew. They which haue eies to see, may see now, what vgly monsters they are grown vnto. They are so monstrous and so great, that many of them, euen their own fathers, and faous
do detest and abhorre: as you maie here sée. Wherfore let all other christians forsake them. Turning the grace of God into wantonnesse.Text.]  in the Gréeke, taketh his name of a citie called Salga (as some thinke) wherein all were vertuous and good, and therefore by a depriuati∣on, it signifieth all incontinencie, and the vnrulie affections of the minde, when as (like a wanton Heifer) it is not kept within the boundes of reason: and also, a merrie iest or fact. Such wan∣tonnesse, our flesh delighteth in; such fleshlie and carnall mirth, mans nature onelie loueth. But this wanton mirth, this carnall ioie, Gods worde condemnes.Ier. 9.23. Let not the wise man glory in his wisedome, nor the strong man glory in his strength, neither the rich man glory in his riches (saith the Prophet) much lesse in these vani∣ties: But let him that glorieth, glory in this, that hee vnderstandeth, and knoweth me (saith the Lord.) And S. Paul saith) Christ is made to vs of God, wisedome, righteousnes, sanctification, and redemp∣tion, that as it is written, he that reioiceth, let him reioice in the Lord.1. Cor. 1.30. So that here is the true ioie of christians, to remember that they haue such an excellent treasure, and gift giuen them of God; to remember these their spirituall riches of their soules; to remem∣ber these benefits of Iesus Christ. And therefore S. Paul saith of∣ten, reioyce in the Lord, that is in Iesus Christ,Phil. 4.4. who of God is gi∣uen to thee, with all his goods, with all his merites, with all that he hath. And againe, I say reioice. This is the true grace of God, this is euerie true christians ioy. But these counterfeite Catho∣liques, haue turned this grace of God into wantonnesse. For in Poperie, few knewe what Iesus Christ had done for them. Ma∣nie for lacke of knowledge of the scriptures, vnderstood not that Christ was made ours: and therfore could not reioice in the Lord. What was the sum almost of all their religion? but wantonnesse. For this reioicing and mirth in the Lord, they had other kinds of mirth and disports: but they were all wantonnesse. They had in those daies mirth enough, but fleshly, wanton, and carnall mirth. What shall wee accompte (to beginne first euen with their best things,) of their senselesse songs without all vnderstanding, of their curious deskants, of their sweete censing, of their costly or∣naments, of their statelie processions, where euerie man must keepe his place? What were all these? but plaine wantonnesse. All these were pleasant to the flesh; but nothing profitable to the
soule, nor delectable to the maiestie of God; Whose worshippe is not now, in such outward things (as our sauiour tolde the woman of Samariah,Io. 4.23.) but in spirit, that is, wish the hearte of man, and in truth, that is, not with any more Iewish ceremonies or shadows: then the which, the Popes religion was almost nothing else. The swéete perfume of frankinsence, the pleasant voice of man, the braue shewe of copes embrodered, delighteth man: but the ma∣iestie of God regardeth no such thing. Nay (our sauiour saieth) that which is highly esteemed amongst men,Luke 16.15. is an abomination be∣fore God. He respected more the plaine and simple mantle, with the faithfull and pure heart of Elias, then all the priestes of Baal, with their costlie vestementes and ornaments. But to let these passe, what were their pilgrimages, their guilde feastes, their feasts dedicated to euerie saint, who bare the name of any church, their feastes of euery arte and occupation once by the yeare, their bonefices, their maypoles, their bookes of fables, (in reading whereof they spent most of their time,) their dauncing, what were all these? but wantonnesse and fleshlie delights. And here note that the Apostle S. Iude saith, that these counterfeit christians shall not embrace wantonnesse onelie, or be giuen to it: but shall turne the grace of God into wantonnesse. They shall account these the chiefe pointes of religion: they shall make these their chiefe ser∣uice of God: as though they worshipped God by these thinges. This is to turne the grace of God into wantonnesse: and did not they so? It is too manifest. And here by the way, this is a speciall note, for euerie true ca∣tholique, that would not bee deceiued, to marke: not to looke on their religion,Reu. 6.8. as nowe they haue cloked it, and refined it: (They haue turned the black horse, in the reuelation, to a pale horse: they haue nowe for euerie grosse error, gotten a fine cloake, and for e∣uery abuse, some couering, & for euery superstition, some salue:) but to looke on it, as it hath béene vsed heretofore, in the daies of their forefathers. Let them not aske the Iesuites what is the popish saith, but let them aske those, which nowe yet liuing, can of their owne knowledge tell them: and then they shall plainly sée the na∣kednesse, the abominations, and superstition, and the blindnesse of it. And surely the lacke of this one thing, I am persuaded, se∣duceth verie manie at this daie. They embrace poperie, and euen marry themselues to her, in the attire and furniture, she now com¦meth
into the world: But they neuer remēber, nor consider, how deformed, how blind, how vaine, how wanton she hath béen. But is their wantonnes, these guildes, these drinkings, these their feasts, those vaine books, this masse or huge chaos of ceremonies, and against the word of God. S. Paul also prophesieth of this wāton religion. Preach thou the word (saith he) to Timothy.2. Ti. 4.2. For the time will come, when they will not abide that doctrine of health, that is, the word of God: but according to their owne lustes shall heape vp to themselues teachers: And shall turne their cares from the truth, and shall be giuen to fables. This heape of teachers, maie signifie the ackes and great multitude of their Friers, which they heaped to themselues, as their onelie teachers: to whome Christ in his gos∣pell, gaue neuer anie commission or authoritie to teach or preach to his flocke; but onely to pastors. And the truth is the word of God: as Dauid saith: Thy lawe is the trueth:Psal. 119.1. and these fables noe doubt, were their legendes, their Beuis of Hampton, their Valen∣tine and Vrson, and such like bookes, which they greatly delighted to reade in. And this is a marke of Antichristes religion, a plaine marke, and an onely marke. For thus we reade in S. Paul of An∣tichristes disciples:2. Thes. 2. v. 10.11. that sathan beguiled them in all manner of de∣ceiueablenesse of vnrighteousnes, because they receiued not the loue of the truth, that they might be saued. And therfore God sent them strong illusions, that they might beleeue lies; That all they might be damned, which beleeued not the truth, but had pleasure in vnrighte∣ousnesse. Let all men here beware, they which loue not the truth, that is, Gods word: but haue pleasure in fables, and lies; To those God shal send strong illusions, they shall be deceiued; naie they shal be dāned. Let all men beware how they loue not Gods word, how they delight in fables and tales, the danger is great. But marke what followeth, which is the onely cognisance or badge of all true christians: But we ought alwaies to giue thāks to God for you (saith the Apostle,) because that God from the beginning hath chosen you to saluation, through the sanctification of the spirit, and the faith of the truth. All Gods children beleeue the truth, and by it are saued, and therefore knowe it. Dauid saith,Psal. 1.2. The man is blessed that hath his delight in the lawe of God, and therein meditates day and night: Then he is accursed that delighteth in tales. And againe in an other psalme.Psal. 4.2. O ye sonnes of men (saith he) how long will ye haue such pleasure in vanity, and seeke after leasing? S. Peter also teacheth
all christians,1. Pet. 4. v. 2. that it is sufficient, that we haue spent the time past of our life, after the lustes of the Gentiles, walking in wantonesse, lusts, drunkennesse, glutony, drinkings, and such abominable idolatries: wherein it seemeth a strange thing to the heathen, that the christians will not keepe them company still; and therefore they speake euill of vs. But they shall giue account to him, that is ready to iudge both quicke and dead. Of these their often, vsuall, and excessiue f¦stings, and drinkings; which they account as nothing, which the heathen in their religion vsed, and nowe sathan hath brought a∣gaine into the church of Christ: this is Peters iudgment. Ban∣queting is accounted of S. Paul a worke of the flesh.Gal. 5.21. 1. Cor. 10.7. Exod. 32.6. The Idola∣ters after their worshippe of their calfe in Exodus, sate downe to eate and drinke, and rose vp to plaie. See if in poperie, they were not like these. So in Daniell, king Nabuchadnezars religion was all musicke,D. 3.5. & pleasant to the senses; marke if papists religion were not like this. And what is it then, but wantonnesse? which  S. Paul so often accounts among the workes of the flesh. Their vaine bookes also, which they delighted in, and which in séede of Gods booke (which sathan had hidde,2. King. 22.8. as in the daies of Io∣sias,) he had put in their handes, to finde them occupied withall, doe not these places of scriptures condemne? Our sauiour that tel∣leth the Iewes,Io. 8.44. yeare of your father the diuell, and the lustes and plea∣sure of your father ye will doe. He hath beene a murtherer from the beginning, and aboade not in the truth, because there is no truth in him. When he speaketh a lie, then speaketh he of his owne. For he is a liar, and the farther thereof. Here are two plaine markes, and badges of Sathans children: to delight in bloud, and in lies: hee was a murtherer, and a liar, from the beginning: and his chil∣dren followe his steppes. Why then lies, whatsoeuer, (either ly∣ing bookes or tales) are the impes and brode of sathan. And shall christians nourish them in their bosomes? And to likewise S. Paul teacheth all christians, howe they should walke and spende thou liues,Ephes. 5.2. Walke (saith he) in loue as Christ hath loued vs, and hath gi∣uen himselfe for vs to be an offering, and sacrifice of a sweete smel∣ling sauour to God. But fornication, and all vncleannesse or cour∣tousnesse, let it not bee once named among you, (as it becommeth saintes) neither filthinesse, nor foolish talking, neither iesting, which are things not comely: but rather giuing of thankes. If these things be not comelie for christians soules: that disorder, what vncom∣linesse,
that horrour was in their former times, in the soules of a great manie? when as nothing was vsed almost but these. And our sauiour saith, That of euery idle word,Mat. 12.30. we shall giue account at the day of iudgment: Howe then shall their idle and vaine bookes be iustified?In Praefat. Retract. Which of his faithfull seruants (saith S. Augustine) hath not Christ terrified, by this saying? It was one reason, that made him make his booke of Retractations. The Apostle S. Paul coun∣selleth all christians,Col. 3.16. that the word of God should dwell plenteous∣ly and richly in their houses: but they being affraide to entertaine that guest, which he commendeth vnto them, least they should take anie harme thereby, least it should make them heretiques (for so they haue saide) haue entertained the words of sathan, vaine and lying bookes; & so in stéede of Christ sathan hath dwelt with them: as their night walking spirits doe plainly prooue and testifie. Of Ceremonies. COncerning ceremonies,Acts 15.28. the Apostles would lay no more on the disciples necks, then necessary things. And S. Paul writes to the Galathians: Stand therefore in the liberty,Gal. 5.1. wherewith Christ hath made you free; and be not againe wrapped in the yoke of bondage. And what this bondage is, he declareth:4. Cap. 4.3. when we were children, we were brought in bondage, vnder the elementes of the world, that is, we serued God with manie ceremonies, and with earthlie thinges: which after he calles beggarly,Vers. 9. in respect of those pretious iewels of the heart, faith, loue, and knowledge, and such like: wherewith now we serue God. But the papistes haue taken wie this libertie, which Christ hath giuen vs: and haue multi∣plied in the church, the number of the Iewish ceremonies. They haue not laide vpon the disciples neckes, onely thinges necessary (as the Apostles did) but infinit thinges vnnecessarie; they haue turned from the right seruing of God, with knowledge, faith, and obedience to his worde. (which iewels they haue quite stolne away from Gods people & lost themselues also:) & haue returned againe to the beggarlie elements of the world, in seruing God, by offe∣ring
of egges, candles, and such like. The worshippe of Christians excelles the Iewes worship in two thinges: First because that, that is according to carnall ceremonies onelie in meates and drinkes,Heb. 9. and righteousnes according to the flesh: but the worship of christians, is according to the spirit. Secondlie, the worship of the Iewes was by shadowes: but the worship of Christians is in truth, & by it selfe pleaseth God. Thesauri noui sermones quadra∣gesimales, a popish booke so called, confesseth thus much. Prudentius also thus verie excellentlie pictures out christian faith, and idolatrie. In psychothae∣chia. Fidei & idololae∣iae Pugna.PRima petit campum dubia sub sorte duelli Pugnatura fides, agrestiturbida cultus, Nuda humeros, intonsa comas, exerta lacertos: Nam{que} repentinus laudis calor ad noua feruens Praelia, nec telis meminit, nec tegmine cingi; Pectore sed fidens valido, membris{que} retectis Prouocat insani frangenda pericula belli. Eccelacessentem collatis viribus audet, Prima ferire fidem veterum cultura Deorum. Illa hostile caput, phalerata{que} tempora vittis Altior insurgens labefactas, & oracruore De pecudum satiata, solo applicat, & pede calcat Elisos in mortom oculos, animan{que} malignam Fracta intercepti commercia gutturis arctat, Difficilem{que} obitum, suspiria longa fatigant. The same in English. VIctorious faith doth enter first. into the bloudie field; And like a valiant champion she will not flie nor yeeld. And though the'uent of cruell warre be subiect vnto doubt, Yet she doth come into the fielde
with courage bold and stout. She cloathed is, with vile attire, not pleasant to the eie, Her shoulders naked are, her haire doth out of orderlie. Her tender armes vnarmed are, They stand in steede of shield Her naked body to defend, not weapons for to weelde. For hope of praise doth so enflame and so enrage her heart, That she forgets to arme her selfe with buckler or with dart. But being of a courage bolde, not fearing perils any, With naked brest, she dare attempt to challenge dangers many. Behold the heathenish worshipping doth come with maine and might, Against her bending all her force, to put her to the flight: But faith amounting to the skies, doth wound her crested head, Her face she dashes on the ground and mouth with bloud beraide, Her eies she putteth out, her winde she stoppeth and her breath. Thus Gentilisme, wanting winde: doth see no way but death, In the reuelation, the name of that great whore of Babylon,Reu. 17. v. 5. the church of Antichrist; the mother of spirituall fornication of the ole earth: hath a mystery written in her forehead, because that all her religion should bee nothing; but mysteries, ceremonies, types, and shadowes. And was not the papistes so? All thinges that euer they vsed in their seruice were almost mysteries: Their apes, censors, ashes, paxes, albes, stoles, crosses, cruets, and chers, as their booke called [Rationale diuinorum] doth detiare.Rationale diui∣norum. And this name is written in her forehead, that all men maie read
and knowe it. And yet will they not knowe this whore? who rea∣deth not this name in her forehead? who séeth not, that popish re∣ligion was nothing else, but mysteries, ceremonies, types, and shadowes? Why then it must néeds follow, that the popish church is that great whore of Babylon, whereof S. Iohn speaketh. The name of a thing, alwaies declareth the thing it selfe. If it cannot be denied, but that this name is in her forehead, then no doubt this is she indéede. And this mysterie, these ceremonies, of that wickednesse (as it may be well expounded) began euen in S. Pauls time, and in the daies of the fathers. They began euen then to de∣part from the simplicitie of the gospell, & to put this yoake againe on the disciples neckes.Col. 2. v 8. Some went about to make christians shoote at a wrong marke, they brought in worshipping of Angels, they had euen then voluntary religion, in pinching their bodies too much, which thinges had a shewe of worldly wisedome. These speeches be∣gan to be in vse againe: Touch not, tast not, handle not, whereas by Iesus Christ, we were made free: we might touch and tast al things. And therefore (he saith) they holde not the head, that is Iesus Christ, and his doctrine, by whom all the body being knit together, by iois and bandes, groweth the growth of God. They growe and en∣crease: but not the growth or encrease of God: They growe not in the knowledge of our Lord Iesus (as Peter saieth:) they aske not counsell of their head,Euseb. lib. 3. eccl. Hist. cap. 37. in these thinges. Eusebius reporteth out of Egesippus, that as long as the Apostles liued, & the hearers of Christ himselfe, so long ye church continued a virgine: but after their deaths, this adulterer had wooed her and wonne her from Christ.Erasmus notes, that there hath been patching in the fathers workes also: Praefat. epist. 58. Aug. And doe we thinke she is a virgine still? The verie workes of Plinie and Seneca, being prophane writers, and the fathers workes; howe hath Sathan that olde deceiuer, the father of ignorance and blind∣nesse; obscured and darkened, and depraued? And do we thinke, that he hath not touched the work of God, his religion, his church? Yea no doubt especiallie he malignes that. In Apol.Bernard writing against the superfluous ornamentes of chur∣ches saies thus: I let passe the great staelinesse of churches, their immoderat lengths, their vaine breadths, their sumptuous polishings, their curious paintings, which while they do draw the sight of thē that pray, vnto them, they hinder their affection, and they seeme to me to resemble the olde custome of the Iewes. Marke howe Bernards saith, that those thinges, which nowe a daies the Popes defend
saie, were ordained to help deuotion; as guilded images & costlie ornaments, Bernard: saith, they hinder it: & that they tast rather of Iudaisme then Christianisme. He in those thick clouds of papisti∣ll ignorance, sawe thus much: and manie nowe in the cleare light of the gospell, will hardly acknowledge the same. And to his agrées Ierom in his Epistle to Nepotian: concerning the life and conuersation of the cleargie. Iewrie had a rich temple,Ierom. Part. 3. Epist. Tract. 3. Epist. 7. and all thinges then made of golde. Then those thinges were allowed of the de. Of the Popes supremacie. DEnying the onely maister of his house and our Lorde Iesus Christ.] And here first concerning the word ,Text. Saint Peter vseth it for the master of a familie:1. Pet. 2. v. 18. Seruants (saith he) be subiect , to your masters, with all feare. And S. Paul also speaking of seruants, saith thus: Let as many seruants as in vnder the yoke, account , their own masters worthy of all honour. And againe, they which haue , faithfull masters, let them not despise them.2. Tim. 2.21. And in another place, comparing the Church of God to a house, and some of the members thereof, to vessels sealed, hauing Gods marke vppon em; and some other therein, to vessels vnsealed, filthie and wic∣ked: If (saieth he) one shall cleanse himselfe from these wicked ones, he shall be a vessell of honor sanctified, , to the master or land of the house. All those places prooue plainly and sufficientlie, at in the scripture this word  is taken for the master of the house. Then the wordes lie thus in the Gréeke and common translation.Although this word God, in the common translation & in some greeke copies, is not read. [Denying the onely master of his house God and our Lord Iesus Christ.] And S. Peter in his Epistle ioineth this word  to Iesus Christ most plainly, and not to God: Denying (saith he) their master or ruler that bought them Iesus Christ. So that   signifieth a master of a house, or a ruler or gouer∣nour. And S. Peter saith, that this master is Iesus Christ. And S. Iude th, that it is he alone. Therefore then, to denie Iesus Christ to be the onelie master, the onelie ruler or gouernour: is a plaine  of false catholique religion.
2. Pet. 2.1And of the same heretickes S. Peter speaketh, to confirme the certaintie of them, that there shall be such in déed: that as  Sauiour saith,Mat. 18.16 in the mouth of two or three witnesses, euery worde might stand. And first he taketh away that great stumbling loc out of the waie, which causeth verie many to fall, that the vissible church cannot erre: yes (saieth Peter) there were false prophets in the law,2. Pet. 2.1 euen as also amongst you shall be false teachers. And these false prophets in the lawe, bare the shewe, they caried the counte∣nance of the church.1. King 22.24 Iere. 38.6 Amos. 7.13 Poore Ieremy, and Amos, and Micah were no body amongst them: Ieremy was cast into the dungeon, Amos was discharged the kinges chappell; Micah was stricken on the face. And euen such false doctors shall bee in the church of Christ. Therefore let euerie one take heede. The deuill shall haue these his mightie Goliahs, as well in Christs Church, as in the sina∣gogue:2. Pet. 2.1 Therefore let not the outwarde shewe, or name of the church beguile vs, as it did many in those daies. And they shal bring in craftly and subtilly heresies of perdition, that is, they shall be soldiours of that great Goliah and champion, the sonne of per∣tion: whom S. Paul speakes of, whose captaine and chiefe heade is antichrist himself.2. Thes. 2.11 Whom as Paul there describeth: so S. Peter  S. Iude here describeth his members. Now their heresies follow, they shall denie their master, (where is the same worde that S. Iude vseth) which bought them. They shall establish another master ouer the church, ouer Gods house, that is, the Pope. This shall be the roote, the ground worke of all their heresies; and after that, they shall denie Iesus Christ, that bought them. And hath it not beene see? For after the supremacie was once established, howe hath Idolatrous worshipping of images, selling of pardons, and masses, and merits of Monkes and Friers, and such like, com∣en into the church, who séeth not? This other principall branch hangeth of this; They shal deny their master that bought them, they shall deny Christes merits, his raunsome to be sufficient. They shall ad vnto it, mony of their own coining, that is, their own merits & works. And this is the very sum of poperie: to make men beleeue, that Christ hath not suffici∣ently paid their ransom: but yt they must buie their pardons, their masses, their merits, to deliuer their soules out of purgatorie.  not this to denie their master that bought them? If hee paide the whole ransome sufficientlie, what néede wee buie anie of these of
them? And they shal bring vpon themselues suddaine destruction.2. Pet. 2.] If men will not be perswaded that these are they, whome the Apo∣stle speaketh of, by tasting their fruites: let them marke their end, and that shall make the matter more manifest. They shall bring on themselues suddaine destruction: As one who but a little mar∣keth the histories of our time shall easelie perceiue. The Pope here in England, by dispensing against the word of God, that the brother might marry his brothers wife: In Germanie, by sending  Tetzelius with his pardons of remission of sinnes, to all that would buie them: Cardinall Wolsey with vs, by beginning first to pull down all smal religious houses, that were vnder the value of a hundreth marks, that he might build his two colleges: The monkes and friers, by one accusing another to the kinges com∣missioners, in that generall visitation, of most grieuous sinnes and crimes. All these haue pulled (as they say) the house on their ne head, and haue ouerthrowne the popes kingdome: and that odainlie, in a short time, against all mens expectation. All the rebellions and counsels which haue béene since, could neuer salue it againe. And many shall follow the way of their riot or wantonnesse.2. Pet. 2.2 This is the same which Iude prophecieth: their religion shall be carnal, worldly, wanton, and many shall imbrace it. Here let them brag of their multitude: that therefore their religion is good, because manie follow it. But this is no good argument. For wee reade here that many shall follow these false teachers; wherfore let not ye number or multitude deceiue any in matters of religion.2. Pet. 2.2 And by thē the way of truth shall be blasphemed, shal be reproched. They shame not to speake euill of the word of God, and to call vs gos∣pellers in despite, and our newe gospell preachers. Neuer here∣tickes haue written so scoffinglie, so despitefullie; as of late they haue done: As master Hardings speeches, (your deuilish spirit,Hardings rai∣ling. your solemne praier protestant-like, your minister-like talke, your minister∣ships) do declare: wherein he blasphemeth the spirit of God, where∣by wee confesse Iesus Christ faithfullie and effectuallie.1. Cor. 12.3 For (as S. Paul saith) No man can name Iesus Christ, but by the holy ghost: and whereby we make our praiers vnto God,Rom. 8.26 for no man can pray as hee oft to pray of himselfe; but the holy ghost helpeth our infirmities. And therefore he that scoffeth at our praiers, blasphemes the ho∣lie ghost, which is the authour of them. And lastlie, he blasphemes
that sacred name of minister,1. Co. 3.5 and 4. vers. 1 which the worde of God so often v∣seth; and S. Paul is not ashamed to giue to himselfe. And are not these blasphemies against the word of truth? Is not this plaine? This their owne writings testifie: and thus they doe apparantlie be wraie themselues. And through couetousnesse with faire wordes they shall make merchandize of you:2, Pet. 2.3 And haue not the Papistes done so? selling all thinges, euen their pardons, their praiers, their masses, their merits. And is not this couetousnesse? Doe not all these pointes of doctrine, these markes to know them by, hit iustly vpon them? Doth not S. Peter and S. Iude agrée in the disciphering and discouering of them? But to returne to S. Iude againe, doe not our false catholickes at this daie teach this? Doe they not saie that the pope is Christs vicar generall or vicegerent? and that he is also a necessarie head of the church? Do they not plainlie agree, with those whom Saint Jude speaketh of: Who shall deny Christ to bee their onely master, the ruler or gouernour of his house, which is the Church? So that then Iesus Christ is the onelie head of his church, the onelie ma∣ster of his familie himselfe: Hee giueth this honour to no other. And to denie this, is heresie: it is not christian religion, it is not the catholique faith. And this prerogatiue here spoken of, S. Paul giueth to Iesus Christ, in his Epistle to the Ephesians, who spea∣king of the great glorie, wherewith God hath endued him after his resurrection,Ephe. 1.22 saith: He hath put all things vnder his feet: and he hath giuē him to be ye head ouer al ye whole church, which is his body: the fulnesse of him which filleth all things, with al things. As no man may seeme to take to himself the former priuiledge, that al things are put vnder his féete; so no man may presume to take the lat∣ter, that he is the head of the whole church. Againe the metaphor, which the Apostle vseth, conuinceth the same; he calleth Christ the head, and the church his bodie: Nowe it is monstrous, that one bodie should haue two heads; wherefore in this verie point, the summe and meaning of this metaphor consisteth. Againe in his second chapter,Verse. 20 he calleth him the head corner stone, which is but one in euerie building.Verse 29 Io. 3, 29 And in his fourth chapter, the husband of his church, which also (as all men knowe) argueth, that hee is the onlie husband, and can abide no companion with him. And in his epistle to the Hebrues,Heb, 3.5. he compareth him with Moses: That as Moses was in the house of God as a seruant; so now Iesus Christ is o∣uer
the house of God as the sonne. And this taketh away,Christ is here opposed to Mo¦ses: And the greater alwaies includes the les¦ser, and som∣what more: so is Christ ouer the church at Moses was, and more. Heb. 3. v. 6 as may seeme, that vaine distinction of a ministring heade, which they make. For Moses was in Gods house but as a ministeriall heade: and euen so nowe is Iesus Christ ouer Gods house, as the onelie heade both chiefe and ministeriall. He succéedes Moses in farre greater dignitie and honour, hee is nowe all in all. And as the Apostle there putteth downe, the onlie maister and ruler of the house and church of God, euen the sonne Iesus Christ:  he setteth downe two plaine and infallible markes and conditi∣ons of Gods house, least any man should be deceiued, by setting himselfe in sathans Sodome, for Gods Bethel; as it is to be fea∣red, manie doe at this daie. Heere is that great doubt dissolued, which is the true church. If anie man would but a little heere marke, hee shoulde see two euident signes, and tokens of Gods true church and house, which are these. But Christ as the sonne is o∣uer his house: whose house wee are (saith the Apostle) if so be, wee keepe sure or firme our confidence, and the reioicing of our hope, vn∣to the ende. Here is first the heade and master of the house, Iesus Christ; 2. then the house it self (we) that is Gods people: then fol∣loweth the conditions, If wee keepe that confidence and assurance: and that reioicing of our hope, firme and sure vnto the ende. Marke well these conditions of Gods church. They which kéepe not these, are none of Gods church. The holie ghost hath put them downe for our instruction, least we should be deceiued. Because the time shall come, that manie shall saie, they are of the catholique church: If they be, here be the markes they must be knowne by. If they lacke these markes, they are no doubt, none of Gods house: but of sathans sinagogue. These are the vndoubted markes and bad∣ges which God himselfe hath giuen to his house. But you will saie, what is that confidence, and that reioicing? Surelie Saint Iohn in his first Epistle telleth vs. This (saith he) is our confidence,1. Iohn, 5.14 this is our assurance, (where the same word  here vsed, is repeated) that we haue to him, that is to Iesus Christ, that whatsoe∣uer we aske, according to his will, he heareth vs: and if we know he heareth vs, whatsoeuer wee aske, wee knowe we haue our petitions which we aske of him. Here are two points of our assurance, we knowe first, and are sure, that what praiers soeuer wee make in the name of Iesus Christ, according to his will; hee heareth vs:
and not that onelie, but 2. we are sure that he granteth our petiti∣ons.Psal. 65.2.8 6.7 This same assurance is confirmed vnto vs, by other two places of scripture. Thou that hearest the praiers, vnto thee shal al flesh come (saith Dauid.) And in an other place: In the time of my trouble I will call vpon thee, for thou hearest me. And S. Paul saith, The spirit also helpeth our infirmities.Rom. 8.16 For we know not what to pray as we ought to pray: but the spirit it selfe maketh intercession for vs, with gronings that are vnspeakeable. And hee that searcheth the hearts knoweth the meaning or wisdome of the spirit. For euen to God, according to the will of God, it maketh intercession for the saints. So that we are sure God heareth vs, and therefore al flesh commeth to him; and therefore in troubles we crie vnto him. And therefore he is called, , the searcher of the hearts, he knoweth the meaning,Acts. 1.24 the wisdome of the spirit; and none other neither angell nor saint, but hee. This assurance the popish church hath denied. They saie, Iesus Christ doth not heare vs, and there∣fore they counsel vs to make other intercessors to him. Secondlie they teach vs to doubt, whether wee haue our praiers wee aske of him or not; as when we pray for remission of our sinnes. Nay they teach to praie, but in latine: So that he that praieth, knoweth not himselfe, what he asketh; and therefore cannot be assured whether he haue his petitious or not. And is not this plainlie to denie this christian assurance, and great confidence, that euerie christian ought to haue; & so to blot out this first marke of Gods house? Se∣condlie, the reioicing of our hope is, in yt, that we shal surely be sa∣ued. This hope maketh vs reioice alwaies, euen in tribulations, euen in chaines, euen in death it selfe. This ioie our sauiour tea∣cheth vs by his Apostles. Reioice (saith he) not that diuels are sub∣iect to you;Luk. 10.21 but that your names are written in the booke of life. And S. Paul: Being iustified by faith, wee haue peace with God, by our Lorde Iesus Christ, by whom also we haue an entrance to this grace, wherein we stand,Rom. 5.1 and reioice for the hope of the glory of God. And S. Peter in his catholique epistle, to all true catholiques writeth thus: Blessed be God, and the father of our Lord Iesus Christ, who according to his abundant mercy hath begotten vs againe to a liuely hope,1. Pet. 1.3 by the resurrection of Iesus Christ from the deade, to an inheri∣tance, incorruptible, vndefiled, and that neuer fadeth away, kepte for you in heauen; which are kept by the power of God, through faith, to saluation, ready to be reuealed in the last time; wherin you reioice.
All true Catholiques will beléeue S. Peter, and will be sure, and will haue a liuelie hope of their saluation, and will blesse & praise God for it, and will reioice in it.Nehem. 8.10. And Nehemias taught all the Iewes this ioie. The ioie of the Lord (saieth he) is your strength. Oh reioice in the Lord then, if thou wilt be strong. I haue written these thinges (saith S. Iohn) to you,1. Io. 5.13. which beleeue on the name of the sonne of God, that you may knowe you haue euerlasting life, and that you may beleeue in the name of the sonne of God, He that know∣eth that he hath euerlasting life, doubteth not, as before is more at large noted on this place. And againe, here is the cause  make vs beléeue on Iesus Christ, that we maie knowe we haue euerlasting life. The knowledge, yt faith bringeth, which is of eter∣nall life, will make euery one pray for faith, labour for faith, heare the word of God diligentlie, yt he may haue faith. But the papists take this reioycing from vs, by teaching vs to doubt: for he that doubteth, whether he shall be saued or not; can neuer reioice, can neuer be merrie: and therfore they are none of Gods house. Thus euerie one maie see plainlie, how the popish Church hath lost both these markes of Gods house, and therfore their church is none of Gods church. This preheminence in the Church of God, to be the only head, ruler and gouernour thereof; all the scriptures, and all the saints of God, yeelde to Iesus Christ.1. Pet. 5.4. Peter himselfe yéeldeth it to him whome he calleth , the prince of pastors, and himselfe a fellowe elder, not a fellow Apostle. Making himselfe equall, not with the Apostles of Christ onely; but with the elders and pastors of ye congregation: and who will not beléeue a mans own words? If this be true, then the Pope, by Peters priuiledge, can haue no superioritie ouer other Bishops. And S. Paul reckoning vp the chiefe Apostles, names Iames, Cephas and Iohn,Gal. 22. whome he calleth pillers; not corner stones or heads: and he placeth Peter among the rest, not as one aboue the rest. Nay hee maketh himselfe e∣quall to him, or rather farre aboue him: For (hee saieth) that God gaue him like and equall authoritie, ouer the gentiles; as Peter had ouer the Iewes. Now the Gentiles were farre more in number, then the Iewes: And Iames, Peter and Iohn confessing this, and ac∣knowledging it, ioyned hands of fellowship with him. Here is no superioritie,Rom. 15.16. but an equalitie or fellowship acknowledged of them all. And of this his authoritie ouer the gentiles: Paul himselfe
after often maketh mention, euen to the Romans in Peters chiefe charge, as they would haue it: I haue written to you more boldly (saith he) after a sort, putting you in remembrance; for the grace gi∣uen to me of God, that I should be a minister of Iesus Christ towards the Gentiles. This his ministerie, this his office, committed to him of God, of preaching the gospell among the Gentiles, made him bolde to write to the Romaines. And to the Ephesians hee writes thus:Ephes. 3.3. For this cause, I Paul a prisoner of Iesus Christ, for you Gentiles: if ye haue heard of the dispensation or stewardship, of the grace of God giuen me to you ward.1. Ti. 2.7. And to Timothy, he calleth himselfe the Doctor or teacher of the Gentiles in faith and truth. Why then, Peter was not pastor of the vniuersall church, Paul was steward ouer the Gentiles and their chiefe pastor. And in that thréefolde commission of Christ,Io. 21.15. Feede my sheepe, feede my lambes, feede my sheepe, were not the shéepe of the whole worlde: but of the circumcision onelie committed to Peters charge, as that place before recited to the Galathians,Gal. 2. v. 7. plainlie prooueth. For when they sawe, that the gospell ouer the vncircumcision, was com∣mitted vnto me, saieth Paul: as the gospell ouer the circumcision was to Peter, they gaue to me and to Barnabas, the right handes of fellowshippe,1. Pet. 5.1. The Iewes con∣tended with Peter concer∣ning his going to the Gentils, and he yeeldes an account to them: which argues no su∣premacie. Acts. 11. v. 2. Ro. 15. v. 15. 16. Cypr. lib. 2. Epist. Epist. 10 & 11. that we should preach vnto the Gentiles, and they vn∣to the circumcision. And hereof no doubt, Peter calleth himselfe Compresbyter, making himselfe equall with the other pastors. And here, what can be more euident, for a mans owne estate and dignitie, then the testimonie of his owne mouth? and not onely that, but his re∣cord in writing to all posteritie: Euerie man will speake best of himselfe: Nay surely Peter had sinned, if he had not both fulfilled, and also challenged that authoritie, that Iesus Christ had com∣mitted to him. Gods commandements and charges maie not be omitted. Hereof also Paul writes to the Romanes more boldlie, because God gaue him that grace, that he should bee , a common pastor, among the Gentiles Paul challengeth this his authoritie, euen in the church of Rome. Hereof Cyprian calles Cornelius Bishoppe of Rome;He makes the Bishoppe of Rome fellow Bishop with other Bishops calling them a Collegas nostros. Collega, or fellowe Bishoppe. He would not so haue forgotten himselfe, to haue matched him∣selfe with the Bishop of Rome, if he had acknowledged anie such péerelesse authoritie in him, as nowe the Pope challengeth. Nay, as it were to quite crosse this succession of Peter, and to maintaine
this equalitie of the Bishoppes: manie of the fathers doe make two bishops of Rome, Peter and Paul,Epiph. haer 27. Prud. Peristo∣phanon. as Epiphanius and Pruden∣tius. So that Paul had as good authoritie as Peter there, as should séeme: Therefore Peter could not conferre the whole authoritie to his successors, which he had not himselfe. All Christes ministers here on earth, are his vicars. For hee saieth of them all, Hee that receiueth you, receiueth mee; and he that receiueth mee,Mat. 10. v. 4. recei∣ueth him that sent me. But he is the head only himselfe; as long before him prophesied Oseas:Oseas 1.11. I wil gather (saieth the Lord) the sons of Iudah and the sonnes of Israell together, and they shall appoint them one head, and they shall ascend from the earth. Here is Ie∣sus Christ, the onely head of his church: here is the vnitie of the church, and their conuersation nowe in heauen. This is Catho∣lique doctrine; they which denie this, are not true, but false catho∣liques. This all Gods saints haue confessed. This doctrine con∣tinued in the church manie yeares: as wee maie plainly sée by reading histories; whereof one notable historie,Lib. 5. eccl. Hist. cap. 24. Eusebius repor∣teth thus. When as a controuersie did arise in the primitiue church, about keeping Easter, Ʋictor Bishop of Rome (pertinaciùs agens) as Ruffinus translateth, that is dealing obstinately, and frowardly, as one that would not yeeld: did goe about to excommunicate all the Bi∣shops of the East church, because they dissented from the Romaine church. But this pleased not the Bishops, but rather writing to him againe, they commanded him, that he should go about such thinges, as concerned peace, and that he should care for peace and concord. To be short, their letters bee extant, in which they did chide Victor very sharpely, as taking small care for the profit of the church. And Irenzus with the Bishops of France, whome he was chiefe ouer, re∣prooueth Victor; that he hath done amisse, in excommunicating so many churches, which obserued the custome deliuered them, of their elders. And after he writes thus: All they, which before Soter were elders of the church, which thou now rulest, (I meane Anacletus, Pi∣us, Higinus and the rest) had peace with these churches. This histo∣rie prooueth, that Victor dealt frowardly, as one that would not yeelde to anie, that they commanded him, that they chidde him sharpelie and reprooued him: and that Irenaeus maketh the Church of Rome, a particular church, that he calleth it not the vniuersall. If this be true, where was then this péerelesse authoritie, that now is practised? that the Pope maie bee iudged of none, that none
maie saie to him,Hist. Tripartita. Lib. 5. ca. 17. why doe you so? That dialogue also, betwéen Constantine the Arian Emperour and Liberius, maie prooue the same thing: We (saith the Emperour) because thou art a christian, and the Bishoppe of our citie, haue thought it meete, that calling for thee, we should giue thee warning, to forsake the communion of wic∣ked Athanasius. For that the whole worlde hath decreed, and the Councell hath excommunicated him. And when as Liberius had replied, that the Ecclesiasticall iudgments should be executed with great iustice; and that an excommunication should be had, Atha∣nasius himselfe being called before him: The Emperour still vrgeth, the whole world hath condemned his wickednesse. And after hee saith to him: Quota pars es tu totius orbis? that is, who are you, in comparison of the whole world? or what chiefe man in the world are you? that you alone should maintaine a most wicked man, and shoul∣dest dissolue the peace of the church? Liberius answered, not be∣cause I am alone, therfore the goodnesse of his cause is the worse. For in time past, there were three only found, that resisted the kings com∣mandement. To whome Eusebius the Eunuch said: Thou hast ac∣counted our Emperour, like Nabuchadnezar. Here Liberius being charged of the Emperour, to declare his authoritie, and who hee was; to maintaine a good cause, could not alleadge for himselfe, that authoritie which nowe the Bishoppe of Rome doth challenge: he might haue said, I am the head of the church, if he had béene so ordeined of God; but hee said no such thing: and yet he was stoute enough, he feared not ye Emperor. For when as he sent him money, to beare his charges, going into exile; he said to those that brought it to him: Go and giue it to the Emperour, he needeth it to paie his souldiers. Concil. Aphri∣can. can. 102. 103.But that discourse, which is contained in the councel of Aphri∣ca, concerning the Bishoppe of Romes authoritie, makes this matter verie plaine. At that councell were present 217. Bishops, amongst whome was S. Augustine himselfe. In this councell, al∣though inSalua chari∣tate. charity, notwithstanding not without much adoe, and disputation, that point amongst other was handled; whether it was lawfull, to appeale to the sea of Rome or no; and Pope Zozimus, who was then departed this life, had sent to the councell the yeare be∣fore, a decree of the Nicen councell, to prooue that it was lawfull to appeale to the sea of Rome. The which decree or Canon, they sus∣pecting to be forged, and affirming that they could finde no such, in
all their latine copies, they write to Bonifacius his successour: First, that they trust by Gods grace, that his holinesse ruling the church of Rome, that they should not suffer this smoak of pride, and that those things should be obserued towardes them, which if they had not rea∣soned about the matter, ought to haue beene kept of brotherly cha∣ritie. And the which thinges also, according to the wisdome and iu∣stice which the highest had giuen him, hee himselfe perfectly knewe ought to be kept, if the Canons of the Nicen councel, peraduenture, were contrarie. And then, that he would ioine with them, and that they might send to the east churches, to Cyrill and the rest of the Bi∣shops there, for the true copies of the Nicen councell. The which thing they did. And when they had receiued the very originall and true copies of the Nicen councell: thus they writ to Celestinus, who succeeded Bonifacius, concerning the matter. Hauing saluted you as becommeth, we earnestly desire you,Epistol. concil. aphric. ad Celest. papā vrbis Rom. that you will not easily admit to talke with any, that shall come from vs to you; nor that you will not admit any whom wee haue excommuni∣cated: because your grauity shall finde, this also decreed in the Ni∣cen councel. For if it be there decreed, of inferiour clergie men, or laie men: how much more wil they haue it obserued of Bishops; that they which are suspended from the communion in their owne pro∣uinces, should be restored of your holinesse, either hastely or rashly, or vnlawfully. Let your holinesse also, as it becommeth you, repell the wicked appellations of priestes and cleargie men, which hereafter shall chance: because by no decree of the fathers, this is derogated from the church of Aphrica, and the canons of Nice haue committed most manifestlie, both the clergy men of the lower degrees, and also the bishops, to their Metropolitanes. They haue most wisely, and iustlie foreseene: that all matters should bee ended in those places, where they began. Neither that the grace of the holy spirit should be wanting to any prouince; by which, equity may be both wiselie per∣ceiued, and constantly maintained of all Christes priestes; especially seeing it is granted to euerie one, if hee bee grieued with the iudge∣ment of them, that shall knowe his cause, to appeale either to the councell of his owne prouince, or to a general councell: Vnlesse per∣chance there be any man that thinks, that our God may inspire to a∣ny one, the iustice of examining causes; and deny it to a great num∣ber of priestes assembled in a councell. Or howe can the iudgement beyond the sea bee good, whither the witnesses which are necessarie,
either for infirmitie of age, or kinde, or sexe, or for many other impediments which may chance, cannot bee brought? Neither doe wee finde it decreed in any councell of the fathers, that any legates should be sent from you. Because that, which you sent not long since, by our brother and fellowe Bishop Faustinus, as a part of the Nicen councell: in the truer councels, which were receiued from Nice, from holy Cyrill our fellow Bishop of the church of Alexandria, and from reuerend Attichus Bishoppe of Constantinople, being sent out of the originals, the which also before this, by Innocentius a priest, and Mar∣cellus a Subdeacon, by which they were directed from them to vs, were sent from vs to Bishop Bonifacius your predecessor of reuerende memorie, in which we could find no such thing. Therefore send not your clergie hither, as dealers in causes, toIt shuld seem to be rather, quibus{que} peten∣tibus: that is, at any mans request, as it is in a copie printed at Pa∣ris. 1565. any mighty mē, or at any mans request rather, nor grant that to them, least you seeme to bring in the smoaky pride of the worlde into the church of Christ, which sheweth to al, that would see God, the light of simplicitie and the day of humilitie. By this historie we may learne manie things. First, that the pope was not then acknowledged supream head, & that S. Augu∣stine & the whole church of Aphrica knew no such superioritie. Se∣condlie, that the holie spirit is not tied to any one man, and ther∣fore not to the Pope: but that it is present in all countries, to go∣uerne the church, to decide all controuersies, as Tertullian also witnesseth;De praescrip. hae∣ret. pag. 99. that Iesus Christ, being taken vp into heauen, doth sit at the right hand of his father, and that hee sent (vicariam vim spiritus sancti: qui credentes agat) the power of the holie ghost, as his Vicar, in his roome: which shoulde leade the faithfull. And thirdlie, that this course was then obserued in all causes: First the Metropoli∣tane dealt in the matter; if the partie grieued would not standt to his iudgement, he might secondlie appeale to a prouinciall; and lastlie to a generall councell. And that was the last refuge, there was an ende. 4. They tell the bishop of Rome, that if the Ca∣nons of the councell of Nice had béene otherwise: yet he shoulde obserue that which he knew to be true, according to that wisdome God had giuen him. 5. They séemed to appeale to his own con∣science, in the matter, that God had ordained no such authority in his worde. 6. They call the authoritie hee challenged, worldlie pompe. 7. They touch pope Zozimus, of forgerie and pride. 8. They say, Christs church sheweth to all men, the light of simplici∣tie
and humilitie, in all her doings: and so on the contrarie, that Zozimus dealt craftilie and proudlie. 9. They thought then, that the pope might erre in those daies. 10. They shewe, that neither the councel of Nice, nor anie other councell, had taken this pre∣rogatiue from the church of Aphrica, nor from anie other: but that she might end all her controuersies at home, without appealing to Rome. 11. They call the bishop of Rome brother. Here is the true copie of the councell of Nice, the testimonie of 217. bishops, the practise of the church; strong arguments and reasons, against the popes supremacie: and yet shall anie man be so wilfullie blin∣ded, that he will not sée and acknowledge all these? Here is that craft which S. Iude prophecieth of, which pope Zozimus went a∣bout to put in practise, which these godfathers espied: and shall we not beleeue them? this testimonie of so manie fathers, this not writing, but presence of Augustine; is enough to ouerthrow quite the popes supremacie. But yet to make the matter more plaine, least anie shoulde thinke perchance that all these were partiall in their owne cause: you shall heare the plaine testimonie, as concerning this matter, of Gregorie; who was bishop of Rome himselfe,Greg. lib. 4 Epist. 91. when as Iohn bi∣shop of Constantinople, because the imperiall seat was there, (as it seemed) puffed vp with pride, by that meanes tooke occasion to preferre himselfe before other bishops, and to be called vniuersall bishop: Gregory being then bishop of Rome, writeth to him after this maner: Mark I beseech thee, how in this thy rash presumption, the peace of the whole church is troubled, and thou resistest or spea∣kest against the grace, which is giuen to all equally or commonly. In which thou maiest so much grow, as thou shalt in thy selfe decrease: and thou shalt become so much great, in as much as thou shalt bridle thy selfe, from the vsing of the name of pride, and of a foolish worde: and so much thou shalt go forwarde, in as much as thou shalt not ar∣rogate to thy selfe, by derogating from thy brethren. Loue therfore (deere brother) humilitie with thy heart, by which the concorde of all bishops, the vnitie of the whole vniuersall church may bee kept. Truly the Apostle S. Paul, when he heard some say: I am of Paul, I of Apollo, I of Cephas; trembling wonderfully at this tearing in peeces of the Lordes body, by which, the members thereof do ioine themselues, as it were to other heades; cried out saying: was Paul crucified for you, or were you baptized in the name of Paul? If hee
therefore eschewed, that the members of the Lords bodie should be particularly subiect to any certaine or other heads, beside Christ; no not to the Apostles; what wilt thou answere to Christ, the head of the vniuersall church, in that strait accompt of the last iudgement, who goest about, by the name of vniuersall bishop, to put all his mem∣bers vnder thee? who is followed as an example, in this froward word? but hee, who despising the legions of angels, ioined fellow-like with him, endeuored to break vp to the top of singularitie; that he would be subiect to none, and alone woulde seeme to bee aboue all. What are all thy brethren, the bishops of the vniuersall church? but starres of heauen, whose both liues and tongues among the sinnes and errors of men, as it were in the darkenes of the night, do shine. To whom while thou doest couet, by a worde of pride to prefer thy selfe, and to tread vnder their names in comparison of them, what saiest thou else, but I will ascende vp to heauen, and I will set my throne aboue the starres? And after: Truely Peter is the first member of the holie and vniuersall church; Paul, Andrew, and Iohn; what are they, but heades of particular peoples? And yet they are all members of the church, vnder one head. Heere wee may plainlie see, by Gregories testimonies these pointes. First, that all bishops were brethren, were equals: and that by the name of vniuersall bishop, he thought, that the peace of the church was troubled; and that by this equalitie rather of bi∣shops, then by anie supremacie of anie one of them, the vnitie and peace of the church, was kept and maintained. Secondlie, that by this name, the grace of God, which was giuen to all Bi∣shops equally, was gaine saide: as though God had giuen to one Bishop, who should bee the vniuersall bishop, more grace, then to the rest. This (saith Gregorie,) is to denie the grace of God, to be giuen to all alike. This he then affirmed: and the papistes now denie. Thirdlie, that Christ is onelie the vniuersall heade of his church, and that all his members are to bee put vnder to none o∣ther, no not of the Apostles, and then not to Peter; but to him a∣lone: much lesse then to the Pope. And doth not the pope yet, now challenge this? Fourthlie, that hee is like Lucifer, that challen∣ged that superioritie, who being fellow with the angels, would be aboue them. So are all bishops as starres equall, and that no one ought to set his throne aboue the rest; who so doth, followeth Luci∣fers example. And doth not the Pope so nowe? Lastlie, that Peter
himselfe, was but the first member of the church; because he first confessed Iesus Christ openlie;As S. Paul cals him a pillar ioining him with the rest: so doth Gregory heere. and not an vniuersall head or Christes vicar, as the pope now challengeth. He was called first in order, of the Euangelistes: because when as one reckons vp manie, there must néedes be one first in order. One may do two thinges at once, as God when as he created heauen and earth, as ne noteth vpon Genesis: but one cannot speake two thinges at once; but one must be named before ye other. So was Peter named first in order, not in honor: herein they were all equall, as Cypriā also herein with Gregorie agréeth.De simplic. praelat. And to make the matter more plaine; Paul, Andrew and Iohn are heades: but particular heads; no vniuersall head, but one Iesus Christ; in respect of whome, all are members, and are vnder him. This is Gregories opinion most manifestlie. But to come nearer, our owne histories proue the same. Eleu∣therius bishop of Rome himselfe, wrote to Lucius our first christi∣an king here in Englād, that he was Gods vicar here, in this his kingdome. And that he néeded nothing but Gods word, and lawes made agréeing with the same, to gouerne his people by: whose e∣pistle to the king is yet to be séen in the records of the Guild-hall in London, as Stowe in his late chronicle reporteth.Lib. 1. eccle. hist. Gent. Ang. ca. 4. Bede also saieth, that the Brittaines receiued the faith in king Lucius daies, and kept the same inuiolable, whole & perfect, and in quiet peace, till the time of Dioclesian. Fidem inuiolatam, integramque quieta in pace seruabant: These be his wordes. But when Augustine the monke afterwarde came from Gregorie, to conuert the Saxons: the Brittaines after they had receiued the faith thus perfectlie and soundlie in king Lucius daies, almost 200. yeares,Bed. 2. lib. eccl hist. ca. 2 all this while knewe no superioritie of the Pope. But when this Augustine (I saie) came to them, to perswade them to ioine handes with him, and others that came with him, in vnitie of doctrine and ceremo∣nies, as the Bishop of Romes legates: the bishops of the Brit∣taines knew no such peremptorie authoritie (as is now taught) that vnlesse they agreed to the Romaines faith and Popes autho∣ritie, they were none of the church, they were damned. But they answered that they would aske counsell of their brethren. And after returning home, and being counselled by an holie Eremite, that gaue himselfe wholy from the worlde to prayers and meditations of the scriptures (as those good monkes and Eremites did in the beginning)
That Augustine if hee were humble and lowlie, then hee was one of Christes schollers; then they should yeelde to him: but if hee were not, then they shoulde not communicate with him. And that they should trie this his humilitie, if he being first in the place, where they should meet, when they came, if hee would rise vp to them and sa∣lute and imbrace them brotherlie. This counsell they followed, and because Augune woulde not humbly imbrace them as his bre∣thren: they vtterly refused his fellowship & cōmunion. By this histo∣rie we may learne plainlie these two things. First that the popes supremacie vnder paine of damnation, was not then acknowled∣ged in the whole church: that all the bishops and learned men of the Brittons neuer heard of it. Secondly, that popish pride then began to spring vp and bud. This Augustine woulde not rise vp to his brethren; and so by degrées, this false catholique doctrine tooke rot & sprang vp,Galfrid. Monu∣met. lib. 8 cap. 9. de gestis Britan∣norian. and not all at once. One of our own writers of this time writeth thus: In the coūtry of the Britains (saith he) al this time christianitie flourished, which from the Apostles time neuer a∣mong them decaied. But after Augustine came he founde in their countrey seuen bishoprickes and one Archbishopricke, guarded or furnished with many learned prelates and many Abbies, liuing with the labour of their owne hands; among whom the Lords flock kept good order.Euseb lib. 3. de demonst euāg. c. 6 So that it shoulde seeme by him, that Ioseph of Ara∣mathia first planted the faith in England, or some of the Apostles passing ouer the Ocean sea, as Eusebius witnesseth. By this we may plainlie see, that these Britaines had the catholique faith a∣mong them, and yet not so much as hearde of the Popes su∣premacie. The Pope a gre while after, obtained this superioritie of Phocas, that hee might be called the vniuersall bishop. And hee was chosen and elected by the Emperours: vntill Leo the ninth, who being chosen by Henry the Emperour as the former Bishoppes were,Pontacus Bur∣degal. in Chro. an. Dom. 1048 first of all refused his election; and affirmed, that the Emperor had no authoritie to chuse him: but he was chosen by his clergie, and by the people. And if this his saying were true, that the Emperor had no right to chose the bishop of Rome: then all the former bi∣shops were not lawfullie elected, and were no lawfull bishops but vsurpers. And here all men that haue any iudgement, may note a strange change or great alteration.1302. The Emperor one thousand thrée hundreth & two years, or there abouts, chose the Pope: and
now since, the Pope is chosen by his Cardinalles; and all those former Bishoppes, by the Popes sentence (who as they saie can∣not erre in iudgment) were not lawfully chosen: but were vsur∣pers, those thousand yeares. And is not this a strange thing, that so manie good bishops, before that time should be vsurpers? Se∣condly, in the beginning the Emperour chose the Pope: but now the Pope chuseth the Emperour: Is not this a great alteration? This their owne histories testifie, and yet they will grant no alte∣ration in the church: they demand of vs, when this alteration be∣gan. Thus all men maie sée, howe they haue plainelie denied the only master of his house, the onelie head of his Church, the only husband of his wife, Iesus Christ, according to Saint Iudes pro∣phesse. S. Augustine, to make the matter more plaine, and that wee maie sée, what was the first faith once giuen to the saintes:In psal. 44. thus describeth Christ and his Church, the bride, and the bridegroome. He is the king of kinges (saith he,) And they are also kinges, of whom it is said, you shal sit vpon the twelue seates, iudging the twelue tribes of Israell. They preached the word of truth, and they begat sonnes, not to themselues: but to him. To this belongeth the mysterie of the lawe: If the brother shall die, let the brother take his wife, and raise vp seede to his brother. Christ is dead, he is risen againe, he is ascen∣ded, he hath absented himselfe in his body, his brethren haue taken his wife, and by the preaching of the gospell, are about to get chil∣dren, not by themselues; but by the gospell, for the name of their bro∣ther. Therefore raising seed to their brother, those whom they begat, they named not Paulians or Petrians: but Christians. Here first Christes absence with his bodie taketh awaie their reall presence in the sacrament. Secondly, if christians maie not be called Pe∣trians or Paulians, then not Dominicans or Franciscans. The brother must beare the name: therefore all Christes séede must be called Christians. Here maie be noted, that christians tooke their name of Christ, as he was called the annointed, and not as hee was called Iesus; because all were partakers of his annointing of the holie ghost: but as he was called Iesus, in the office of his saluation, none were ioined with him: and therfore in those daies, none were called Iesuites. This name is a newe and vsurped name. And a little after: In thy honour, kinges daughters haue delighted: the daughters of kinges, the daughters of the Apostles:
but in thy honour, because they raised that seede to their brother. Yea those which he had raised to his brother, when Paul sawe them runne to his name, he cried out, was Paul crucified for you? What saith the lawe, let him that is borne, haue the name of the dead, let him be cal∣led by the name of him that is dead. This point of the law Paul kept, &c.Contrarie to that master Harding writs: The church of Rome is the vniuersall church: is the onely church of God. And after: behold Rome, behold Carthage, behold diuers other cities, they are kinges daughters: and they haue delighted their king in his honour, and of them all is made one Queene. Why then, the church of Rome (by Augustines iudgment) was not then accoun∣ted the catholique church. She was but a member of the church. She, with the rest of her sisters, made that one Quéene, that one catholique church, that one spouse of Iesus. And after he descri∣beth the garments of this Quéene; And what (saith he) be the gar∣ments of this Queene? It is pretious, it is diuers: The mysteries or sa∣craments of the doctrine,Saint Austen here makes the Aphrican tongue no barbarous tongue. in all, in diuers toongs. There is ye Aphrican toong, the Syrian toong, the Greeke toong, the Heb. toong, and diuers other toonges. These toongs make the diuersitie of the garments of this Queene. But as all the diuersitie of the garments, agreeth in one: so all these toongs are to one faith: In this garment there is diuersitie: there is no rent: there is no diuision. So that the scriptures were then, in all languages. And this was the garment of diuers co∣lours most glorious, which the church then ware: but since that time, the Pope hath changed her coate: she goeth nowe in a coate of one colour, all must be in latine, in his kingdome. This gar∣ment of diuers colours, he cannot abide. In Augustines daies the came clothed in a garment of diuers colours, but in vnitie of wis∣dome. It was the same golde, the same wisedome, in all these tongues, as he there saith. And as he describeth the husband, the person, the vesture of this Quéene: so he describeth her beautie also. The king (saith he) hath greatly desired this beautie. What beautie? but that, which he made. He hath desired thy beautie, what beautie? of a sinner, of one that is vniust among her owne people? No, but that whereof it is said, who is this that ascendes, being made white? Before therfore, she was not white: but afterward she was made white. And a little after: Thou art married to God the king; being endowed of him, being beautifi∣ed of him, being redeemed of him, being healed of him. What soeuer thou hast, by which thou pleasest him, thou hast it of him. Thus Au∣gustine also condemnes their frée will. We haue no goodnesse, not
a droppe of our selues; no beautie, not a sparke: but from him. And after he describes the state of the Church. The daughters of Tyre, shall be there with their giftes. The king commeth (saieth he) and he will haue giftes. But what giftes, almes, &c. And also he de∣scribes her gouernours. For fathers (saith he) thou shalt haue sonnes. The Apostles haue begotten thee: but can they be alwaies in body present? No, one of them said, I desire to be loosed, and to bee with Christ, Therfore by their departure, is the church forsaken? God forbid. For fathers, thou hast sonnes borne to thee. And what is that? The fathers are gone, that is, the Apostles: and for the fathers, sonnes are borne to thee, Bishops are constituted. So that in the Apostles place, Bishops succéeded, and they gouerne the church throughout all the world. And this is the catholique church, (saith Augustine) sons borne to the church, whome she shall make princes ouer all the world: that is, Bishoppes gouerning the church throughout all the world: This is the Catholique Church, saith he. Chrysostome also teacheth vs the same faith of the Greeke church, concerning this matter, in his daies.Hom. 20. ad Popul. Ant. Speaking of the Emperours loue towardes the citie of Antioche, hee saith thus: Haue I not euer preferred this citie before all others, and accounted it more deere then my countrey? If Rome had béene the catholique church, the Emperour had béene too blame, to haue preferred An∣tioche before it. And of the Emperour himselfe, after in the same Homilie, thus hee writes: Oh howe great is the power of Chri∣stianity: the man (meaning the Emperour) vppon earth, hauing none equall vppon earth vnto him, hath bridled and restrained his power, of destroying and ouerthrowing all thinges, and hath taught such Philosophie, as a priuate man woulde not haue shew∣ed. Truely great is the God of the christians, which maketh of men Angels, and setteth them aboue the necessity of mans nature. If the Pope had béene aboue the Emperour, Chrysostome had béene both a lyar, and a flatterer, in preferring the Emperour before him: which I trust, no true catholique will affirme. And after: In this also, the city hath not a little honoured their king, when as they sent no embassadour vnto thee. For they gaue a most excellent and honourable speech of thee,Qui omni principatui tuo subiectos Dei sacerdotes prae∣honoras. that thou honourest very greatly all the priestes of God, which are subiect to all thy dominion, and principali∣ty, though they be neuer so simple. If priestes were not subiect to the Emperors rule and gouernment, this had béene a false spéech,
which the whole cittie of Antioche had giuen of him. One maie perchance make a lie: but it is not likely, that a whole citie should make a lie. Here the Romish catholiques maie sée, howe manie liars they must néedes make, if they will maintaine the preroga∣tiue, either of their Pope, or of their Rome. First the Emperor, 2. then Chrysostome, 3. then the whole citie of Antioch. And in ano∣ther Homilie,Hom. 18. thus he writeth of the citie of Antioche. Thou art sorie that the worship of the citie is lost. Learne what is the worship of the cittie: and then thou shalt surely know, that if the inhabitants doe not betray it, no man else can take away the worship of the citie: Not that it is the mother citie, nor that it hath stately buildings, nor many pillars, and porches, and walkes, not that it is commended before other cities: but the vertue, and religion of the inhabitantes; these are the worship, and ornaments, and defence of the citie. And a little after: What is the worshippe of our citie? It chanced first at Antioche that the disciples were called christians: This priuiledge, of all the cities that be in the world, none hath. Neither that same citie of Romulus, for this cause may looke aloft, against all the world; be∣cause she hath the fire of the loue of Christ; for this trust, for this ver∣tue. See here howe he preferreth plainlie Antioche before Rome, and he calleth it Romulus citie, as it were in contempt, in respect of Antioch: which he would not haue done, if he had beleeued that Rome had béene his mother church, as our catholiques now teach. No doubt Chrysostome would haue spoken more reuerentlie of his mother. And after he concludeth, that although Antioche were in some displeasure, with the Emperour: yet hee hoped, that shee should resume her former countenance, and bee in her former pre∣heminence. Of the Emperors authoritie also, agreeing with Chrysostome, Tertullian writes thus: We worship the Emperour (saith he) so as we may, and as it is expedient for him, as a man next to God, & what∣soeuer he is, hauing obtained of God, lesser then God alone. This also he willeth:Apol. ca. 30. For so he is greater then all others, when as he is lesser, then the onely true God. And in another place: The Emperours knowe who gaue them their Empire: They knowe what are men, they perceiue who are soules or spirits, that he is God alone, in whose power they are alone, from whom they are second, next whom they are first, afore all and aboue all Gods. And after: Moderating the maiestie of Caesar vnder God, I commend him more to God: to
whom alone I make him subiect. I put him vnder, to whom I doe not make him equall. Thus we maie see plainlie, by thrée euident testimonies, that in Tertullians daies, the christians beleeued that the Emperour in this world, was the next man to God. For thus he writeth in their apologie or defence, in the person of them all. And after: least anie should thinke, hee flattered and had forgot∣ten the danger that followeth flatterers, thus he writeth.Cap. 34. If flat∣terie be not ashamed of lying: yet let it feare cursing. He speaketh of those flatterers which called the Emperour a God. Ferus also writeth thus vpon the 6. of Iosuah. By this also (saith he) is shew∣ed that there are three orders necessary in the church. In the first or∣der, are the secular princes: these must go before, and make a waie for the priestes with the Arke: And therefore armour is permitted vnto them. In the second order, are the priestes, and to these belong not weapons but the trumpet, and the arke. For none is to be com∣pelled to the faith with armour; but by preaching of the word: and they which are the Lordes souldiers, must not entangle themselues with secular affaires. In the thirde order, are the common peo∣ple, and they must obey the secular power and heare the priests. Augustine also in an Epistle he writes to Casulanus,Epist. 86. concerning the fast of the Iewish Sabaoth, or our satterdaie, that we ought not then to fast, declareth his opinion of the authoritie of ye church of Rome. It should séeme that the Church of Rome, fasted on the sabaoth, and that this Vrbicus, against whome he writes, vrged this authoritie of the church and Bishop of Rome, for his defence, to whome Augustine answereth thus: In this opinion (saith he) he blasphemeth the church dispersed ouer the whole world, except the Romaines and a fewe westerne churches. But (he saith) it is certaine, that the life of the sheepeEx arbitrio pendere pastorū. depend of the iudgment of their pastors. But wo to them that call good euill, and euill good. &c. What mean these wordes saith Augustine, I cannot tell: for if as you write, Vr∣bicus saith thus, the people depending of the iudgement of their pa∣stor, doth fast with their Bishop on the sabaoth day; If he haue writtē these things thus vnto you, because in your Epistle you haue put such a like matter: let him not perswade you, so to praise a Christian city fasting on the sabaoth, that you may be compelled to condemne the whole christian world, that day dining.
