At these feastes, were some of these heretikes the Apostle here speaketh of, present: These feastes were not taken away, till they had set foote in the church: And therefore hereby wee maie see, howe poperie came into the church, by stealing steppes, by degrées, and not all at once; after
these psalmes and feastes, and all, were gone.In Apolog. c. 39▪ In those feastes was great sobriety, as Tertullian writeth of them: & yet in these feasts, these vsed riot and excesse. They which should haue béene orna∣ments, were spottes and staines, they which shoulde haue beene lights, were slanderers to the church: They fed themselues with∣out regard of anie man, they made much of themselues. And by this is noted, that these heretikes, should not only be cruell in per∣secution, and couetous in conuersation, and rebellious in practi∣ses: but also riotous and belly gods in their liuing.Ezec. 34.2. They shall re∣semble those olde Iewish false prophets, which should feede them∣selues, and not féede their stockes. And were not the whole popish cleargie such like? were not these spottes in your feastes? did not they féede themselues? They should haue fedde the soules of their flockes, and feasted them spirituallie: but they tooke part of their feastes and good cheere, but they neuer feasted their soules:1. Cor. 9.11. They reaped their carnall things, but they neuer sowed them any spirituall thinges. And is not this to be spottes in their feastes? But they saie they kept good houses in those daies. It maie be so. But then they fedde the bodie onelie: and not the soule. But Christ com∣manded his pastors chiefely, to feede the soule. Feede my sheepe,Io. 21.17. feede my sheepe, feede my lambes, saith our sauiour to Peter. And those three féedinges (as some note) argue thrée kindes of foode: of word and doctrine, and of example of life and conuersation, and of foode and meate in hospitality and sustentation. The first & chiefe of these in those daies, they for the most part neglected: and of yt the Apostles said, It was not meet, to leaue the word of God,Acts 6.2. and serue tables; preferring preaching of the word of God, before the féeding of the poore. And of this our sauiour saith,Luke 12.43. Happy is that seruant whō his master when he commeth, shall finde giuing meate to his family in due season. Oh then twise vnhappie is he, that giueth none at all! And here by the waie (this in due season) toucheth them, that be non-residents, that seldome come at their flockes, they cannot giue them meate, in due season. But the Epistle of S. Peter, who with S. Iude (as I haue before noted) ioines hands in discouering these heretikes, more at large sets them out.2. Pet. 2.13. They account plea∣sure daily banqueting, saith he: they fare deliciously euery day, with that rich glutton; they follow the steppes of those riotous pastors and sonnes of Belial, whom Esay prophesieth of. These greedy dogges (saith he) can neuer haue enough,Esay. 56.10. & these sheepheards cānot vnder∣stand.
They all looke for their owne waies, euery one for his aduan∣tage,Verse. 12. for his owne purpose. Come (saith one) I will bring wine, and we will fill our selues with strong drinke, and to morrow shall bee as this daie: and much more aboundant. They forget that lesson of the preacher,Eccles. 3.1. there is a time for all things. And were not their Ab∣baies and Frieries, in time past like these? neuer satisfied, neuer hauing enough. This one thing maie bee a plaine proofe thereof: That when by the statute of mortmaine, they were abridged, without licence of the prince, to receiue the gift of anie moe tem∣porall landes, at the death of anie man (which they still gaped af∣ter, although they had enough alreadie) then they obtained license of the Pope, that they might haue benefices impropriate to them, placing some poore vicars in the cure, and they might receiue al the commoditie themselues: And so they robbed the true pastor of his liuing. And thus they, by their excessiue couetousnesse were the adulterous fathers, of impropriations. It was also, they said, the propertie of a Frier, still do be begging. It should séeme these earthly things they so gréedelie sought after: they tooke part ther∣of, they tooke some pleasure therein. 2. Pet. 2.13. .But that which followeth in the Apostle Peter, toucheth them is the quicke: They banquet and make good cheere, in their deceipts and fraudes: They themselues, call their oblations and offerings, as the bloud of Hailes, and such like (which they confessed to be but lies) holie deceiptes and fraudes. And by this, they beguiled the people, and got their mony from them; and with this mony, they made merrie and kept good cheere: And is not this to banquet with their deceiptes and guiles? euen by their owne confession. Naie besides all this, all their good chéere, in their Abbaies & Frie∣ries, which they maintained, came of deceipt. They perswaded the people that they would praie for them,Mat. 25.9. that they should haue part of their oyle to light their lampes, when the bridegroome should come, they sold them the merits of all their couent: and they sold them deare enough. And by these meanes, they obtained all their landes, they gat all their riches, they maintained their good cheere: Whereas in Epiphanius daies, and in Beades daies here in En∣gland, the first good Monkes, in all monasteries as they reporte, were glad to worke, with their handes to get their liuings. They knewe not this gainefull trade and merchandise of selling their praiers, as these did of late daies: and yet they prayed as much as
they did both daie and night as they report,Bede mentions there three daies fast, tri∣duanum ieumi∣um, with prai∣ers: at the bat∣tell with Ed l. frithe eccl. hist. 2. lib. ca. 2. Mat. 25.8. Mat. 23.14. and were as full of good workes, as euer they were. But they thought according to the gospell, they coulde not haue oyle enough for themselues and for others also: These latter knew not the gospel, and that made them so bolde and hardie. And is not this deceipt? surely the greatest deceipt in the worlde, to make merchandise, and that false mer∣chandise, of mens soules: to eate the sinnes of the people, to make no bones of them: vnder pretence of long praiers, with the Pharises, to deuoure widowes houses. Thus we maie sée how plainly S. Peter and S. Iude agrée together, in disciphering these heretiks; and thus we maie plainly sée, if we be not ouermuch blinded with partiali∣tie, who fulfill both their prophesies. S. Paul saieth,2. Cor. 5.10. Wee must all giue account for our owne workes what we haue done in our bodies: And Chrysostome saieth to his hearers,Hom 13 ad Pop. Antioch. I would to God I coulde worke for you, that my works would serue your turne: but you must doe your good workes your selues.Mat. 7.19. The tree it selfe that beareth not good fruit is hewen downe, and cast into the fire (saith our saui∣our) Is cutte downe alreadie, euen as sure, as that it were cutte downe. But they will saie, maie not one praie for another? And so ones good workes profite another. It is true, one maie praie for another, and so helpe another. But euen as proppes to a vine, or cares to a boate; are our praiers for others: They are helps, they are outwarde meanes: but if the vine be dead it selfe, what profi∣teth the vnderpropping of it? If the boate take water, if it be not made of good wood, if the boardes be not compact together, what profiteth the oares? Euen so, if as vines, we haue not the life of faith our selues; if we be not grafted in that vine Iesus Christ; if like good boates, we be not compact together, with the bondes and ioints of christian charitie: these props, these oares, these praiers,Heb. 10.38. or whatsoeuer of our brethren will not help vs. The iust man liueth by his own faith. But this sale of their workes, & that of bad workes, of praiers in Latine, of de profundis, for another man, which Dauid made for himselfe, which was a plain mockerie of God: yea & that they standing in néed of them, themselues (as who is it, yt dare say to God, he is not an vnprofitable seruant?) And lastly,Luke 17.10. our trust in these their workes, is the thing that Gods word condemnes. But the church (saie they) hath a treasure, and the Pope is the dispenser of it, and out of that, he maie bestow or sell merites to
whome hee will. Wee reade no such thing in the scriptures. In Christ Iesus wee reade,2 Col. 9. Io 1.16. 2. Col. 3. are all the treasures of wisedome and know∣ledge: and if of these, then of mercie, of merits also. For another text saith, All fulnesse dwelleth in him, then fulnesse of mercy. And of this his fulnes, we all like empty vessels, must receiue. And the ministers of the gospell with S. Paul, must preach , vnsearchable riches of Christ, among the Gentiles. If the riches of Christ be so aboundant,Ephes. 3.8. what néede we anie other? If it be the duetie of his ministers to preach these: then they are anti∣christes ministers, that preach anie other. And S. Paul saith, the church is the fulnesse of him that filleth all things in all thinges.Ephes. 1.23. Why then, she is filled of him: she hath no treasures of her owne to sel. Let all runne to the well head,Psal. 35.10. Ier. 2.13. and not to the streames, as ye scrip∣ture commandes. And here also that text of the gospell condem∣neth their merchandise or sale of their workes: you haue receiued freely,Mat. 10.6. giue freely, saith our sauiour. Their workes are fréely giuen them of God, why should they then sell them? Text.Cloudes they are without water, carried about of windes, corrupt trees, and without fruite, twise dead and plucked vp by the rootes.] Hitherto the Apostle hath shewed vs these deceiuers by manie and most liuely examples: now least wee should bee deceiued by them, and that we should discerne them in déede; he pointes them out by similitudes in their colours, as we saie. And he puts down heere two similitudes of them, to teach vs their vaine bragging and oftentation. They shall make great shewes, they shall pro∣mise much: but performe nothing. They shall be like good shéepe∣heardes in shewe: but in truth nothing neare them. Ministers are compared by S. Paul to the Hebrewes,Heb. 6.7. to cloudes which raine vpon the earth: after whose heauenly showers, if the ground and hearts of their hearers, bring forth no fruit, they are as barren ground, accursed,Eccles. 11.3. and adiudged worthy the fire. And the preacher saieth, if the cloudes be full, they will power out water: So Gods ministers will plenteously declare his will to his people.Am. 7.16. And Amasiah cō∣manded Amos, prophesie not against Israell, neither drop any more against the house of Isaak: So that all Gods pastors are cloudes, which raine, which droppe like dewe, which poure out aboundant∣lie, as occasion requireth, the heauenly raine, vpon the ground of Gods church. But these are cloudes: but voide of water, carried about with windes. They haue the habit of pastors, the authority:
they are placed aloft, they are called Prelates, they make great shewes, euen as thicke cloudes doe sometime of raine, but not a droppe followes. The soules of their people, euen as it were drie ground, thinke for lacke of heauenlie moysture. And were not the Popish cleargie like these cloudes? with all their ornaments and robes and gownes and habites like pastors: but no raine fel. They were caried about with winde,Ephes. 4.11. for lack of the firmament of Gods word. God hath giuen Apostles, and Euangelists, and pastors, and teachers in his church: least we should be caried about with eue∣rie blast of vaine doctrine. These clouds, lacking the soundnesse of the Apostles doctrine and euangelistes, like emptie vessels, were tossed vp and downe. They beléeued euerie thing. They were not built vpon the rocke, that is, vpon Iesus Christ, and his word.Psal. 1.3. They are also trees in Autumn withering] The Godly are called trees growing by the waters side, that bringe foorth their fruit in due sea∣son, whose leaues do not wither. And our sauiour saith, euery good tree bringes foorth good fruit. But these are like trees blasted, for so the greeke name importeth, , which bringeth foorth nothing but corrupt and wi∣thered fruit. Such workes were most of theirs, not workes com∣manded of God in his worde: but of their owne deuises. Not workes that tooke sappe by faith, but which tooke sappe of mans fancie; as oblations, pilgrimages, buying of ornamentes to the church making great windowes, guilding images: all these lack the sappe of Gods word, these were like blasted fruit. And such for the most part, were the workes of these pastors, the fruit these gaue to their hearers. [Twise dead] not onelie by nature borne the children of wrath, and in life liuing like the sonnes of Beliall: but by their doctrine, falling awaie from the life of grace.1. Ti 5.6. A wi∣dowe wallowing in pleasure, though liuing bodily, yet the Apostle countes dead to God: much more these couetous, riotous, fruite∣lesse, and barren pastors. [Twise dead] dead men by their sinnes, and dead pastors by their doctrine. For no doubt, although they, which in that time of ignorance died,2. Chro. 15.3.4. and called for mercie ob∣tained it; as wee reade of the like time of ignorance among the Iewes, and so we doe not damne all our fathers that died then: yet no doubt, there remaineth an eternall woe, as vpon the Pha∣rises, so also vpon those blind guides, which by their holie deceits, beguiled Gods people. Or twise dead:] neither teaching by tongue
nor by example of life. Plucked vp by the rootes.] That is they are like trees plucked vp by the rootes, which are past all hope of reco∣uerie: euen so these will hardlie be brought to the light of the gos∣pell, they will hardly be brought from their olde kinde of liuing. They can sing masse well: but they are vnfit to open their mouths to speake to the glorie of God, to preach his word, to edifie his con∣gregation. That they cannot awaie withall. Text. Verse. 13.They are raging waues of the sea, foming out their owne shame: they are wandring starres: to whome is reserued the blackenesse of darkenesse for euer.] Before, the Apostle seemeth to describe the persons of these heretikes; they are cloudes without raine, they are emptie vessels, they are blasted trees: Now he describes their workes, their dealings. Christes church is compared to a shippe Heb. 6.Heb. 6.20. and the shippe wherein hee was, may resemble very fitly his church: which was almost ouerwhelmed with waues: In so much that the Apostles cried out:Mat. 8.25. saue vs Lord, wee perish. And in the Reuelation we reade,Apoc. 12.16. that the serpent out of his mouth, threw after the woman, that is the church, water like a floud; in so much that she was caried away with the floud: and if the earth had not helped her, she had vtterly perished. Surely this sea is the world: and these waues are heretikes, and false catholiques, that trouble and vexe the church of God. No shippe in the maine sea was euer so tossed, as the shippe of Iesus Christ is tossed in this world, by sathan himselfe driuing her (if it were possible) to the rocke of despaire; and therefore it hath néede of hope, as it were a most sure anchor, fastened with the oath and promise of God, as it were with two most strong cables: by his ministers,Heb. 6.18. assaulting and persecuting it; and therfore it hath néed of Iesus Christes power and presence, with it, euen to the end of the world. If he should not put to his helping hande, it could not haue chosen, but this shippe had beene sunken, long since. Hee helpeth with his mightie hand this poore ship, he maketh the earth, that is death, deuoure her raging waues, her persecuting ene∣mies. Herod a length died, persecuting Christ: so shall all He∣rods, persecuting his christians. And surely these waues may re∣semble the Cardinalles, Bishoppes and Prelates of the church of Rome, who in all kingdomes, since Popedome beganne, haue beene readie to persecute the church, and to assault this shippe. No man durst once speake against the Pope, or his doings; but hee
was catched by and by: So that these men maie bee fitly compa∣red to waues for their doinges, waues for their worldlinesse and couetousnesse, waues for their pride and ambition.In Apologia ad Guilielmum Abba. em. Bernard spea∣king of the state and pride of the Abbots of his daies, writes thus: I lie (saith he) if I sawe not an Abbot haue in his traine, threescore horse and aboue: you would say, if you saw them ride by, they were not fathers of Monasteries, but Lordes of some Mannors: not rulers of soules, but gouernours of prouinces. Then they must haue caried with them, their table clothes, their goblets, their basons, their can∣dlestickes, their trunkes stuffed, not with litter for their horses: but with ornaments for their beddes. They scant trauell seauen furlongs from home, but with all their stuffe and furniture; as though they should go to some armie, or into some wildernesse, where no proui∣sion were to be had. The Bishop of Elie here in England,Stow in his Chro. in king Ri∣chard ye first his daies, being in his absence gouernour of the Realme, ridde with fiue hundreth horses. Pius the second came into Perusia,Campan. in eius vita. riding on a white Palfrey, twelue others of the same colour, going be∣fore emptie, couered with purple, being led with golden bridles. The magistrates of the citie carrying a cloth of state of purple, wrought with golde: vnder which was the pope carried in fine white linnen, with a stole of golde put about him, and a scarlet hatte. What pompe was this? What greater pride could be imagined? And what is more vaine, and more like the vaine and mightie waues of the sea? They are wandring starres,Text. for whom is reserued the blackenesse of darkenesse for euer.] The pastors of Christes church are called starres by Daniell, because they giue light to others,Dan. 12.3. in the darke night of this world: because they take their light of the sunne, be∣cause they séeme little, though in deede greater then the earth; be∣cause they are fixed in the firmament, they kéepe their place. But these would séeme to be starres: but they are wandering or erring starres. The sunne is called Sol, because it onelie shineth (as one noteth) and giueth light to all thinges. And therefore the wicked complaine of the lacke of this light:Wisdom. 5.6. Therefore haue we erred from the way of truth, and the light of righteousnesse hath not shined vnto vs; and the sonne of vnderstanding rose not vpon vs. These borrow not their light of the sunne:Leu 10.1. They bring into the Church strange fire with Nahab and Abihu: they seeme profound doctors: but their doctrines are not constant, are not sure: are not grounded on the
word of God. They ground, they build vpon the sand; that is vp∣on nature, vpon worldly thinges. So the papistes make heauen like a kings court, and Peter the porter; and saintes mediators to God. They drawe frée will from Aristotle. Their schoolemen, were almost as manie in opinions, as in number. The sande is in∣finite; and so are the deuises of mans reason. It is impossible, that euer they should come to an ende, that followe it, and are ru∣led by it. To whome is reserued the blacknesse of darkenesse for euer.] Be∣cause they like owles, loued darkenes more then light, because they haue delighted more in the darkenesse of mans braine, then in the light of Gods word: therefore shall they dwell in darkenesse for e∣uer. For God in the same measure againe, repaies the wicked; and heapes their owne euill waies vpon their owne heades. They which loued darkenesse, shall bee tormented in darkenesse: they which like wilde beastes, deuoured and destroied all thinges (for Bestiae taketh his name à vastando of wasting as some thinke) shall bee de∣stroied themselues of deuilles: they which haue loued the pleasant fire of sinne, shall suffer the sharpe fire of hell. Text. Verse 14. Some thinke that Enoch wrote bookes, as of this book Tertullian de habitu muliebri makes mentiō and defends.And Enoch also the seuenth from Adam prophesied of such, saying: Behold the Lord commeth with thousands of his saintes.] This say∣ing of Enoch maie séeme to be by tradition committed to his po∣steritie: as no doubt was that promise of God made to Adam, the womans seede shall bruise the serpents head. This place also proo∣ueth, that God will haue some alwaies to preach his truth: as E∣noch and Seth, and Noe to the old world, & Lot to the Sodomites; but neuer so manie in anie age, as in this of ours: And therefore not one wo as our sauiour pronounced ouer Capernaum and Beth∣saida, but euen as S. Paul saith, Anathema Maranatha, that is, woe and againe wo shall fall vpon those, which despise Gods word, nowe so plainely and plentifully taught.Luke 12.48. For as the gospell teacheth, to whom much is giuen, of them much shall be required againe. And a∣gaine, he that hath eares to heare let him heare. But take heed what ye heare:Mar. 4.24. as though hee should saie, you shall one daie giue ac∣count of it. The Lord commeth, that is, shall most assuredly come with thou∣sands of his saintes and angelles. For both these shall adorne the tri∣bunall seate of Iesus Christ.Mat. 17.3. And as Eliah and Enoch in the trans∣figuration: so now all saintes in his great glorie and maiesty shal
bee present with him. And thousandes here are named, that the number of the wicked should not terrifie the godlie. The wicked to vs séeme manie in number, seeme mightie in power: but they are but as waxe before the fire when God ariseth,Psal. 68.2. their enemies are but a handfull in comparison of his. The chariots of God, are twenty thousand euen thousands of Angels, and the Lord is amongst them, as in the holy place of Sinah.Verse 17. And there was a great company stoode before the throne of God, of all nations, kinreds and people, which no man could number. And euen in this world no doubt,Reuel. 7.9. the Lordes wheate is infinite: though hidden amongst the chaffe, though the chaffe of the wicked beare the greatest shewe. To giue iudgment against all men,Text. Verse 15. and to rebuke all the vngodly among them, and all their wicked deedes which they haue vngodly committed, and of all their cruell speakings, which wicked sinners haue spoken against him.] He speaketh of the second comming of Christ. For at the first, when he came into the world, he came not to iudge the worlde, but that the worlde by him might bee saued.Io. 3.17. With God mercie alwaies goeth before iudgment, pardon is of∣fered before punishment, saluation before destruction: So Iesus Christ came a sauiour first, before hee comes a iudge. And euen now his long tarrying from this his fierce iudgment, which here so long before Enoch prophesieth of;Phil. 4.5. Ia. 5 10. 2. Pet. 3.9. and the Apostles saide was hard at the doore, is nothing else, but his great aboundant tender mercie to vs ward, as S. Peter teacheth: he is loth to come, he de∣ferreth the time, no doubt, as long as may be, that all men might bee prepared against his comming. And the great vengeance which remaineth for the vngodlie, should kéepe Gods children in his feare and obedience. If the elements shall burne with fire, what kinde of men ought we to be (saith Peter) in holy conuersations and good workes,Verse 11. looking for and hastning to the comming of the day of God? We should by our workes declare our selues, as though we greatlie desired that daie, as though we would euen run to méet it. Euery daie hath his proper workes. The scripture teacheth vs what workes belong to the daie of iudgment:Mat. 25.35. To feede the hun∣gry, to giue drinke to the thirstie, to harbour the harbourles, to cloth the naked, to visit the sicke, to go to prisoners. These workes we should doe with all speed, and so we should as it were make haste to that daie. These are the workes which at that daie shall be loo∣ked for at our hands; shall be allowed of in our accountes; shall
be crowned of our mercifull and mightie king. These the iudge himselfe, who cannot lie, who would haue all his ready and prepa∣red, hath foretold vs. And what can be more louingly done to vs then this? that the iudge should tell one what he should doe or saie, before hee commeth to the barre. Our iudges maie not doe it, they maie giue no counsell: but this great iudge of his excéeding great loue towardes vs, hath done it: and oh foolish men, who wil not followe his counsell, who regard it not, who nowe this iudge∣ment drawing neare, will doe quite contrarie. These dearthes of corne which we haue had of late, this dearth of wooll and cloth, these rents raised of houses in all places: are but trialles of vs a∣gainst this great daie of God, what we will doe: whether we had rather fill our purses, or feede the poore; whether we had rather for lacke of rent, turne the poore out of doores, or else haue patience with our brethren; and if our tenants be not able to pay vs, looke for our rent at Iesus Christes handes: whether wee had rather clothe our selues with our wooll money, and hang the walles of our houses; or the liuelie walles of the temple of Iesus Christ? The most men hope and wish corne will be deare, and hourd it vp, they will sell none yet, that they maie fill their purses, they wil not sell to the poore, much lesse relieue the néedie. The landlordes inhaunce their rents, that the poore cannot reach to them, and so doe not harbour them; but as much as in them lieth, turne them out of dores: naie they inhaunce their rentes so, as the tenant is not able, both to paie his rent, and maintaine his familie. And this is the chiefe cause, why hospitalitie decaieth so in our daies, especiallie in great lordshippes, which should bee as it were wel∣heads to relieue the whole towne. Their rents are so great, that the tenantes of them are not able to giue anie almes, or reliefe. And is this to haste to the daie of the great God? Is this to follow our iudges counsell? Is this to haue faith? This is plainlie to saie in déede, there shall be no iudgment. For if they beléeued it, they would prepare themselues against it. S. Paul giueth all christians this notable lesson against the daie of iudgment: We must all be made manifest before the tribunal seat of Iesus Christ,2. Cor. 5.10. that euery one may receiue according to those things hee hath done in his body, either good or euill. Wherein euerie word hath his force: First in that he saith (we must) there can be no excuse, God will pardon none. All, euen euery one, euen kings
and others that be in authoritie and nowe iudge others. (Be made manifest:) not onely make appearance, as we doe in our courtes oftentimes, and then depart: but all the corners of our heartes, all our workes, all our secret thoughts, all our imaginations and priuat practises (which we keepe close in the bottome of our harts, as the prophet Dauid saieth, and which wee would haue no man knowe) shall then be made manifest, euen as cleare as the sunne, to the eies of all men: And that not before a friend, which would couer and cloake their faultes; but before the tribunall seate of a most terrible iudge, at whose presence heauen and earth quaketh: who is now come to render to euery man according as he hath done. Oh therefore, let vs nowe take héede what wee doe, let vs studie nowe to please him, that at that daie we maie be accepted. Wee knowing this feare of the Lord, saith the Apostle, this terrible day of iudgment: we doe perswade men that they do good,2. Cor. 5.11. that they now striue who can please him best. For no doubt there is a reward. It is not, as most men thinke, that there shall be no regard had of our workes. Although our workes shall not iustifie vs, yet this shall be required at our hands, God will not haue his seruants idle:2. Pet. 1.8. And therefore he saith to all his faithfull seruants, I come quickly and my reward is with me: As though he should saie,Reu. 22.12. be not weary of well doing, or do not thinke it long ere I come, for I will come quickly, in respect of eternitie. Labour you, sweate you, endure you but a mynute of an hower; and you shall rest for euer. And my rewarde, my wages is with mee; I come not emptie. And surelie hee that bringes wages with him, lookes for some worke∣men. Let vs all therefore be the Lordes workemen against this great and appointed daie, that we maie receiue our wages. For he will giue to euery one as his worke is. Our daies are like the daies of Noah and of Lot,Luke 17.26.27. whereof as our sauiour prophecied, the men of the worlde at this day, doe as they did then. Let vs marke euerie circumstance and euerie word well, and we shall find it so. As our earnest desire and great studie of building, planting, buying, selling, purchasing, banque∣ting, marying in tender yeares without consent of parents, neg∣lecting degrees of consanguinitie, more then euer heretofore, e∣uidentlie proue. May it not trulie be saide of our daies that wee eate and drink? when as fasting nowe almost in all places and a∣mongst all sortes of men is quite banished. Neither maister nor
seruant, nor artificer, nor laborer will fast: If they do fast at any time, it is by constraint and with murmuring. Luk 18.12The Pharisie fasted twise in the weeke, as appeareth in the gos∣pell; and shall not we christians fast as often? Especiallie seeing our sauiour saith to all christians,Mat. 5.20. that except your righteousnesse exceede the righteousnesse of the Scribes and Pharisies; yee shall not enter into the kingdome of heauen. This terrible sentence shoulde moue vs to fast.Barthol. George viz. de morib. Turcar. The Turkes haue their Lente which they call ORVTS: and they fast one moneth and a weeke, euery yeare: and when they fast, they tast nothing, neither bread nor water til the stars appeare in the firmament: And shal not we obserue our Lent? shall they go beyonde vs in fasting? That were a shame for christians, whome S. Paul commandes euen twise in one chapter,Tit. 3.8.14 Ignat. in epist. ad Phillip. Aug. epist. 119. ad. Ian. Ieron. in 3. cap. Ionae. Brent. in cap. 19 Exod. to excell in good workes. The primitiue church obserued Lent, as Ignatius, Augustine & Hierome do testifie, and our church & Prince now also commands it: and yet such is our intemperancie, that we wil not obserue it. Brentius a learned man of our age writes thus, concer∣ning the fasting of Friday and Saturday, vpon that place of Exo∣dus, Moreouer the Lorde saide vnto Moses, Goe to the people and sanctifie them to daie and to morrow, and let thē wash their clothes, and let them be readie on the thirde daie: for the third daie the Lord will come down in the sight of al the people on the Mount, &c. Then Moses went downe from the Mount vnto the people, and sanctified the people, and they washed their clothes: and he said vnto the peo∣ple, Be ready on the third day and come not at your wiues. I thinke (saith Brentius) that from this place our ancestors consecrated to so∣brietie and abstinencie the sixt day and the Sabaoth: that on the next Lords day ye people might come pure and prepared to heare the law of God. The superstition of daies is to be misliked; yet this preparatiō and instruction is necessarie, that men may be made more fit to heare the worde of God: we sowe no seeds in the earth vnlesse we plough before, &c. And surelie it is to be feared that for lacke of this pre∣paration, the seede of Gods word, which is so painfullie and plenti∣fullie sowen in all places, at this daie, taketh so small effect & brin∣geth forth so ltitle fruite. Men come to heare the word of God on the sabaoth daie with vnprepared heartes. It is a seede sowen on land that is not plowed; and can the seed then be it neuer so good, bring forth anie fruit?Trem. in cap. 29. Exod. And Tremelius vpon the same place writes thus: Nowe altogether applie your selues, that you may be instruc∣ted,
insomuch that nowe come not at your wiues. And vpon that place of Samuel, where Abimelecke asketh Dauid if the young men haue kept themselues, at least from women:1. Sam. 21.5 This question (saieth Tremelius) is drawn from the Analogy of the commandement Exod. 19.15. and of the Oracle of God, of which mention is made hereaf∣ter in the tenth verse, and in the chap. following verse 10. As though hee would say, they which will vse most holie thinges, such as these loaues of bread are: must be endued with that purenesse, which God requireth of them that come nigh to him, and now also he comman∣deth. They which heare the worde of God, or participate his holie sacramentes, by Tremelius iudgement grounded by that place of Exodus, should abstaine euen from their lawfull pleasures, euen of meates and drinkes, euen from their wiues, before they come to be guests of the Lordes table. But I feare me that before wee come to the Lordes table, either to eate the bread of his worde, or of his sacraments, this washing our garments, this fasting, this abstaining from our wiues is neglected. In Hebrew, fasting is called Tsom, deriued by transposition of letters, of Mots, that signifieth to sucke out:Dan. 10 2. and surelie so it may verie trulie. For thus we reade of Daniell. Daniell was in heauinesse three weekes: I did eate (saith he) no pleasant bread, nei∣ther came flesh in my mouth,  neither did I annoint my selfe at all till three weekes of daies were finished, and then Daniell lift vp his eyes, and he sawe a man clothed in linnen, whose loynes were girded vnto him with fine gold of Vphaz, his bodie was like the Chrysolite,  & his face to looke vpon like the lightening, and his eies as lampes of fire, and his armes and his feet were like to polished brasse, and the voice of his worde was like a multitude. And hee saide to Daniell: Feare not Daniell: for from the first daie,  that thou didst set thy heart to vn∣derstand, and to humble thy selfe before God, thy words were heard. And I am come for thy wordes: and I am come to shewe thee what shall come to thy people in the latter daies. Daniell fasting sawe this strange vision, and euen suckt from heauen that great myste∣rie, that shoulde befall his people in the latter daies, and thinges that concerne vs. Peter also fasting till the sixt houre of the day, that is, till noone:Acts. 10.10. had that great mysterie of ye calling of the Gentiles reuealed vnto him. And Cornelius fasting til the ninth houre, till three of the clock,verse 3. sawe an Angell appearing vnto him, and suckt euen by this means,
by sending for Peter, faith in Iesus Christ, & the saluation of his soule. In our daies Napier a learned man, that hath taken great paines in vnfoulding the mysteries of the Reuelation,Napier to the christiā reader confesseth to the glorie of God: that hee found more fruite in searching that high mysterie, in one howres sobrietie, praier, and humble meditation, then in a thousand daies of curious or presumptuous inquisition. And no doubt Philippus de dies, Granatensis, and Ferus amongst the papists: all the iewels they haue,Phil. de Dies. Fer. 2. in lit. maior. they haue obtained by this meanes of praier and fasting. It is fasting that makes the mind apt to con∣templation, as they themselues doe confesse. Granatensis confes∣seth that the three children in Babilon,Fer. in c. 9. Mat. Granat. de Ieiu∣nio lib. 2. cap. 19▪ who despised the kinges deli∣cates and pretious wines, which were brought them euen from the kings own table, being content with pulse and water, by this meanes attained to so great wisdom. And that by the same meanes Saint Ber∣nard gat all his learning, whereas hee was but a little while brought vp at schoole. And that by the benefit of fasting and abstinence, S. Gregorie, who did eate nothing but raw pulse, which his mother ho∣lie Siluia did send him, became so wise: So Hierom vsed the same ab∣stinence in his life, as he writeth of himselfe. And S. Basill that most famous preacher, and most eloquent and wise Oratour and Deuine, that euer was in the world: yet in clothing himselfe and sleeping hee was most abstinent. He couered his naked bodie but with one gar∣ment, and he slept alwaies on the ground; nay rather hee watched al night, and continued in holie exercises. All these doctours beeing so excellent in wisdome, were no lesse famous for their abstinencie, then for their wisdome. They knewe howe necessarie the one vertue was to obtaine the other. So Thomas Aquinas that subtill dispu∣ter (as he at his death reuealed to his companion & brother Reig∣nold,Anto. part. 3. tit. 18. ca. 10. which thing as long as he liued he kept close as a secret) had all his wisdome, by diuine reuelation; and therefore it was his custome, when as he would write or speake any thing, he woulde first go to praier. And comming from praier, hee had that as rea∣die which he should vtter as if he had learned it in some booke. And no doubt he ioined fasting to his praier and mercie. And therfore Augustine saieth:Aug. lib. quest vet. & noui te∣stam. quest. 120 Our Sauiour which had no neede to fast, fasted, that he might giue vs an example. For then a man declares that hee would obtaine that which hee desires, when hee punisheth himselfe with fasting. And hereof it is saide, that praier is good with fasting. Therfore that praier may be acceptable, it wil haue with it as a com∣panion,
fasting. And because neither of these is sure, without pittie: he addeth, And almes with righteousnesse. So great is the force of fasting. If wee would then knowe the secret mysteries of God, let vs fast. Basil also of fasting verie excellentlie writes thus. As much as thou shalt take from thy flesh:Basil. ser. 2. de ieiunio. so much shalt thou adde to the liuelie force of thy soule: and the Angels who are appointed keepers of our soules, doe more willinglie and carefullie keepe those which by fa∣sting are purified. Nay, there are angels in euery church and con∣gregation, marking and registring those that doe fast. Take heede therefore least thou be punished for thy short pleasure of thy meate, and least thou make thy selfe guiltie to the Angell the Lordes Recor∣der, as a runnaway from the Lordes armie. Surelie it were lesse dan∣ger for one to throw away his shield in the field, then to slacke to take in his hands the great weapons of fasting. Art thou a rich man? despise not fasting: vouchsafing to bid it to dinner with thee, and make it thy guest, least thou make thy house wherein pleasure and belly-cheere beareth the rule, vile and worth nothing; least thou thy selfe also smart for it, at that Lawgiuers hands, and pay deerely for thy ryot: greater troubles being iustlie laid vpon thy backe, either by some bo∣dilie sicknesse, or by some other grieuous mischance. Againe, if thou beest a poore man, do not thou despise fasting, when as now thou hast fasting, as thy bedfellow, and thy daily companion. Fasting is as pro∣per to women, euen as the ayre they breath, and that euen by na∣ture. Children as young plants, must be watered with the water of fasting. And the olde acquaintance of fasting maketh it seeme lesse laborious to old men. What can be said more forcibly to perswade all meen to fasting? Angels note in euerie parish who be good fa∣sters. But some will saie perchance, this is but Basils opinion. But I saie more, and that out of the gospell: that euen God him∣selfe notes and markes those that fast. Doth not our sauiour say?Matth. 6.17. But when thou fastest, annoint thy head, and wash thy face: that thou seeme not to men to fast, but vnto the father which is in secret: and thy father which seeth in secret, wil reward thee openly. Surelie I feare me nowe, that neither God nor Angels see anie fast. Let vs re∣member to fast: for Basil saith that Angels register those that fast. And our sauiour saieth, that euen God himselfe seeth them, and knoweth them euerie one, and will reward them. And againe, he writes thus:Basil ibidem. Doest thou not see how horsebrea∣kers
and masters do tame their horses first, and make them nimble by fasting? But thou euen of set purpose, doest so with fulnesse presse downe and spoile thy selfe, that in gluttony thou goest beyonde the bruite beastes. A full bellie is not fitte for a race, no not to sleepe quietly, because being ouercharged with heauinesse, it causeth vs not to be quiet, but to tosse ourselues hither and thither. Fasting preser∣ueth children, it maketh young men sober, it maketh olde men com∣lie, and reuerende, it is the fittest ornament for women, a bridle for them that be lustie and healthfull, the safe keeper of wedlocke, and the nurse of virginity. This is the care, that abstinencie hath in euery particular family. But common abstinence gouerneth our whole life, it bringeth euery citie & people to a good state, it stilleth all quar∣rels and braules, it rootes out suites, it controwleth all reproches and reuilings: Euen as the masters presence stilleth the noyse of children; so fasting bridles the sturres of cities. Who euer came wanton or de∣sperate from fasting? What company was euer out of order, that vsed fasting? nice scoffings, wanton songes, madde merriments, straight way depart the citie, beeing banished of fasting, as of a seuere iudge. And if all men would vse this in all their affaires, as a counseller; with∣out all doubt, nothing could hinder but that quiet peace shoulde bee thorow the whole world. Here are excellent commodities of fa∣sting, singular commendations and ornamentes to euerie age: nay peace to our common wealth. And no doubt all those troubles which are now so common amongst vs, arise for want of fasting. The well fed horse, can abide no spurre: so they which delicatelie féed themselues can endure nothing; they will bee reuenged for e∣uerie little iniurie. And surelie hereof no doubt it commeth to passe, that sithence fasting hath not béene vsed: so manie sortes and quarrels haue sprung vp amongst vs. Wine and good cheere engenders hot spirits, which will soone be inflamed to anger. He∣raclitus the Philosopher in an vproare of the people,Eras. li. 8. apoph. beeing desired that he would shewe his iudgement how the citie might be brought to concord going vp into the pulpit, he desired a cup of cold water to be giuen him, and he mingled with it a little meale, and a little wilde Pnniryal or some pulse, and drank of that water; and so speaking ne∣uer a word went downe: signifying that if the citie woulde leaue their riot, and be content with a little and simple fare, they would soone bee at vnitie. Thus much the blinde Philosopher could see by the light of nature, and shall not we see so much being indued
with gods spirit? Nay faithful fasting turnes away gods plagues from vs▪ Ahab when he had grieuouslie offēded God,1. King. 21.27 & had heard ye heauie sentence of Eliah, what did he? He rent his cloathes & put on sackcloth, & fasted, & lay in sackcloth, & walked softly. And the word of the Lord came to Eliah, saying; Seest thou not how Ahab is hum∣bled before me? because he humbleth himselfe before me: I wil not bring this euill in his daies. Let vs marke how Ahabs fasting cried to God for him: we do not reade that he praied; and yet God had respect to his fasting. Wee haue manie at this daie as sinfull as Ahab: I woulde to God they would followe Ahabs steppes. The same force had fasting in Niniue,Ion. 3.5. euen when Gods plagues were now readie to fall on their heades. Iehosaphat also when his ene∣mies assaulted him, proclamed a fast thorow his whole land.2. Chro. 20.3 We are in the same case, God threatens vs manie waies, and shakes his rod ouer vs our enemies dailie assault vs: Oh let vs fast and praie with Niniue and Iehosaphat, that wee may escape all these euils. The flesh is that Eue,Gen. 3.6 Gen. 39.7 Iudg. 16.19 Mat. 26.69 that with her pleasant fruit beguiled Adam; that wife of Putiphar, that intised Ioseph; that Dalila, that lulled Sampson a sleep in her lap, and bereaued him of his strength, and put out his eies: that same handmaide, that made Peter de∣nie his maister. Let all Gods faithfull seruants beware of it: let them refuse her pleasant fruit; let them flée from her entisements; let them not be allured with her pleasures; let them not heare her voice; let them tame her with Paul, least they become reprobates.2. Cor. 9 27 They are not wiser then Adam, stronger then Sampson, more cou∣ragious then Peter.Eus. hist. eccles. lib. 2. ca. 17 The first christian Monkes laide abstinence in their heartes, as the foundation of all vertues, and vpon that as vpon a rocke they built all other vertues.Chrys. ho. 18. ad pop. Ant. Surelie in our daies for lacke of this foundation, other vertues are so scarce. Chrysostome writes thus of his daies. I see many glad, and saying among themselues, we are happie now, wee are glad: halfe the daies of fasting are gone. But I exhort such that they should not bee glad, because halfe the fast is past: but rather to consider that if halfe their sinnes bee quite gone and vanquished, and then to be glad; for that is to be reioiced at, and that is the marke that is shot at, and for which all thinges are doone. And after: The corne appearing in the spring, and the trees florishing with leaues; teach the beholders, what profit winter hath brought. Let the same thing be don in vs We haue receiued much raine (of the heauenly grace) in the time of our fast: by continuall preaching, we
haue receiued seede, and wee haue quite cut awaie our thornes; let vs continue our fast, that we may keepe those thinges we haue receiued, that when fasting is done, the fruites of fasting may appeare. Our fieldes may teach our soules: These late yeeres sithence we haue lacked the accustomed frost and snow of winter; we haue also lac∣ked the accustomed increase of our winter corne. And so no doubt where this frost and snowe of fasting is not, the spring of vertues cannot be. God himselfe, as should seeme, punisheth this our riot: and yet we marke it not. The riuers and the sea (as I haue heard) yeeldes not that plentie of fish which heretofore they haue doone. We canne digest no fish nowe. All men at all times must haue flesh: And God seeing this, therefore diminisheth and takes from vs that plentie of fish which we haue had. What shall I saie of mariage? May it not also bee verified of our daies, that now we marrie and giue in mariage? Euery one now will be maried. There will almost none continue either vir∣gines or widowes: whereas I reade, that in the primitiue church there were manie both virgines and widowes. In the church of Antioch in Chrysostomes daies,Chrys. hom. 34 ad pop. Ant. as he himself reporteth, there were three thousand Virgines and widowes. And in the church of Rome I reade in Eusebius,Eus. lib. 6. eccle. Hist. ca. 34. that there were a thousande and fiue hundreth poore people, and widowes that were relieued of the common stocke of the church. But in our daies, both widowes and virgines are rare to bee found. No father now will kéepe his daughter a Vir∣gine. And whereas in other matters concerning our children we will do the best: in this waightie matter we regard not what is best for them.1. Cor 7.37.38 For S. Paul saieth, Hee that giueth his daughter in mariage doth well: but hee that giueth her not to mariage, doth bet∣ter. Who regardes this better now? who thinkes of it? who once moues it to his daughters? Philip no doubt the Euangelist had re∣spect to this:Acts 21.9 He had 4. daughters, and they were al Virgines. It had béene a great matter and worthie the marking, if two of them had béene virgines; but that all the foure should bee virgines, was wonderfull. And this saying of the Apostle, and this practise of Philip: made so manie virgines in the primitiue church, of whome Chrysostom and Eusebius do make mention. And likewise of widowes he saieth: The wife is bounde by the law, as long as her husband liueth: but if her husband be dead, shee is at libertie to marrie with whom she will,  only in the Lord. But shee is
more blessed, if she so abide in my iudgement. And I thinke that I haue also the spirit of God. Euerie widow nowe be shee neuer so old will be maried, despising this counsell of S. Paul.Luke 2.37.38 Annah which had liued seauen yeares from her virginitie with a husband being a young widowe) continued a widowe fourescore and eight yeares af∣ter. But now a daies young widowes must needes marrie: And the reason is because they will not follow the true widowes,1. Tim. 5 5 whom S. Paul makes mention of, and Annah her footesteps: Of whom it is reported, that she went not out of the Temple, but serued God with fasting and praiers day and night. Our young widowes will not be good church women like Annah,Gen. 34.1 but towne women rather like Dinah: They will walke the streetes to see and to bee seene. They will not serue God with fastinges and praiers as true widowes ought to do; but with feastings and pleasures serue the flesh:1. Tim. 5 6 & there∣fore they must needes marrie. But why was this example of An∣nah so preciselie set downe? For vs to reade onelie? nay no doubt, but for widowes to imitate. For whatsoeuer is written,Rom. 15.4 is written for our learning, as S. Paul saieth. Nay in mariage now if there bee anie hope of gaine, as though there were no more choise nowe, then in the daies of Adam: wee will come as neare the degrées prohibited as may be, no respect being had, either of consangui∣nitie, or publike honestie. Neither is there almost anie accounte in mariage made of age. Now euen verie children in yeares will be maried. When was euer so manie stolen mariages heard of as in our daies?Iudg. 14.2. Children now will marie without their parents consentes: Which Sampson would not doe. Sonnes daughters and brothers sonnes will marie together. Nay brother hath ma∣ried the brothers wife. Examples of these are to too manifest. We now forget those two manifest histories of the scriptures concer¦ning mariages. Isaac that sonne of promise,Gen 24 3 that great heire of the world: He committed to his father the choise of his wife, And his father committed this great matter to his trustie seruant:Verse 12. but in the feare of the Lorde. And the seruant praied in his iourney, that the Lord would prosper him. And the maid when shee was seene and liked of, and as it were picked out of God, was not conuaied a∣waie without the consent of her parentes. And her parentes said to the seruant, this thing is comen of God,verse 50. besides his will wee can say nothing to thee. Here is no speech of dowerie; no considerati∣on of beautie: but God is all in all, No doubt if our great heires
would be thus ruled by their parents in their mariages, and haue God, rather then riches, beautie or worldly respectes, before their eies: they would speede better. But verie manie now adaies fol∣lowe Sichem the sonne of Hamor the Heuite, his hart claue vnto the maide, he spake kindly to her, he tooke her and defiled her: and after spake to his father Hamor: get me this maide to my wife. And then he left nothing vndone, that might helpe to bring the matter to passe. This is the course that manie both mightie and simple, take in their mariages at this daie. And few virgines are married, few with ye parents consents: And therfore their mariages thrine so euill. And shall it not be saide of our daies, that nowe we mar∣rie and are giuen in marriage? What shall I speake of our sumptuous and stately buildings: which at this daie are so common amongst vs? If wee respect the plaine buildings of our Auncestors in comparison of ours; wee maie be truely said, now to build. And this stately and sumptu∣ous kinde of building hath taken such roote, that nowe euerie one will haue such a stately and sumptuous house. The buildings of our forefathers were but, as it were, simple cottages in compa∣rison of our stately pallaces. So that it maie truely be said of our daies, that we build now. But in the scripture we read, that Iecho∣nias the king of Iudah was reprooued of Ieremie the prophet,Ier. 22.15. be∣cause he built him a stately house with large windowes, and painted it with vermilion, and seeled it with Cedar. And will God allow ex∣cessiue building in meaner men?Es. 2.15.16. Esay prophesieth, that the day of the Lord shall be vpon euery high tower, and euery strong wall, and vpon all braue prospects, as Arias Montanus translates it. And the day of the Lord now drawing neare, shall we now build such? Ioel prophesieth, that the land shall be as the garden of Eden, like a pa∣radise, before him: but behinde him he shall make it a desolate wil∣dernesse.Cuspinianus writes this of the Turkes. And doe we not feare this threatning? The Turkes shew great plainnesse in their buildings, hauing no delight in building hou∣ses, though they be very rich in gold and siluer: accounting this a vaine thing. And they build their houses seldome of stone: but most com∣monly of wood, and they laugh vs christians wonderfully to scorne, when they see our great buildings, which they beleeue we build ther∣fore,Iohannes Stump∣sius reports this historie. as though we should liue for euer. And shall we giue them any occasion to laugh vs to scorne? I reade a historie, which I would all our great builders would imitate. Two brethren being Ro∣maines,
escaped out of the destruction of a citie called Vindonissa, whereof the one being preferred to be Bishop of Argentine: perswa∣ded his brother with money that he gaue him, to builde a castle neare vnto Vindonissa, which nowe they call Halspurge, so famous with the petigrees of so many kings and Emperours. The Bishop hea∣ring that the castle was built, comming to his brother when as he saw that the building thereof was very rude and weake; first he began to wonder at the folly of his brother, and after to demaund an account of him of his money. To whom his brother made answere. To mor∣row you shall see, both the bulwarks of my castle, and also my recko∣nings. In the meane while the same night, he commanded all the no∣ble men and country men his neighbours, whose landes and seruices hee had redeemed and set free, with his money: to bee ready in the morning armed, as though they would assault the castle. The Bishop not knowing what the matter meant, amased with the sight of such a multitude, as though they had beene his enemies; was tolde of his brother, that those were his walles of yron, which he had bought with his money. I would to God our great builders would make such walles to their houses. Such walles would please God, and pro∣tect their builders more surely, then anie walles of stone. But we build now adaies, or care for few such walles. But some will saie, is it not lawefull to builde then? Surely thereis a time for all thinges, A time to breake downe,Eccles. 3.3. and a time to build, as saith the preacher. But now to beginne to build so cu¦riouslie, so statelie, so costlie:1. Pet. 4.7. when as we are taught by the scrip∣ture, that the ende of all thinges is at hand, and that we liue in the daies of Noah; is out of season. This is plainely to gainsaie the gospell, and to saie with the wicked,2. Pet. 3 4. where is the promise of his cō∣ming? And to doe as the men did in the daies of Noah. As we doe inherit our fathers landes, why should wee not, euerie one in his degrée, be content also with his fathers buildings? Do we thinke their buildings too simple for vs? This our blinde pride doth teach vs.Gen. 18.1. 1. King. 22 39. Let vs remember that Abraham our father dwelt in a simple tent, and he entertained Angelles: which thing Ahab in his Iuorie house neuer could doe. And in the psalme we reade of all ye righ∣teous, that in the tentes or tabernacles of the righteous is the voice of ioie and gladnesse. Surely in our stately houses manie times,Psal. 118.15. is not this voice of ioie and gladnes, but rather of sorrow and pen∣sinenesse.Heb. 12.13. The saintes of God account themselues pilgrimes in this
world: and therefore as pilgrimes, they make no account of their houses; they doe account them, but as Innes, wherein they shall lodge but a night. Let vs marke the Paganes in their common wealthes:Pet. Gregor. Tholos. de Rep. lib. 2 ca. 10. howe they bridled this excesse in building. By the Ro∣maine lawes they were not suffered to build the walles of their hou∣ses, aboue halfe a foote thicke, and that because they should haue but one loaft or flooring aboue them; and their bricke walles but two or three brickes of thicknesse: But now adaies, we build thicker wals and make our houses more loftie. Augustus Caesar the Emperor, although he had a pallace:Suetonius. yet he dwelt sometime in Hortensius hou∣ses, which were lowe and simple, without any marble pillars. Such was this Pagane Emperours humilitie. But such houses now will not content Christians: Manie bestowe so much cost on the wals of their houses, that they are not able to bestowe any thing within the walles, as long as they liue after. Will God allowe this prodigalitie? Let vs rather bestowe our cost vpon the poore, and liuelie stones of Iesus Christ.1. Pet 2.5. Let vs relieue them sufficientlie, which are now sent home, by a good and christian law, to their pla∣ces where they were borne.Ezech. 16.49. Let vs strengthen the handes of the poore: as Sodome would not doe: Let them bee well relieued, not only to kéepe life and soule together (as they say) but that they maie be strong to labor, least we be like Sodome in punishment. Let vs repayre and maintaine Gods house that is the church:Mat. 21.13. which in most places now is ruinous & lieth desolate. That complaint of Agge is verified of our daies most manifestly,Agg. 1.4. we our selues dwel in seeled houses, and Gods house lieth wast. The churches in times past, were the best houses in the towne: but now of all other they are least regarded. This declares the coldenesse of our loue, to∣wardes the owner of them.Mat. 11.15. Christ when he came to Ierusalem, the first house he went into, was the temple: And doth he regard his houses of praier, that is our churches, lesse now? No, no doubt, at his comming as he whipped the buyers and sellers then out of the temple: so will he also whip out, all those now that buy and sell in his church, whosoeuer they are, and what fine pretence soeuer they shall make to cloake this their Symonie; and will punish the spoyle and desolation of his house. And to let this house lie wast and to build our owne, is not this to build? The like may be said of purchasing and buying land. Men were neuer so giuen to purchase and buy land, as at this daie. What
shall I speake of planting? Heretofore they hedged in their gar∣dens and orchardes: but now we will haue our corne fieldes hed∣ged about. So that without all doubt, the daies of Noah are come vpon vs: And this prophesie of our sauiour is most euidently ful∣filled in our eies. And it is to bee feared, least that as at the first comming of our sauiour, the Iewes hauing a plaine prophesie, that when the scepter should depart from Iudah, then Messias should come; yet they were so blinded with worldlie ambition, that al∣though this prophesie was cleerelie fulfilled, that they would not sée nor marke it, and so perished in their blindnes: so at the second comming of our sauiour, least we, hauing also this plaine prophe∣sie that our daies shall bee like the daies of Noah, and we sée the same manifestly fulfilled, shall bee like them carried awaie with the course of the world; and also perish in our ignorance and care∣lesnesse. The Lord Iesus open all mens eies that they may marke this. These are the workes of the world: these are not the workes which Iesus Christ commands against the daie of iudgment. Let them that bee godly wise, marke well; least while they followe their steppes, they perish in their destruction. Let the course of the world beguile no man: That because others doe so; therefore we maie doe the like. This reason could not saue the olde world, nei∣ther shall it saue vs. There were but eight persons then saued, who beleeued the Lorde, all the rest that followed the world, were drowned. Let euerie christian therefore learne that lesson of Saint Iames: There shall be iudgment without mercy to him,Ia. 2.13. Mat. 5.7. that sheweth no mercy: And that of our sauiour, Blessed are the mercifull, for they shall obtaine mercy. These lessons then will be accounted worth the marking, let vs practise them now that we may then obtaine mercie, though the practise be neuer so costly. In this iudgement Enoch prophesieth what our iudge shall re∣prooue: wicked workes, and wicked and hard wordes against God: Let all christians beware of these two thinges. And here ye works which shall be reprooued, are called in the gréeke. irreligious works; such as haue no taste of religion, or godlinesse, which taste of the dealinges of the worlde. Let vs beware of such workes: let vs not be like this wicked world in our dealings;Mat. 7.13. Let vs not followe the broad way which leadeth to destruction: let vs striue to enter in at the narrow gate: let vs followe the light of Gods word, which shi∣neth now most plenteously amongst vs. But if we shall do so, saith
one:Marke 8.36. we shall loose. This counsell is against our profit. O foole, what will it aduantage thee to winne all the world, and to indanger thine owne soule? It is but an apple that here thou now gainest, and thou loosest paradise with Eue:Gen. 3.6, It is but a messe of redde pot∣tage, which thou heere enioiest, and thou loosest thine inheritance with Esau.Gen. 25.33. What great follie is this? But some will saie: do any giue harde speeches against God? none is so wicked. Yes, ouer manie. It is a common saying, If anie rebuke a wicked person, and tell him of this iudgment of God: Hee will say, It maketh no matter, if he may escape to that day. Is not this to giue hard spee∣ches, euen against the Lord, to decide and set light his iudgment, which euery one ought to quake and tremble a? which maketh the earth to tremble as Dauid saith,Psal. 18.7. The earth trembled, the very foun∣dations of the hilles shooke, and were remoued, because he was wroth. And in another place,Psal. 119 120. my flesh trembleth for feare of thee, and I am affraid of thy iudgments. Text. Verse 16.These are murmurers, complainers, walking after their own lusts. Whose mouthes speake prowde thinges, hauing mens persons in ad∣miration because of aduantage.] Now he describeth these false Ca∣tholiques, by their delightes and desires: because they measure and account felicitie or happines, to consist in thinges of this life: Therefore i anie affliction or misfortune chance, they murmure, they are impatient. And it cannot chuse, but such were our for∣mer Friers and Monkes. For they were couetous and gréedie of these worldlie riches (as I haue prooued before:) they were euer begging and neuer satisfied.Psal. 23.4. They lacked Dauids staffe of Gods worde to comfort them:Rom. 15.4. when God said his rodde vpon them they lacked the knowledge of the scriptures, which were written for our learning, that wee thorowe patience, and comfort of the scriptures, might haue hope: and therefore it could not chuse, but they should mourne and repine, at the manifolde crosses, which at that time fell vpon them. Kinges haue often pinched them, fire hath consu∣med their houses, and manie other chances haue beflane them; as wee maie reade in the Chronicles, which to sustaine with pati∣ence, they no doubt needed the castle and bulwarke of the scrip∣tures. Text. Ps. 70.4.145.11. Ps. 33.1.134.21.Complainers, finders of faults] Dauid giueth this note of the faith∣full, that ye praises of God are euer in their mouthes: and of himselfe, my mouth shall euer speake the praise of the Lord: And the Apostle
commandeth all christians that in all thinges they should giue God thankes. So that then,1. Thes. 5.17. good christians must not finde fault with Gods workes: whatsoeuer he sendeth, they must be content with all, they must thanke him for it. They must in all chances, with Iob saie, The Lord be blessed. What artificer among vs,Iob. 1.22. will pa∣tientlie abide his worke to be found fault withall? Much lesse our most mightie God. And therefore Ecclesiasticus teacheth vs this lesson, Blesse the Lord in all his works, giue honor vnto his name,Eccl. 39.14. and shew forth his praise with the songes of your lips, & with harpes, and ye shal say after this manner. Al the works of the Lord are exceeding good, and all his commandementes are done in due season. And none may say: wherefore is this? what is that? For at a time conue∣nient, they shall be sought out. But at this daie, it is a common fault amngst many olde men, to finde fault with Gods workes: manie times, with the weather, with the increase of the earth. And therfore it should seeme, in the former times, they were not taught this good lesson: it maie séeme, their teachers knewe it not them∣selues. And therefore this marke hits iustly vpon them. Their mouth speaketh proud thinges.] They are Thrasoes,Text. they brag of themselues. So haue they seduced the people, by bragging of their masses, their reliques, by making thē come a pilgrimage farre and nigh to them. They haue bragged of their Popes autho∣ritie: that no man maie saie to him, why doest thou so? that hee is a God vpon earth. Hauing mens persons in admiration because of aduantage.Text.] They are worldly minded, and this is the second marke of Antichrist. First, he shall denie, that Iesus Christ is come in the flesh: Hee shall denie that he is that onely king, priest, and prophet;1. Io. 4.3. which all the scriptures prophesie of. Whose shadowes and types, were all the kinges, priestes, and prophets that euer were: Melchise∣decke, Aaron, Samuell, Dauid, Salomon, Esay, Ieremy and the rest: Iesus Christ alone, is more then all these. And yet euerie of these in their times had God, sufficiently furnished, to bee able to doe their offices. And yet Antichrist shall substitute other to Iesus Christ, as not sufficient or willing to doe his office: whome the scripture adorneth with this kinde of willingnesse,Heb. 7.25. Verse 5. that he euer li∣ueth, to make intercession for vs. Secondly, they shall bee of the world, and therefore shall speake of the world, and the world shall heare them. And were not the Abbots, Monkes and Popes king∣dome,
of the world? Their statelie buildings, their pleasant seats, their insatiable mindes; declare what they were. Those that en∣riched them, them they reuerenced, them they praied for. Was not this to haue men in reuerence because of aduantage? Such were the priestes among the Iewes.Hos. 4.11. They did eate the sinnes of Gods people; whoredome and wine, and newe wine, take awaie their heartes, they were as a snare on Mispah, and as a nette spread on Tabor (as saieth the Prophet:) All was fish that came to their nettes. Mat. 23.14.So did the Pharises vnder pretence of long praiers deuoure widowes houses: So did they in S. Pauls time that counted gaine religion.1. Tim. 6.6. But Saint Paul teacheth Timothie, and in him all Gods ministers, to forsake and separat themselues from such couetous tea∣chers: and that godlinesse is great gaine, with contentment; and to be content with meate drinke and cloathing; not with monkish and popish state, and superfluitie: And to followe righteousnesse, godlinesse, faith, loue, patience, and meekenesse. Of which riches Gregorie also speaketh, If you will be (saieth he) truely rich in deede, loue the true riches, that is vertues. And of charitie Saint Augustine saith, that by charity a poore man is rich. Charitie alone is like a pre∣tious iewell, the valew whereof is so incomparable, that it enricheth the soule of him, whosoeuer hath it. These celestiall and spirituall riches Christes ministers shoulde pursue after, with might and maine (as they saie.) Those other transitorie and earthlie riches, are baites fit for Antichristes hirelinges: who for them haue men in great admiration,Gal. 1.10. whome if hee should studie to please (S. Paul saith) that he were none of Gods seruant. Text. Verse. 17.18.But you beloued, remember the words which were spoken before of the Apostles of our Lord Iesus Christ. Howe that they tolde you, that there should be mockers in the last time, which should walke af∣ter their vngodly lustes.] Here first we may learne that S. Iude be∣ing himselfe an Apostle, was not ashamed to alledge the testimo∣nies of the Apostles; condemning the arrogancie of those, that despise the authoritie of their equalles: nay of those, that haue bin their fathers in Christ. Secondly, that he liued after the other A∣postles. Thirdly, that he referreth this Epistle, to the predictions, and prophesies of the other Apostles: That those whome hee heere speaketh of, they also prophesied, that such should come: So that then his Epistle must be a prophesie, a prediction to the church, as
well as others. Although perchance in some part, that wicked seed began in his daies, more to shewe it selfe, then in the daies of the Apostles, (as I haue noted before.) And as he cites ye prophesies of the Apostles: so especially of Peter, whose very words he alleageth.2. Pet. 3.3. That there shall bee mockers.] So that his Epistle of all the rest most agreeth with this Epistle: So that as it should séeme, they had euen ioyned handes, to the discouering of the same heretikes. He calleth them mockers, which being drowned in worldlie plea∣sures, and being set in the chaire of pestilence, doe make a sporte of sinne: Who dare saie, in the manifolde threatnings, and knoc∣kings at the dore of their heartes, by Gods spirit:Ier. 5.12. Let the worde of the Lorde come. Tush it maketh no matter, these are but wordes, no euill shall happen vnto vs, we haue béene tolde this long ago; but we throue neuer the worse since. Such Atheistes, and sonnes of Beliall, all ages haue had: and our age hath too ma∣nie of them, which fulfill the prophesie of Iude, to their owne de∣struction. Walking after their vngodly lustes.] This barren branch,Text. sprin∣geth of the former wicked roote. For those that make a mocke of the worde of God: to such pleasure is life, and their own wicked lustes and desires, are reason. The worde of God is the onelie hatchet, to prune the vines of Iesus Christ,Io. 15.2. Ios. 5.2. that they maie bring foorth more fruit. It is the onelie sharpe knife, that Iosuah made, to cutte awaie the foreskinne of all carnall pleasures, from the true Israelites: that they maie serue the Lord with all their hart.Psal. 31.89. It is the onelie bridle, that keepeth both young and olde, from stumbling like horse and mule, which haue no vnderstanding: and therefore where this lacketh, there all sinne flourisheth, all plea∣sures abounde, and men fall downe headlong into the pitte of destruction. And therefore Dauid praieth,Psal. 119.133.17.5. Order my steppes in thy word, and so shall no wickednesse haue dominion ouer me. And stay my steppes in thy pathes, that my feete do not slide. These are makers of sectes, hauing no spirit.]Text. Verse 19. Heere wee may marke how in the verse going before he saith, that such shall bee: and here he speaketh after the maner of the Prophets, in the pre∣sent tence: these are makers of sectes: as though they were come alreadie: which may seeme to expounde his like phrase of spéech, verse 4 These are makers of sectes:] there is no one vertue that the Apostles vrge more in all their Epistles, then peace, peace in doc∣trine,
peace in life and conuersation. And therefore the Apostle Saint Paul writing to the Romaines, doth beseech them earnestlie as a last farewell that shoulde sticke déepelie in their heartes,Rom. 16.17 to marke those which make diuisions or offences, besides that doctrine which they had learned. Hee doth not saie, which is against the doctrine which you haue learned, but besides it: As adding anie thing, as it should seeme, of their own braine vnto it. For (saith he) such serue not the Lord Iesus, but their own bellie. I would to God the church of Rome had remembred this farewell of the Apostle: Then no doubt, she would not haue brought in so manie orders of her Fri∣ers and Monkes; which should after a newe manner, besides the word of God, not by preaching the gospell; but by singing Masse, saue soules. They serue not Iesus Christ, (though they rise ne∣uer so earlie,) that obey not his word. S. Paul willeth Timothie to take heede to himselfe and to his doctrine:1. Tim 4 16 To continue in them, that is,Verse 13. those thinges hee had commended to him before; which are rea∣ding, exhortation, and doctrine. For if thou shalt doe so, thou shalt saue thy selfe and them that beare thee.Rom. 1.16 And to the Romaines hee saieth, The gospell is the power of God to saluation, to all that shall beleeue it. So that then, not to sing masse: but to preach the gos∣pell, is the ordinarie waie of saluation, prescribed by God in his word. These sectaries S. Paul speaketh of, with flatterie and faire spéeches seruing their bellies, not Iesus Christ: haue deuised a new waie of saluation, which the scriptures teach not, nor our sa∣uiour commandes: Go preach the gospell (saith he) to al nations, he that beleeueth and is baptised, shall bee saued. This worke all his seruants, all his ministers must doe earnestlie and earelie in the morning. Psal. 87. Her foundati∣ons are vpon the holy hils. Ephes 2.10.The prophet Dauid describes the church of Christ, and he giueth it eight priuileges. First, that it is not founded vpon earthlie hils, as was Ierusalem: but vppon holie hils, euen vppon the hils of the scriptures, vpon the Apostles and Prophets, as S. Paul saith. Se∣condlie, that the Lorde loueth the verie gates, the meanest congre∣gation of Christs church, more then al the dwellings of Iacob, euen aboue Salomons temple. Thirdlie, that all the Prophets and Pa∣triarkes haue spoken very excellent things of this citie: As Esay, In that day this song shall bee sung in the Lande of Iudah.Esa. 26.1 Wee haue a strong citie; he hath put saluation her walles and her bulwarke. As walles doe kéepe and defende, all euils and enemies from a citie:
euen so the certaintie of saluation, as a wall kéepes all euils and enemies from the church of God. They know they shall be saued; and therefore they feare not, what colde stormes of afflictions, what wilde Boare of the forrest, what sicknesse or sorrowe, nay what death doth assault them. This wall and bulwarke of saluation re∣pels all euill from the church. Fourthlie, this city receiueh in it all the nations of the world. Christ as soone as he was borne wente into Aegypt: and by a starre, hee drewe out of the East the wise men: to declare that superstitious Babylon, and sinnefull Aegypt should nowe embrace Iesus Christ. Fiftlie, that the founder of this citie, is the eternall God, who was borne in her. Sixtlie, that the gospell is preached (as it were) by Trumpetters in this citie. Sea∣uenthlie, that all that dwell in this citie, are merrie and ioyfull.Shorim ce∣chollim. Or rather (as it is in the Hebrew) the Lord will number in writing vp the people, that this man was borne in her, and the singers as the Trumpeters. Here are two sortes of people, which God wil write vp, and enroll in his heauenlie citie, when hee surueyeth his city, The singers as well as the trumpetters. All Gods people must either bee praisers of God, or preachers of him. And therefore generally of praising God in his church,Esa. 26, 1. (saieth Dauid) In that day this song shall be sung: As though all men should sing that song, and should praise the Lord. The people should sing and praise God, the mini∣sters should bee trumpetters and preachers of the glad tidinges of the gospell. And therefore of the ministers, is that saying verified, Extol thy voice like a trumpet. And lastlie,Isa. 28.1 that al Gods fresh springs should be in his church. Knowledge should abound in it euen as a streame. And hereof no doubt commeth the number of so manie famous men, and excellent preachers, as wee haue at this daie. The chiefe office of the minister, is to be a trumpetter, not to be a singer of masse, as it was in poperie. And this diuision also of the church of God, we reade in an other psalme. They sawe how thou my Lorde and king goest in the sanctuarie: that is, they would see,Psal. 68.24. might see, the going and pompe of the people, giuing thee thanks in the temple for the victorie ouer their enemies. The singers went before, that is, all the people lauding and praising God: The mu∣sitions followed after, that is, the priests and ministers. In the mid∣dest of them were the damsels playing on tymbrels. That may bee expounded of the virgines, who had made their bodies like tim∣brels dried and withered, as S. Paul said of his bodie:I tame my
flesh,1. Cor. 9.27. and make it wanne or drie, least when I haue preached to o∣thers, I my selfe should be a castaway. These singers, and these mu∣sitions, and these plaiers of timbrels, in the shadow of the lawe, resemble no doubt the truth of the gospell. All our people must be singers and praisers of God; all our pastors must bee musitions, must be trumpetters; our virgines must plaie on tymbrels. And of these musitions Christ meanes when he saieth, Wee haue piped to you,Mat. 11.27. and you haue not danced: meaning his own preaching and his Apostles. And of these singers Dauid here saith, that the Lord shall write them vp, and enfranchise them in his heauenly kingdome: As well the singers as the trumpeters. These trumpeters the pro∣phet Esay meaneth when he saith, Cry as lowde as thou canst, lift vp thy voice like a trūpet. These trumpeters the Angels in the reuela∣tion blowing with trumpets resemble.Reu. 8.6. They which do not this worke in the church of God, whatsoeuer they doe besides, are sectaries. And of these sectaries and heretickes S. Paul speaketh: If any man shall teach any other doctrine,1. Tim. 6.3 and shall not giue heede to the health∣full doctrine of our Lord Iesus Christ, and to that doctrine which a∣grees with religion, he is puft vp and knoweth nothing. Here is the badge of Heretiques, not to preach the doctrine of Christ, not to giue héede to the worde of God, to teach doctrines besides it, to be puft vp with pride, to knowe in truth nothing. Such ignorant, proud, and erroneous teachers were the Monkes and Friers, and therefore no doubt these makers of sectes, which S. Iude here spea∣keth of. Text. Rom. 8.9.14.15Fleshly hauing no spirit.] All Gods children haue Gods spirit, and are led by Gods spirit, and the spirit maketh them come to God with great boldnesse,1. Cor. 2.15 by this spirit they discerne all thinges: and haue a right iudgment in all thinges. 1. Pet 4.10.Of this spirit and of the manifold giftes thereof, Peter speaketh, Euery one, as he hath receiued the gift: let him minister the same one to another, as good stewards of the manifold grace of God. If anie man speake, let him speake; as the wordes that God putteth in his mouth. If any man minister, or doe any good worke; let him doe it, as of the strength that God ministreth vnto him: that God in al things may be glorified by our Lorde Iesus Christ. All Gods children then, must be partakers of this spirit, and must acknowledge what good things soeuer they doe proceed from the power and might of Gods spirit, yea euen the wordes of their mouthes. This spirit especial∣lie,
all Gods ministers haue; as S. Paul witnesseth: God hath not giuen vs the spirit of feare: but of power, of loue and of sobrietie:2. Tim. 1.8. and of these two, he willeth Timothie not to bee ashamed: to testifie the Lord Iesus: and not to be ashamed of him his prisoner. The prophet Micah had this spirit.Micah. 3 8 And I trulie (saith he) am fil∣led with the power of the spirit of the Lord, and with iudgement, and with strength and courage, to shew Iacob his transgression, and Is∣raell his sinne. Heare this I beseech you,Verse 9. ô ye heads of the house of Ia∣cob, and leaders of the house of Israell, which commit abhominable thinges, and writhe and peruert al iudgement and equitie.
