Here is the strength the courage of the Prophet of God, euen Gods spirit. Here is his office, to tell Iudah their transgressions,verse 10. Acts. 7.15 and Israell their sinnes. Stephen was ful of this spirit, when he rebuked the obstinate and stifnecked Iewes. These sectaries, these pseudocatholikes shal lacke this spirit, they shall not be able to vnderstand the scrip∣tures: they shall lacke iudgement; the scriptures shall bee vnsa∣uorie vnto them. But you beloued,Text verse 20 building forward your selues in your most holie faith, and praying in the holie ghost; keepe your selues in the loue of God, looking for the mercy of our Lorde Iesus Christ to euerlasting life.] The Apostle hauing sufficientlie made manifest to all men the former deceiuers: now he concludeth with a generall exhor∣tation, to all true christians; and he sheweth in it, what true chri∣stians ought to doe. He putteth down certaine principall pointes of christian religion against their Antichristian superstition. One contrarie placed by another, is made more bright: So this com∣paring of false religion and true together, will adde light to the truth. And the first point of true christian religion is, to build for∣ward our selues in our most holie faith. By this place then is proued that it is a chiefe point of christian religion, that al christians should be builders: that is, should make themselues a fit temple for God, to dwell in.1. Chro. 17.1.4 Wee reade what care Dauid had to build Gods tem∣ple; but God would not suffer him: but nowe, euerie man must build a temple to God, euen his owne soule. We reade what cost Salomon bestowed vpon the temple;2. Chro 4. 1. Pet. 2.5. but now God careth not for such temples made of stone; he will haue a temple of liuely stones; we must be his temple. And to build this temple for him, it must be the first worke we should do. Seeing then this worke of buil∣ding the Lordes temple, is so necessarie and so generall, it behoo∣ueth
euerie man to learne how to build; and that is, by the know∣ledge of the scriptures. What Mason can builde a wall, without rule or square? The rule or square of christian building, is the word of God. By it our harts & soules are squared & framed fit for Gods walles. And therefore S. Paul, taking his leaue of the church of Ephesus:Act. 20.32 commendeth them to God, and to the word of his grace, which (saieth he) is able to build further, and to giue them inheritāce with all them that are sanctified.2. Pet. 3.18 And therefore S. Peter saith, grow in grace, and in the knowledge of our Lorde Iesus Christ: and Saint Paul thankes God for the Thessalonians,2. Thes. 1.2 that their faith grewe excee∣dinglie. Why then, euerie christian must know Gods word, or else how shall he be able to builde? would anie of vs allowe, or giue wages to a worke man, that shoulde builde our walles without line, rule or square? no more will God allowe anie in his spiritu∣all building.1. Pet. 2.4 Of this building S. Peter also speaketh: Ye are come to the Lorde Iesus as to a liuing stone, reiected of men; but precious and chosen of God: wherefore you your selues bee built as liuelie stones,1. Cor. 14.27. a spirituall house: and S. Paul. Let all things bee done to edifi∣cation: that is, let this bee the ende of all thy workes, the buil∣ding of Gods spirituall temple: Be more carefull to build it, then Salomon was for his temple.1. King. 5.14 If Salomons workmen were one mo∣neth in Libanus, about the worke of the temple; and two moneths at home, about their owne businesse: Let vs exceede them, let vs emploie two moneths about the Lordes building, and but one a∣bout our owne businesse.Matth. 6.33. Let vs first seeke the kingdom of God, and al things else shalbe added vnto vs. Let all our other workes giue place to the Lords worke. And here we must not onlie build our selues by reading, & hea∣ring,1 Cor. 14.35 and meditating of the word of God: but we must also build our wiues, as these places proue. If wiues wil learne anything, let them aske their husbandes at home: they ought to bee able to teach them.1. Pet. 3.7 And ye husbands dwell with your wiues according to know∣ledge, that is, knowing the law of God, and according to that, dealing and gouerning. And our brethren also, as S. Paul com∣mandeth.1. Thes. 5.11 Rom. 15.2 Edifie one another, euen as you doe, and let euerie man please his neighbour in that which is good, to edification. But es∣peciallie we must edifie our children. A sonne in Hebrew is called Ben, that is, a building, because the father should especiallie build his sonne in religion and vertue. Nature teacheth all men this:
The sauage beare fashioneth her whelpes beeing deformed with her tongue: So shoulde all christians with gentle admonitions, frame the deformed maners of their children. The Doe her fawn being young, will hide it in the thicket, will cherish it; but beeing waxen strong, she will thrust it out, and make it seeke for liuing it selfe: So should parents their children being yong, nourish them at home: but now waxen strong, send them out into the common wealth. The Tyger when she perceiueth that her whelps are stolen awaie, when shee, being verie swift of fool, cannot recouer them, (the théeues by taking ship, and passing ouer the sea hauing pre∣uented her) on the shoare for sorrowe shee will kill her selfe: and shall it not grieue christian parentes more? to see their children, by the deuill stolen from them, and hoyst vp vpon the vaine sea of this worlde to all sinne and wickednesse? That commandement of the lawe, whereby fathers were bounde to teach their children,Deut. 6.10 that the passeouer ment: teacheth them this building. And that children ought to know the scriptures: the 119. Psalme,Psal.  19. which like an alphabet is made for them, plainlie prooueth. All the ver∣ses of that Psalme, beginne with Hebrewe letters, in order as they are in the alphabet. By if they may not onelie learne the let∣ters, but the principles of religion: and also the second part of that Psalme teacheth the same most euidentlie. Where withall shall a young man cleanse his way (saieth Dauid?) euen by ruling himselfe after thy word. Why then young men must knowe the worde of God. And Saint Paul writeth, that Timothy knewe the scriptures,2. Tim. 3.15 euen from his childhood. No doubt his grandmother Lois, and his mother Eunice, (whose faith hee commendeth a little before,) had taught him them. And Saint Iohn to all young men thus writeth: you are strong, and you haue ouercommed the wicked:1. Ioh. 2.13 because the word of God dwelleth in you. So Isaac no doubt, knew what sacri∣ficement; being a childe, he coulde saie: father, here is the woode,Gen. 22.7. where is the sacrifice? So that then, if wee will haue our children leade a pure life, if we wil haue them strong, if we will haue them ouercome the deuill, if we will haue them true catholicks, sonnes of Abraham: we must see, that the worde of God dwell and abide in them. They must not knowe it onelie: but as in their carnall weapons, they must bee cunning in it. So that then, the papists heretofore in their manie workes they did, and whereof they brag; they left this principall work vndone, They did not build thēselues
by the word of God, in their most holy faith. That worke which God himselfe commanded from heauen, that is: This is my belo∣ued sonne,Mark. 9.7 heare him, these did not, they minded not, they heard not the gospell of Iesus Christ. Their guides, and master-worke men, tooke the rule and square out of mens handes, and who then could build? Therefore in this very pointe, they declare themselues to be those, whome S. Iude here condemnes: They are no builders in the most holy faith. All true christians and catholiques must bee builders, and that by the leuell or square of Gods word. Text. Phil. 2.15.And that in the most holie faith.] Christians must shine as lights in the world. Now what fellowship is betwixt light and darkenesse? saith Saint Paul. Their libertie must not bee an occasion to the flesh: They must not nowe sinne,2 Cor. 6.15 Gal 5.14. Rom. 6.1 2. Tim. 2.19 2. Pet. 1.5. that grace may abounde. Let him vtter∣lie detest iniquitie now, that nameth the Lord Iesus. Our faith must be holie, and therefore S. Peter saith: Ioyne to your faith vertue, to your vertue knowledge, &c. Our faith must haue al vertues linked to it: Such a faith had the first christians; they coulde be a touched with no open crime,Eus. eccle. Hist. lib. 3. ca 32. or notorious fault: but that they sung psalmes to Iesus before daie, as Plinius Secundus writeth of them to the Emperour.Matth. 5.20. Our Sauiour tolde his disciples, that their righteousnesse must exceede the righteousnesse of the Scribes and Pharisies: and so must we now tell all christians, that theirs must excéede Turkes and Paganes, or else they shall neuer enter into heauen. And yet (as it is reported) their faith in their dealinges, their religion in swearing, their zeale in seruing their deuilish gods; farre excee∣deth ours. God stirre vs vp, and pricke vs forward; that we may one build another in our most holie faith, and that we may exceed them. Text.Praying in the holy ghost.] Praier is one of the chiefest exercises of true religion. And therefore after the building and encrease of faith, the apostle addeth praier, which is a speciall meanes to ob∣taine the same.Luk 17.5 And therefore the apostle praied: O Lord increase our faith. But because our heart of it selfe is vnfit to praie, and we cannot of our selues,2 Cor. 3.5 Ezech. 36.26. Zach. 7.12. Gen 6, 5. so much as thinke a good thought; and the heart of man vnregenerate, is called a stony heart and an adamant by the prophet; and Moses saieth, that all the deuises of it are euill euen continuallie: Therefore the apostle teacheth vs here, if we will pray acceptablie, to pray in the holy ghost. And the holie ghost helpeth our infirmitie in praier,Rom. 8.25 as S. Paul teacheth vs: Likewise the spirit
(saith he) also helpeth our infirmitie; for we know not what to pray, as we ought: but the spirit it selfe maketh requests for vs, with sighes which cannot be expressed. Of this,Heb. 5.7 came those sighes and grones of our sauiour, whereof we read: Who in the daies of his flesh, did offer vp praiers and supplications with strong cryings and teares: And of Dauid, Heare the right ô Lord, consider my complaint,Psal. 6.6.17.1 37.10 and hear∣ken to my praier, that goeth not out of fained lippes: and I am wea∣rie of my groning: and Lorde thou knowest all my desires, and my groning is not hid from thee. So then the spirit maketh vs knowe what to aske, it maketh vs to praie feruentlie, euen with sighing and groning. In warre, the soldiors do not onlie fight with hand: but crie with voices against the enemie. This crie of the voice, in our spirituall warfare, praier is:Ephe. 6.18 and therefore S. Paul hauing ar∣med a christian soldiour perfectlie; hee addes, praying with all ma∣ner of prayer, and supplication in the spirit: and watching thereunto, with all perseuerance. Thus (Iosuah fighting with the hand,Exod. 17.11) Moses cried with the voice against Amalecke: and it is saide there, that Moses praying to God with his voice, did more preuaile then Io∣suah with his sworde. Such an excellent thing praier is, against our spirituall enemie the Deuill. And therefore they are not cap∣taines or leaders: but traitours to Gods people, that take from them the sword of the spirit, that is, the word of God, and this cry∣ing and courage of the heart, christian praier. To pray in the spirit, is to know what we praie for, to praie with sighing and groning, to praie with faith and assurance.Rom. 8.16 For the spirit of God doeth assu∣redlie witnesse to our spirit, that we are Gods children. But to praie in latine, taketh away all these. They which praie so, know not for what they praie; and therefore cannot sigh or grone in their praiers, which sighing procéedeth of wanting:Mat. 15.22. As we read of the woman of Canaan, who being touched no doubt at the hart, with the sicknesse of her daughter, cried after our sauiour: and the men of Niniue, knowing and fearing their destruction, fasted and prai∣ed to the Lorde strongly, and mightely.Io. 3.8. So that then the papistes heretofore haue not praied in ye spirit, they haue not had the right vse of praier, they haue taken from christian soldiours, this chiefe helpe against satan their spirituall enemie. Keepe your selues in the loue of God.Text v. 21] Here is another spiritu∣all point of true catholique religion: You beloued (saith S. Iude) building your selues in your most holy faith, and praying in the holie
ghost: keepe your selues in the loue of God.] This is the chiefe worke of all; In anie wise doe this: Be ye sure that God loueth you. And here let vs marke well the first assault of our enemie,Gen. 3.5. God doth knowe (saith he) how that in what day ye shall eate of that tree, your eies shall be opened, and yee shall be as Gods, knowing good and euill. He goeth about to perswade Eue, that God loueth her not, that he enuieth mans welfare. And not onely sathan: but our owne flesh, will go about, thus oftentimes to perswade vs, as Dauid telleth vs:Psal. 30.23. And I said in my haste, I am cast out of the sight of thine eies. Because God doth not heare vs by and by when we pray, we thinke that he loueth vs not, that hee hath cast vs out of his sight: Neuerthelesse (saith Dauid) thou heardest my praier when I called vpon thee. And the wicked also will cast this in our téeth: Tush,Psal. 71.9. Mat. 27.43. God careth not for him: persecute him and take him, there is none to deliuer him. And so the Priestes and Pharises vpbraided our sauiour Christ: hee trusted in God that he would saue him; let him deliuer him, if he will haue him. Against all these temptations, we must arme our selues, and most assuredly keepe vs in the loue of God, as in a most strong tower. This is that which Dauid saith so often:Psal. 18.1.61.3. The Lord is my stony rocke and my defence: and thou hast beene my hope, and a strong tower for me against the enemy. And the name of the Lorde is a strong tower,Pro. 18.10. the righteous runnes into it, and is exalted. And this loue of God towards vs, that we should not doubt of it, is confirmed to vs, as a most strong? su soldi∣er, by manie places of scripture. Our sauiour praieth to his fa∣ther,Io. 17.23. that al his may be one with him, as he is one with his father; that the world may knowe, that God sent him, and that he loued all his: euen as he loued him. What can be saide more then this? God lo∣ueth his, and that not coldely, after the maner of manie men: but euen as hee loued Iesus Christ, that is, with vnspeakeable and most assured loue.Rom. 5.5.8.38. And S. Paul saieth, the loue of God is poured out into our harts, by the holy ghost. And againe, I am perswaded, that neither death, nor life, nor angels, nor height, nor depth, nor any other creatures in the world, are able to separate vs from the loue of God, which is in Iesus Christ. All the creatures in the world, are not able to batter this castle.1. Pet. 5.7. And in another place, Cast your care on him, for hee careth for you: He that careth for one loueth him. This care and loue of God towardes vs, our sauiour teacheth all his,Luke 12.4. as a sure rocke against persecution. And I say vnto you, my
friendes, be not affraid of them that kill the body; and after that, are not able to doe any more: but feare him, which after hee hath killed, can cast into hell. And after:Luke 12. v. 6.7. are not fiue sparrowes bought for two farthings, and yet not one of them is forgotten before God? Yea all the haires of your head are numbred: feare not therefore, ye are more of valew then many sparrowes. And our sauiour himselfe saith, No mā can haue greater loue then this; to giue his life for his friends. And it is said of him: that he loued his vnto the end.Io. 15.13.13. v. 1. Rom. 8.15. The holy ghost also maketh all christians to crie, abba, father, which is a name of loue. And our sauiour teacheth all his to praie thus: Our father, &c.Mat. 6.9. He that bids vs call God, our father, teacheth that he loueth vs. And S. Iohn saith: We knowe and beleeue the loue of God towardes vs:1. Ioh. 4.16. then we doubt not of it. The loue of God, is the fountaine of all our good thinges we enioie at Gods handes.Ephes. 1.4.6. Hee hath chosen vs through loue and through grace, and not through any thing in vs, saith the Apostle. He that stoppeth this fountaine: stops the well of life. So that then all christians must kéepe them in the loue of God, as in a most sure castle. This loue of God must be their trust in all thinges, euen in the assaultes of sathan,2. Cor. 12.9. as it was taught S. Paul: my grace is sufficient for thee. Let not sathan by all his sleightes or deuises at anie time, driue vs awaie from this:Heb. 2.4. Let this alwaies be our castle. Behold saieth the Prophet Habacucke (gnuphlah) he that trusteth in himselfe as in a tower, that reacheth to the heauens, (be he neuer so politique, as Herod: neuer so high in authoritie, as Nabuchadnezar: neuer so mightie as Goliah) his soule is not right in him. The iust shall liue by faith in his God: that is his life, his castle, his refuge. Looking for the mercy of our Lord Iesus Christ vnto eternall life.Text.] This great mercie of God towardes vs, is declared by two nota∣ble allegories in the word of God, First by the prophet Esay:Esay 51. Har∣ken vnto me ye zealous followers of righteousnesse, you that pursue after it, euen as the hart doth after the water floud:Psal. 42.1. ye seekers of the Lord, looke vnto the rocke, whereout ye were hewen, and vnto the hole of the pit, whereout ye were digged. As though the Prophet should teach them, that are nowe zealous in religion, and forward in good workes; that they should remēber from whence they came, and what they were in the beginning: least they should be proude. They should not consider their white feathers: but their foule, and blacke legges, with the swanne. They were all, as rude stones,
hewed out of a rocke; polished, squared, and made fit for the tem∣ple of God, euen by God himselfe. They were all, as taken out of a most déepe and filthie pit, all defiled with myre and claie, wash∣ed with cleane water powred on them, euen of the louing mercy of God himselfe; and that the best of them were no better: God biddeth them looke to Abraham their father, and to Sarah that bare them. For God called him alone, and blessed him, and multipli∣ed him.Gen. 12.1.4. Abraham would haue dwelt in Vr of the Chaldees still, if God had not called him thence. And this first calling of God, is repeated twise, Gen. 12. v. 1. & 4. And he feared his life in Egypt: and Sarah laughed behinde the tent doore.Gen. 18.12.12.11. Here were apparant imperfections in Abraham, and Sarah: Here are manifest argu∣ments, of Gods great mercy. And by the prophet Ezechiell; Thus the Lorde commndeth the prophet to saie to Ierusalem:Ezech. 16.4. Thy ha∣bitation and thy kinred was from the lande of Canaan: Thy father was an Amorite, and thy mother an Hittite. As though hee should saie; before thy natiuitie thou hast nothing to bragge of; as ma∣nie men are wont to bragge of their pedegrees, and of their nobi∣litie and vertue. In this spirituall generation, all pedegrees must cease; but the pedegrees of shame and confusion. (And in thy nati∣uitie in this case thou wast: Thy nauel was not cut, thou wast not wa∣shed in water, to soften thee; thou wast not salted with salt, nor swad∣led in cloutes. No eie pitied thee, to doe any of these vnto thee, or to haue compassion vpon thee; and thou wast cast into the open field, in contempt of thy soule, in the day thou wast borne.) Man had no an∣cestour to glorie in, nor no friende to helpe or pittie him, in the daie of his birth. (And when I passed by thee, I sawe thee polluted with thine owne bloud, and I saide vnto thee, in thine owne bloud, liue: and I said to thee, in thine own bloud, liue:) Here is mans mi∣serable estate, destitute of all helpe, polluted in his owne bloud, euen at deathes doore: and here is Gods great mercie, euen then, to saie liue. And least this great benefit should be forgotten, both ye miserie, and the benefit, is twise repeated: I said vnto thee, in thine owne bloud, liue; I said vnto thee in thine own bloud, liue. And this same our frée saluation, of the meere grace and mercie of God without anie thing in vs, is likewise repeated of S. Paul twise, 2. Ephes. vers. 5.Eph. 2.5. Verse 8. When we were dead by our sinnes, hee hath quickned vs together in Christ: by grace ye are saued. And againe in 8. verse for by grace ye are saued, through faith, and that not of your selues, it
is the gift of God, not of workes, least any man should boast in him∣selfe. God would haue man challenge to himselfe nothing, nor bragge of anie part of his saluation: that glorie he reserueth on∣ly and wholie to himselfe. Neither hath God alone thus giuen man life: but adorned him, but sanctified him; as followeth in the prophet. I caused thee to multiplie, as the budde of the fielde, to in∣crease, to waxe great; I caused thee to haue ornaments of ornaments: that is most excellent ornaments. Thy brests are fashioned, and thy haire is growen: whereas thou wast naked and bare. Now when I passed by thee, and looked vpon thee, behold thy time was the time of loue. Where this worde, behold is in the scriptures, there fol∣loweth some strange and wonderfull thing. One in this case, was beloued: this was the time of loue. To loue one beautifull or braue∣lie attyred, were no maruell: but to loue one thus defiled, thus deformed, thus naked, in this miserable estate, O thing most won∣derfull. And such was the time, when God loued vs first: Euen then: It followeth in the prophet, I spread out my skirtes ouer thee, and couered thy filthinesse. Yea I sware vnto thee, and came into a league or couenant with thee (saith the Lord God Iehoua) and thou becamest mine. Then I washed thee with water, and I washed thy bloud from thee, and I annointed thee with oile, and adorned thee with all manner of costly ornaments. Here is Gods great mercy set out to vs ward, by a most liuelie example.Rom. 5.8.9. And if God shewed this great mercie vppon vs, being his enemies: what shall wee hope for, now being iustified, and being his friendes? If he shew∣ed this in our birth: what shall we hope for, at our latter ende, at our iudgment? And surely this is the only staffe we must lean to. And therefore Dauid saith,Psal. 130.3. 1. Io. 2.1. If thou Lord wilt marke what is done a∣misse, who may abide it? And S. Iohn saieth, If any man sinne wee haue an aduocate with the father Iesus Christ the righteous, and he is the propitiation for our sinnes: and not for ours only, but for the sins of the whole world. Iesus Christ was the propitiation of the Apo∣stles sinnes: And S. Paul saith, God hath shut all vnder vnbeliefe,Rom. 11.32. that he might haue mercy on all. So that all must come to God for their saluation, like beggers, like damned & guiltie prisoners, and must he saued by pardon: not by pleading innocencie. And in another place he concludeth: that all mouthes must be stopped, and the whole world must be subiect, that is, must yéeld themselues as guiltie, to the condemnation of God.Rom. 3.19. No man must bragge of
his workes, or challenge anie merit before the maiestie of God. The workes which the Pharisie did,Luke 18.11. were good workes, as to fast, to pray, to pay his tithes: but he bragged of them, he trusted in them, he confessed not, that he was an vnprofitable seruant, hee looked not for, he desired not the mercie of God, for his saluation: and ther∣fore hee was reprooued. For who amongst men, will bragge of that, which is not his owne? And such like are our good workes: They are none of ours; they are the free giftes of God. Hee hath wrought all our workes in vs,Es. 26, 12. Ephes. 2.10. saith the Prophet. And againe, S. Paul saith, we are his workmanship, being created in Christ Iesus to good workes, which God hath prepared before, that wee should walke in them. Here is a second creation in Iesus Christ, to good workes: so that they wholy belong to Gods grace. Mans nature of it selfe, can challenge no part of them. Therefore it hath nothing to brag of, as concerning them: Nay we being regenerate haue not so much of our selues, as of our selues, as to thinke a good thought, or to deuise a good worke. For it is said also, that God hath prepared them long before, that we should walke in them. And therfore S. Au∣gustine writeth thus verie excellently,In Enchirid. ad Laurent. de fide cap. 32. and manifestly concerning Gods frée mercie, and mans frée will. Againe (saieth he) least anie man should brag, although not of his workes, but of his free will, as though desert had his beginning of that, to which the reward of do∣ing well as due, should be requited; let liberty her selfe, euen the freest man in the world, heare the preacher of grace, saying: It is God that worketh in you, both to wil and to worke, according to his good plea∣sure. And in another place: Therefore it is not of him that willeth, or of him that runneth: but it is of God, that hath mercy. And after he expoundes this thus against our Semipelagianists, that ioine grace and nature together: If it be said, It is not of him that willeth, or of him that runneth, but of God shewing mercy; because it is of them both, that is both of the will of man, and mercy of God, that we should thus vnderstand it to bee meant: It is not of him that willeth, or of him that rūneth, but of God shewing mercy; as though it should be said, the wil of man alone sufficeth not, if the mercy of God be not there also; nor the only mercy of God, if the will of man be not there also. And in this sense, if it bee well said so, that (it is not of man wil∣ling, but of God shewing mercy,) because mans will alone is not a∣ble to bring it to passe; why may it not then on the contrary, be as wel said, It is not of God shewing mercy, but of man willing; because the
mercy of God alone also, doth not bring it to passe? Therefore if no christian dare say, It is not of God shewing mercy, but of mans wil∣ling, least hee should most manifestly speake against the Apostle: it remaines, that therefore it is truely saide, It is not of man willing or running, but of God shewing mercy; that all may be yeelded to God, who prepareth mans good will, that it may be helped, and helpeth it also being prepared. Mans good will goeth before many of the gifts of God; but not all: but those which it doth not go before, it is among them it selfe. Thus farre Augustine most plainly writing of the christian faith to Laurentius, not disputing earnestly against Pela∣gius; and so by heate of disputation, caried ouer much to speake in the commendation of Gods grace, to depresse the pride of mans nature, as some haue written: And his opinion is grounded vpon the scripture so firmely, as all the enemies of Gods grace, shall neuer be able to ouerthrow it. But most manifestly in his booke of Retractations he taketh away this obiection & friuolous cauil. For first he retracts nothing out of this booke ad Laurentiū de fide. And againe,Ret. lib. 1. cap. 9. Behold (saith he) how long before the Pelagian heresie sprang, we haue so disputed, euen as though we had disputed against them. So that Augustine neuer changed his opinion in this mat∣ter. He was of the same mind before Pelagius and his heresie was hatched: as he was also after. So that then Augustines opinion is cleare, that man of himselfe, can challenge no part of merit, for his good workes: and that God when he crownes our good works, crowneth his owne giftes. Man must therfore ascribe all his sal∣uation wholie to God, and no part thereof to himselfe. And in ano∣ther place he saith, O Lord my strength,Meditat. li. 1. c. 5. there shall no flesh be iustifi∣ed in thy sight. My trust is not in the sons of men, whom if thou shalt iudge, setting mercy aside, shalt thou finde righteous? & vnlesse thou preuentest by shewing mercy vpon the wicked, there is none that shal glorifie thee being mercifull. As concerning his regeneration then (as these two allegories of Esay & Ezechiel do prooue) as concerning his daily preseruation and finall coronation, as Dauid, S. Paul, and the fathers Augustine and Bernard do affirme; and as concerning his remuneration, as S. Iude here teacheth: Euerie one must looke for the mercy of Iesus Christ to his saluation. The summe of all this, our sauiour the wise∣dome of God the father, comprehends in two words, as the toppe of all happinesse & felicitie: Blessed (saith he) are the poore in spirit,Mat. 5.3.
for theirs is the kingdome of God. Here is the toppe of blessednesse, to be poore in spirit. And what meaneth this, Our sauiour in ano∣ther place expoundes it,Luke 17.10. when as you haue done al you can, (saith he) say you are vnprofitable seruants, and we haue done but that was our duety to doe: That is, not to trust in our works, as the Pharises did, not to iustifie our selues. This God cannot abide; they that do so, though they fast often, and pray long praiers; the kingdome of hell is theirs. They are poore in spirit, which with Marie, though they excell in good works,Such a one was the womā of Canaan, who acknow∣ledged her selfe euen a dogge. as she did: yet thinke themselues as no bodie in Gods sight, and account of themselues basely with her, as those her wordes declare. Thou hast respected not the humility (which is a rare & excellent vertue) but rather the. Psal. 8.4. base & vile estate of thy handmaid: for so the gréek word signifieth, who account my selfe as a vile woman before thee: And saie with Dauid, What am I, that thou visitest me, or that thou regardest me? Such a poore man in spirit was our father Abraham, who though he were rich in good works:Gen. 18.27. Gen. 32.10. Iob. 15.15. yet called himselfe, speaking to God, dust and ashes. Such a one was Iacob, who confessed himselfe lesse then all the mercies of God. Hereof Iob said, If the heauens be not cleane in thy sight, how much more man, being borne of a woman, a very wonne. Here∣of Dauid called himselfe, a worme and no man. Hereof Paul called himselfe,Psal. 22.6. the least of the Apostles, and not worthy to be called an A∣postle.1. Cor. 15.9. Hereof our sauiour himselfe the chiefe patterne of all vir∣tues, would not haue his most glorious workes to be preached or published abroad:Mat. 9.30. to giue vs an ensāple, that we should not brag of our workes. And when as his Apostles had returned againe, and dare great miracles, and reioiced therein, he taught them not to reioice in their owne works: but in the mercy of God towards them, and that their names were written in heauen. Here is the on∣ly cause of reioicing,Luke, 10.21. that he that wil reioice, must reioice in ye Lord. And againe, that we must not reioice, in things priuate or proper to our selues (as the most part of the world doth at this daie) but in thinges common to all their brethren, that they haue one God, one father, one sauiour, one faith, one baptisme, one common inhe∣ritance. These should cause vs to reioice, & not here on earth, our priuate worldly commodities. But to let these ancient Patriarks passe, euen many of the Paganes, who were otherwise very gréedy of vaine glorie,Plut. in Apol. haue béene but poore in spirit. Alexander the great; when as his friendes bragged that hee had done more, then euer
Hercules had don: Truly (saith he) I do not think yt al my acts with my whole Empire are to be cōpared to one word yt Hercules spoke.Gal. 7. li. Therap. And Galen that famous Phisition did so disdain the peoples com∣mendation, that hee neuer put his name to anie of his workes. And he earnestlie requested his friendes, that they would not doe it after his death, being desirous onelie of knowledge and truth; Accounting (saith he) no possession more pretious then vertue, I neuer put my name to any of my bookes. What shall I speake of these Paganes, the fathers themselues verie excellentlie haue taught vs this lesson.Manual. ca. 23 Augustine writes thus: That hee doth God great wrong which distrusts in his mercie. As much as in him lieth; he denieth God to haue loue, truth, and pow∣er, wherein all my hope consists: in the charity of his adoption, in the truth of his promise, and in the power of his redemption Let my foo∣lish conscience murmure as much as it will, saying, who art thou? and howe great is that glory? by what merits doest thou hope to ob∣taine it? And I will answere boldlie, I know whom I haue beleeued. For through exceeding great loue he hath adopted me to be his son: and hee is true in his promise, and mightie in his performance: hee is able to doe what pleaseth him. I cannot bee terrified with the multi∣tude of my sinnes: if I remember the death of my Lorde, my sinnes cannot ouercome him. Here we may plainlie see howe Augustine was poore in spirit, his whole trust was in the loue, mercie, and power of God. Here is no mention of his owne workes or me∣rits. Bernard also in a gréeuous sicknesse,Author vitae. seemed to be arraigned at Gods iudgement seate, and was there accused of sathan; and there despairing of the righteousnesse of his owne merits: I con∣fesse (saith he) that I am not worthie, nor by my owne merits that I can obtaine the kingdom of heauen. But my Lord, possessing it by a double right: by the inheritance of his father, and by the merits of his passion: being content with the one himself, he hath giuen me ye other. By whose gift. I lawfully challenge that vnto me, and shal not be con∣founded. Here we may also see plainly Bernards claime to ye king¦dom of heauen: ye free gift of Iesus Christ, his merits, his passion. Hee was also poore in spirit, hee had not anie merit or worke of his owne to plead. But to come to our daies; that same saying of Cosmus Medices, the grandfather of that familie,Ludo. Guici∣ard. in diludiis. who was ador∣ned with the name of the wise: When as hee had bestowed fortie thousand rials vpon hospitals, & monasteries, and churches, and
was therefore commended of one, who tolde him, that hee might looke for a recompence at Gods hande, who was a patrone of the poore. He answered, that he could neuer finde as yet in his billes of reckonings, any mention of these expēses. Surelie, as should seeme, hee followed the counsell of our sauiour in giuing of almes: Let not thy left hand knowe what thy right doth:Matt. 6.3 Hee neuer writ nor made anie reckoning of that he gaue to the poore; he was poore in spirit, he confessed it was but his duty to bestow that he bestowed, and ten thousand more if he had béene able. And that no mans righteousnes consisteth in himselfe, though he had done neuer so manie good workes,Epist. ad Diognes Iustine the martyr thus verie excellentlie teacheth: But when our naughtinesse was comen to a perfection, and that it was made manifest, that the reward of sin was punishment, and death was to bee looked for, and the time ap∣pointed of God was come, to declare from henceforth his liberalitie and power, and how for the vnmeasurable loue he loueth men, hee hath not hated vs, neither hath he forsaken vs, neither hath he shew∣ed himselfe mindfull of our sins; but hath patiently borne it, and hath taken vppon him our sinnes. Hee hath giuen his owne sonne to bee the price of redemption for vs; the holy, for them that transgressed the lawe; the good for the euill, the iust for the vniust, one that knewe no corruption, for them that were guiltie of corruption, the immor∣tall for the mortall. For what other thing could couer our sinnes, but his righteousnesse? In what other man can we wicked and vngodlie wretches be counted for iust, but onely in the sonne of God? O sweet permutation! Oh vnsearchable cunning! oh kindnesse aboue all ex∣pectation! that truly the iniquity of many should be hidden in one iust person; and the righteousnesse of one, should make that manie iust persons should be counted for iust. Here we may plainelie set that doctrine of imputation of Christes righteousnesse, which the church of Rome nowe cannot abide, accounted as catholique, in Iustine the martyrs daies: His righteousnesse onlie couers our sinnes; and we vnworthie sinners can be accounted iust in none other but in him. This is then our righteousnesse, to haue our sins couered and to be accounted righteous in Iesus Christ. S. Paul saieth, The wages of sinne is death: But eternall life (is no wages) it is the gift of God (as the word  importeth) in our Lord Iesus Christ.Rom. 6.23 Mat. 25.34 . And our sauiour calleth eternall life an inheri∣tance, which in ye gréek taketh his name of Lots, whereof Salomon
writes thus: The Lots are cast into the lappe,Pro. 13.6 but the whole dispo∣sition thereof is of the Lord. So that in those things, which are don by lots, man hath nothing to doe, there is no respect of him: but all is of the Lorde. Such an inheritance is our heauenlie inheri∣tance. Ferus writing of Iosuah his diuision of the land of Canaan, saith thus. It is to be obserued (saith he) that Iosuah deuided the land by no other meanes then by lots, committing freely the disposition of the matter to God, by whome the lots are gouerned: that hee might purchase himselfe lesse enuy, and euery man might so receiue his in∣heritance, as giuen him of God. And so he that receiued more, should giue more thankes, and he that receiued lesse, should not murmure a∣gainst men; but should hope in God that hee could giue him more: Euen so Christ deuided his land by lots. For our electiō is of the grace of God, &c. Whosoeuer the refore in the church, hath Christ Iesus for his possession or inheritance: let him know, that it is of grace, and not of merit: that all mouthes should be stopped, and he that will reioice, must reioice in the Lord alone. No man in that inhe∣ritance might attribute it to his valiantnesse in fighting, or to a∣nie great exploit that he had done, more then anie other. It was not Gods will that anie then should do so: No more may wee in our heauenlie inheritance when we haue done what we can. The mmot in gréeke, is called ,Pro. 6. ver. 6 and thereof commeth  a schoolehouse. And surelie verie fitlie. For she may bee a schoolemistresse to christians in manie vertues; as Salomon also himselfe sendeth the sluggard to her to learne. But as she hath ma∣nie excellent properties, as to prouide against the time to come, and that not the basest, but the best corne, that is wheate: yea and that she will carrie a corne, euen bigger then her selfe, that she is girle about the bellie, and that shee hath winges on her former partes, As she may teach all christians by these, to prouide also a∣gainst the time to come, and that not base, but excellent workes: and that no man should excuse his inhabilitie, seeing she wil beare a graine, as big as her selfe: and that she is girl about the bellie, that wee shoulde also vse abstinence, and fast, if we will haue the winges of angels: So her name in the Hebrew no doubt giuen her, of her chiefest propertie, teacheth all christians the most excel∣lentest lesson of all; she is called Nemalah a gnawer, because she gnawes off both ends of her corne; least they should sprout in win∣ter, and so become vnprofitable to her when she had gathered it.
Herein especiallie must all christians follow this Emmot, when they haue done all they can, if they will haue their workes doe them any good: they must gnaw off both endes of them; that is, bragging of them, which may be compared to the vpper ende; and trust in them, which may be compared to the lower ende. For lack of this, both the Pharisies and the Paganes (which were greate workers) lost all their workes: and it is to be feared the Papistes also. All christians must take heede by the example of Lot, who (as Origen allegoriseth on verie finelie) after hee had escaped the fire, both of couetousnesse and lust in Sodome, and the brimstone of their stinking conuersation; who is called in Hebrew Lot, that is, most precious frankensence: yet after he had attained to the hill of perfection, from Soar, that is, a small citie, as he calleth it: begot of his two daughters Benammi the son of the people, which may resemble vaine glorie, and Moab, which is in Hebrewe, the fa∣ther of them; which may resemble trust or confidence. Which two nations (the Moabits and the Amonites) were banished the con∣gregation of Israell to the fourth generation. Let all christians though they be Lot, that is, excellēt in good works, beware of these two children, Ammon and Moab; that is, of vaine glorie and con∣fidence: these two shall marre all their works: they are outlawes from Gods church. To conclude, Iesus Christ is the heade of his church and of all his members,Ephe. 1.22 as S. Paul calleth him: And as the heade beeing aboue the water, the bodie cannot drown; so we beléeue verilie, that our heade being in heauen, all the waues and troubles of afflictions, and of our sinnes whatsoeuer cannot drown anie one of his mem∣bers.Ephe. 5.23.24 He is the spouse of his church, as S. Paul testifieth. And there∣fore, euen as no man will sue the wife at the lawe for anie debte; so we beleeue that in the manifold debts of our sinnes, which euen thousand thousands in number the best of vs all doe owe to God, and in all sathans inditements, and in the accusations of our own consciences, Iesus Christ shall answere for vs: Hee is our hus∣band. As Dauid also beléeued when hee said, Thou shalt answere for me,Psal. 38.15 Rom. 8 33 ô Lord my God: And as S. Paul saith, Who shall lay anie thing to the charge of Gods chosen? It is God that iustifieth, who shall condemne? It is Christ which is dead, yea or rather which is ri∣sen againe, which is also at the right hande of God, and makes re∣quests
for vs. The accuser of our brethren nowe (saieth S. Iohn) is thrown down from heauen:Reu. 10.1 he dare not nowe there against Gods elect once shew his face, or open his mouth: Wee haue there such a mightie sauiour, such a louing husbande. What shall separate vs from the loue of Christ (saith S. Paul) shall tribulation or anguish, or persecution, or famine or nakednesse, or peril, or sword? as it is writ∣ten, for thy sake are we killed all the day long, and are accounted as sheepe for the slaughter. Here is the state of all christians in this world. But what is their comfort in all these externall euils, nay in death it selfe? Neuerthelesse (saith the Apostle) in all these things we are more then conquerers, we conquer exceedingly through him that loued vs. The loue of our husband Iesus Christ, which wee be∣leeue hee hath towardes vs, makes vs conquerours in all these. This is that which S. Paul saith to the Philippians,Phil. 1.21 That Christ to his, bo in life and in death is aduantage. Nay the Apostle is so certaine of this loue of Iesus Christ, that hee saieth it more vehe∣mentlie, and addeth: I am certainlie perswaded, that neither death nor life, nor angels nor principalities, nor powers, nor things present, nor things to come, nor height nor depth, nor any other creature can remoue it. If all these shoulde conspire together, or goe about to bring Gods elect out of his fauour by accusing them: yet all these were not able to separate vs from the loue of God, which is to vs ward by the meanes of Iesus Christ. Iesus Christ is the most lo∣uing and constant husbande to his spouse that euer was. Iesus Christ is our garment: and therefore the Apostle saieth,Gal. 3.27 As ma∣ny as are baptised, haue put on Iesus Christ. And therefore as a gar∣ment couers all the nakednesse, the botches and blemishes of the bodie: so wee beléeue, that Iesus Christ couers all the naked∣nesse, imperfections, vlcers, and blemishes of all his. And there∣fore Dauid saith, Blessed is the man,Psal. 32.1. 1. Epist. c. 2. v. 2 Psal. 32.7 whose vnrighteousnesse is forgi∣uen, and whose sinnes are couered: And S. Iohn, Iesus Christ is the propitiation or couering for our sinnes. Iesus Christ is that onelie place of securitie to hide vs in, from the wrath of God, whereof Dauid speakes. Hee is that mightie one,Psal. 89.19 Gen. 28.12 on whome God alone hath laid helpe. Hee is that ladder, which Iacob sawe standing on earth, which reached to heauen: Hee is the onely way to heauen. And as sure as by our ladders, wee may clime aloft:1. Cor. 4 8 so much more sure∣lie we shall ascende euen to heauen by Iesus Christ. Hee is that true Paschall lamb which is slaine for vs, whose bloud being sprin∣kled
vpon the postes of our houses, by faith: that is in our hearts and vnderstandings, by beléeuing, and in our mouthes by confes∣sing: the destroier shall passe ouer vs. To this agréeth that of S. Iohn:Io. 3.36. Hee that beleeueth in the sonne, hath euerlasting life; but hee that disobeieth him, shall neuer see life: but the wrath of God abi∣deth vpon him. If the bloud of the shadowe were of such force, to saue the sinnefull Israelites: what force shall wee thinke that the bloud of the true lambe it selfe Iesus Christ is?Pro. 30.1 Ithiel and Vcal, that is, God is with vs, and we can do all things: As S. Paul saith, If God be with vs,Rom. 8.31 Phil. 4.13 who can be against vs? And I can doe all thinges by Christ who strengthens me. Hee is that Isaac, that true ioie and laughter:Ioh. 8.56. Io. cap. 20. v. 6 which ioy made Abraham laugh, seeing him but a farre off. He is that high Priest, after whose death euen the murtherer may re∣turne home to his citie againe: and so may all Adams faithfull po∣steritie to Paradise. Hee is the true corke; for they write, that the corke it selfe cannot be drowned, nay if you binde any thing to it, it will not suffer it to be drowned; and it is a verie low tree: So humble and mightie is Iesus Christ, that neither by Sathan, hell or death, hee could be drowned himselfe; no nor as many as are ioyned to him, by a liuely faith, they also cannot be drowned. He is that horne of salua∣tion,Luke 1.69. that hath deliuered vs from the hands of our enemies, that we might now serue God without feare. The enemies of man are sa∣than, sinne, and death: Christ Iesus hath so mightilie deliuered vs, that we néed not now feare anie of these. But all these things, if we beleeue, shall be done vnto vs. For so Christ said alwaies to those hee saued.Mark. 9.23. Mat. 9.28 Doest thou beleeue I canne doe this? And as thou beleeuest, so be it vnto you. And euen so no doubt, hee speakes to vs now: If we beléeue these things; all these things shall be done to vs. No head so saueth the bodie from drowning: no husband so quits his wife from danger of lawe: no garment so perfectlie co∣uers all the imperfectiōs of the body: no place kéepeth any so close from danger: no mightie man so assists and preserues: no ladder so certainlie lifteth vp, and causeth to ascende; no corke so assured∣lie makes swim aloft; no high priest dying, did assure ye returne of the poore vanished murtherer; no Isaac or childe whatsoeuer, hath made anie father euer so merrie or ioifull: As Iesus Christ him∣selfe alone doth al these things for his. If they beléeue these things in their hearts firmelie and vnmooueablie; all the wisdome and power of heads, loue all husbandes, couering of garments, hiding
of places, helpes of men, Iewish passeouers, ladders, corkes, laughters of men whatsoeuer, are but shadowes in comparison of him. But if we beléeue not, none of these shall be done to vs. So that then these are the principall duties of the true church of God, and of all true christians, to build one another in their most holie faith, by the knowledge of the holie scriptures; to pray in the ho∣lie ghost with knowledge, with sighing and groning: to keepe them∣selues in the loue of God; to be sure that God loueth thē, and to looke for the mercy of Iesus Christ to eternall life. But these workes the church of Rome hath neglected, therfore she is not the true church of Christ. Her schollers and followers could not build one another in the faith; because they knew not the scriptures: they praied not in the holie ghost, with knowledge and vnderstanding, but in la∣tine: they kept not themselues in the loue of God, they doubted of their saluation, they were not sure whether God loued them or not: And lastlie, they looked not for the mercie of Iesus Christ to saue them; they trusted in their workes; and manie of them had more workes then they needed, to sel to others. And doth this faith agrée with that faith S. Iude here teacheth? let all men iudge. Concerning good workes, S. Paul teacheth all christians plaine∣lie, that God hath ordained vs to the adoption of sonnes,Ephes. 1.5. through Ie∣sus Christ, according to the good pleasure of his owne will, to the praise of the glorie of his grace. Hee hath not made vs his sons for our workes sake: but according to his own good pleasure, when we were beggers, and void of all goodnesse, that we should be to the praise of his glorie: All the workes we can do should be to glo∣rifie him; who hath bestowed such a great benefit vpon vs. And to the Galathians he  h,Gal. 4.30 that the sonne of the bondwoman shal not in∣herit with the sonne of the free woman: Ismaell, the bondwomans sonne is a figure of the law, Isaac the sonne of promise, is a figure of the gospell: In the inheritance of heauen, Ismaell and Isaac, the law and the gospell, faith and workes, shall not be ioined together. As Isaac; so his inheritance, must come of promise: it must come of faith, it must come of God. In this matter, Abraham must be deade, and Sarah barren. And Ferus of workes writes thus: A good worke is not to be esteemed by outward shew or cost:Ferin 1. epist. Io. ca. 5. but by faith. And S. Paul saith, yt faith cōmeth by the word of God. And this is the true maner of teaching, that first faith be taught, & then works: and yet, that they againe be directed to faith, and trust in the merits
of Christ. And after: Many of the simpler sort trust in their works, & so build on the sand. Thus far Ferus. And in that epistle of Christ to the faithfull soule wee may reade thus:A booke inti∣tuled the Epi∣stle of Christ to the faithful soule, which ye papists haue put forth. Aske alwaies at my handes mercy and grace, not relying on any worke or merit of thine own: but trusting altogether, in that onely worke of redemption which I haue finished for thee, and in that vnspeakeable mercy which I shewed towardes thee. And againe in the same Epistle they faine that Christ speakes thus to the faithfull soule: And yet notwithstanding I wil not haue thee serue me, or to suffer these things in hope of reward but onely of meere loue towards me: I know what reward I wil giue thee; I say I will, because I doe not owe it thee in any other sort, then for that it is my will to bestowe it vpon thee: for all my giftes are of free grace. Thinke not thou therefore of any rewarde, be not so base minded: but thinke of mee with a more noble, louing, and faithfull heart, and submit thy selfe vnto me, euen of meere loue for mine own sake, to endure whatsoeuer my will is to lay vpon thee. And againe, Referre all thinges to me alone, holde this with a resolute and assured minde, and for an infallible principle, that if I do grant thee any good gift, it is giuen meerely without desert, as to an vnfaithful and vnwor∣thie creature. And direct thine eies to thine own vnworthines, (which art of thy selfe meerely nothing) and to thine own dishability, which art able to do nothing. And if thou doest any man good, thou maiest reioice in the good which I did by thee as my instrument: and thou maiest neuer ioyne together thy selfe and my benefit, except when thou comparest my infinite goodnesse, with thy vnspeakeable base∣nesse. And yet for all this, whereas master Beza vpon the Phari∣sies bragging confession, on the 18 of Luke hath giuen this note; Although whatsoeuer we haue we confesse wee haue it of God, not∣withstanding we are reiected of God as arrogant, if wee put neuer so little trust in our workes before God: Index expurgatorius, a booke which the Papistes haue made of late, and by which they controll all mens workes at their pleasure, giueth in charge that that note shall be blotted out quite. It is likelie they which made that book thought wee might lawfullie put some trust in our workes, or else they would not that that note should haue been blotted out. De contempt mundi. li. 2. c. 29Of good workes also Stella a Frier writeth thus: Yea if thou shalt depart from sinne, for this ende onely or principally, that thou maiest obtaine eternal lie, and not for God, thou shalt neuer obtain it. And if thou doest forsake the worlde for this ende onely or princi∣pally,
that thou maiest not go to hell; & not for God: without doubt,A shame for true christians that wil not do so much for loue vnto God, as these papists did for loue vnto thēselues thou shalt go to hell. For this thy end which thou purposest, doth pro∣ceed from the loue of thy selfe. If this be true, then it is likely al∣most all the Monasteries and Abbies here in England, were buil∣ded to a wrong end. They erected them principally for the saluati∣on of their owne soules, because they would not go to hell; as ap∣peareth by their foundations at this day: and then those could not profit them. They procéeded of selfe loue, & not of the loue of God; and therefore by Stella his iudgment without Gods great mercy they should go to hell. We must do all our workes for the glorie and loue of God (as Stella by the force of the scriptures is forced to confesse.) But before the light of the scriptures came into ye world, their blinde guides, and wandring stars, taught men otherwise: That they might build Monasteries and Nunries, for the saluati∣on of their soules. For thus I find recorded in an old booke, which belonged to the Abbey, of Kirksted of the foundation of it. Bee it knowen to all the faithfull, that I Hugh, the sonne of Eudone, haue gi∣uen and granted to the Lord, and Saint Mary, and to the order of the Monkes of Chester, ground to build them an Abbey, in a place which is called Kirksted, &c.Prosalutemea. for my saluation, and the saluation of my wife, and all my heires, and for the soules of my father and mother, and all my parents. And this gift was made before Alexander Bishop of Lin∣colne, and others. Here this ende is onelie expressed, the health of their soules; and the glory of God is left out & forgotten: and thus their teachers taught them. For this was made before the Bishop of Lincolne. And so they haue made them shoot at a wrong mark, and derogate from that great glorie of Iesus Christ, as though he had not sufficiently saued them: and so while they would saue their soules, they endanger their soules. This one point, by a Papists owne iudgment ouerthroweth all Papistes workes. And haue compassion of some in putting difference:Text. Verse 22.23. and other saue with feare pulling them out of the fire, and hate euen the gar∣ments spotted by the flesh.Mat. 24.12.] In the end of the world iniquitie shall haue the vpper hand (as our sauiour prophesieth) and heresie shall preuaile, that if it were possible, the verie elect should be seduced. False Christs & false prophets shall arise; such Christs as the gos∣pell teacheth not; which teach another waie of saluation, then is therein contained: and false prophets,Rom. 1.1. 1. Cor. 15. v. 5.6. which shall preach false do∣ctrine (not according to the scriptures) as the Apostle often addeth,
as a sure testimony to his doctrine; shal come into the world, and shall shew great signes and wonders, not so much in doing anie externall miracles (which none take vpon them to doe at this day) as in their manner of liuing, verie straite and austere: like frogs (as S. Iohn in his Reuelation prophesieth of them) in venturing their liues for their errors,Reu. 16.13. in vsing all manner of meanes to con∣firme their opinions, in all counterfeit holinesse and deuotion: so that if it were possible, the very elect should bee seduced. After the drying of Ephrates, that great riuer and streame of selling par∣dons, which enriched Babylon: there came frogs out of the mouth of the beast, to do wonders before the kings of the earth. Frogs liue hardly in the water, leape here & there, and haue a kinde of voice: They may resemble their Seminaries of late founded by ye Pope, and their preaching and hypocrisie. Out of this generall fire, which shal burne in all places, and from this great heresie & superstition, which now shall cary a zeale with it, like fire; the Apostle here wil∣leth all true christians, that as they haue a care of their owne sal∣uations: so to haue a care of others, as much as in them lieth, and to saue them. And he maketh two sortes: the one to be dealt more gentlie withall, to be pitied; the other with feare, to be pulled out of the fire: of both which sortes, we haue plenty at this day. There are a great many simple soules seduced by the vaine perswasions of others, which themselues are not able to defend their opinions: but are led by others. Such surely are to be pitied, and with al cur∣tesie, to be perswaded, that seeing they are men & haue reason, that they would not stop their eares,Psal. 56.4. like the deafe adder, and that they would vouchsafe to heare, that which should doe their soules good: That they would not in their faith, hange on other mens sléeues, knowing,Heb. 10 38. Mat. 9.22.29. Mat. 10.52. Ier. 31.32. Heb. 8.11. Esay 11.9. Hab. 2.14. that the iust man must liue by his owne faith. They shal all know me (saith God) from the greatest to the smallest. And speaking of the kingdome of Christ, the prophets Esay and Habacucke do af∣firme, that the earth shalbe filled with the knowledge of the glory of the Lord, as the waters couer the sea. Why then, who will nowe bee without knowledge? which the Lord here giueth so plenteously. It shall couer the earth, who will not stoupe downe to put his hand to it?Reu. 21.8. The fearefull soule, God will exclude out of his kingdome. Let no man be affraid to read the scriptures, to pray as the saints of God heretofore haue praied, to hope to be saued as they were. Those thinges that came in since, as Latine praiers, pardons, agnus dei,
images and such like: what neede we care for? the former saints of God were saued without them. Others, which be as it were in the fire through their ouermuch zeale, we are with feare to pull out: telling them with S. Paul,Rom. 10.2. that zeale without knowledge, profiteth nothing. Such a zeale as hee witnesseth the Iewes had, but it was not agreeing with the word of God. They defended the traditions of the fathers,Mat. 15.1. and expounded the scriptures according to them, as manie doe now adaies: but they should rather haue brought their traditions to the scriptures, and haue seene how they had agréed with them. And therefore as our sauiour saide to them of their traditions,Verse 13. euery planting which my heauenly father hath not planted, shall be rooted out: so we may saie to those, that maintaine the traditions of the fathers, and of the church: if their traditions be not planted of God in his word, they shall be rooted out. Such a zeale S. Paul himselfe had,Gal. 1.14. as hee witnesseth; and I profited in the Iewes religion, aboue many of my companions, and of mine owne nation, and was more zealous of the traditions of ye fathers. But this his zeale made him a blasphemer; these his traditions had well nigh drawen him, into hell. And Saint Peter affirmeth, that we were not redeemed with gold or siluer,1. Pet. 1.18. Verse 21. from the vaine conuersation we had receiued of our fathers, but by the pre∣tious bloud as of a lambe immaculate Iesus Christ. But now (saith he) we are borne againe, not of mortall seede but of immortall, that is by the word of the liuing God, which endureth for euer. If then Christ hath redeemed vs from the vaine conuersation, we had receiued of our fathers; let vs beléeue no more such a false schoolemaster: if we be regenerat, by the word of God which endureth for euer, let vs beleeue that, let vs be zealous in that: This is S. Peters lesson. Againe, in the lawe by the prophet Amos, God teacheth the same: Thus saith the Lord, for three transgressions of Iudah, and for foure,Amos 2.4. I will not turne to it: because they haue cast away the law of the Lord, and haue not kept his commandements. And their lies caused them to erre, after the which their fathers haue walked. Their fathers steps, besides the lawe of God, coulde not excuse the Iewes: no more shall ours excuse vs. Let our zeale be therfore according to know∣ledge, grounded vpon Gods word, maintaining it: not the tradi∣tion of the fathers. Papias a diligent searcher, and enquirer of the A∣postles traditions, in ye primitiue church fell into heresies:Euseb. ecel. hist. lib. 3. cap. 39. much more traditions may deceiue vs. Let euerie one take héede what hee
buildeth:1. Cor. 3.17. If any man destroy the tēple of God, him shal God destroy, for the temple of God is holy, which yee are (saieth the Apostle.) The teacher of false doctrine destroieth the temple of God: Oh therfore let euerie man take héede, what he teacheth! The doctrine which is grounded on the scriptures, is sure, it cannot be false: Oh let vs teach that! That which is grounded vpon traditions, may be false: Oh let vs beware that,Psal. 19.8. Rom. 6. v. 17. least we destroy the temple of God! The law of God (saith Dauid) is a perfect lawe, conuerting the soule, and S. Paul calleth the scripture , the platforme or mould of doctrine;Col 2. v. 20. and therefore all doctrine which agreeth not with that, is to be reiected: and to ye Colossians ; why are you led by the conceites and opinions of men concerning the elements of the world and outward thinges; as though now the worship of God consisted in them, in ouermuch pinching and pining the body, as the Iesuites doe, or in humblenesse of minde and worshipping of angels, as now also the catholiques teach. These our head Iesus Christ commandeth not; these are the opinions of men; these haue a shew of holinesse in voluntary religion: but in Christes religion, because he neuer taught them, they ought as superfluous to bee quite cut off and repelled. Such worshipping of angels, through humility; and such excessiue fasting, through ouermuch deuotion or rather superstition, began to spring (as it should séeme) as a part of Gods worship and religion, euen in the Apostles daies: but since it hath ouerspread almost the whole church, and quite choked all the true worship; which, according to our sauiours doctrine, should be only of God, and in spirit and truth. This only place if it be well marked, ouerthroweth the verie principall groundes of poperie: which is, a voluntary religion and seruice of God besides his word, and a wor∣shipping of angels and saints, and a religious & excessiue abstinence. For there is a measure in al things, which the gospell doth not take away,2. Cor. 10.13. as in doctrine: we will not reioice in thiges aboue our mea∣sure, saith the Apostle: so in fasting, in reproouing sins, and in all other spirituall exercises  (saith S. Paul:Rom. 6. v. 19.) I speake according to mans hability. And in the epistle to the christian soule, thus they faine that Christ doth speake to his spouse: I do not hold my selfe satisfied, though thou doest serue me, seeke me, and binde thy selfe to heare me: but I will haue thee serue me in such sort, as my will is to be serued, that is I will haue thee cleane forsake thine owne will, yea though it be in a thing vertuous and commendable; and to
follow my will in another thing, which is not halfe so good, but see∣meth to be vile and of no valew. Here we maie plainlie sée by their owne confession, that Gods will in his worship is chiefelie to bée respected: and how shall we learne that, but in his word? And that all voluntarie worship is condemned against this his will, séeme it to vs neuer so commendable, and full of deuotion. If we will be led by traditions: the church of Ethiopia hath a certaine booke,Mat. Dresserus in oratione de eccl. Aethiopicae. which they suppose was made of all the Apostles, when they were together at Ierusalem, and they call this booke in their language Manda and Abetylis, and they beléeue that all things written in it are as true as the gospell: And in this booke is contained that priestes may haue wiues: so that, both ecclesiasticall and ciuill persons, after they haue companied with their wiues, must abstaine from the church 24. houres. Also it containeth other ceremonies of womens purifications; and that a Synod ought twise euery yeare to bee kept in the church, &c. Why should wee beléeue the Popes traditions vnwritten, more then these which are written? Why should wee beléeue the church of Rome more, then of Ethiopia? For of the whole church Christ spake, that hell gates should not preuaile against it: And S. Paul, that it is the piller of truth, as well the church of E∣thiopia, as of Asia; as well the church of Ephesus,Epiph. haer. 27. where Timothy was Bishop, as of Rome, where (as some thinke) Peter and Paul were Bishops, not Peter onlie. Irenaeus of the traditions of the Iewes writes thus:Lib. 4. ca. 35. The traditi∣ons of the elders, which they faine that they obserued according to the lawe, were contrary to the lawe which was giuen by Moses. And therefore Esay saith, thy hucksters do mingle wine with water, shew∣ing, that with the tart precept of God, the elders did mingle their waterish tradition, that is setting vp an adulterous law, and that con∣trary to the law: as our Lord made manifest, saying vnto them, why doe ye transgresse the commandement of God, for your owne tradi∣tion? And they haue not onely broken the law of God, by transgressi∣on mingling wine with water; but they haue also on the contrarie part, set vp their owne lawe, which till this time is called the Pharises law. In the which they take somethings away, and some things they adde, & expound as they list, which their doctors vse especially which traditions whilest they would maintaine, they would not bee subiect to the lawe of God, instructing them of the comming of Christ; but also they reprooued the Lorde for healing on the sabaoth day: The
which thing truely, as we haue said before, the lawe did not forbid. Here we maie see by Irenaeus opinion, what the Iewes did: And haue not the papists done the like? Do they not saie, that their tra∣ditions are grounded on the scripture? haue they not added things of their owne, more then Gods word commanded, as the Iewes did the keeping of the sabaoth: so they haue added their pilgrima∣ges, and infinite such like? haue they not expounded ye scriptures, as they list? And as the Iewes at the first comming of Christ, maintaining their traditions, would not beléeue the word of God, which plainly prooued, that he was comen: Do not they so likewise now, against his second comming, maintaining their traditions of Enoch and Elias, and of Antichrist, that he shall be borne of the tribe of Dan, withstand the scriptures, and saie that Christ shall not come as yet? Text.And putting a difference, haue compassion on some &c. And hate euen the garment spotted by the flesh.] That is hate not onely the wicked works of the flesh: but also, all things which are nigh vnto it: all prouocations or intisements therunto. And so S. Paul willeth that all christians should abstaine not only from all euill,2. Thes. 5.22. but from all shew of euill: as though he should say, take héede to your selues, hate the garment spotted of the flesh.Ephes 4. v. 22.23.24 Col. 3. v. 8. & 12 The outward workes and conuersation of the olde man, are compared to a garment, as also the new man and his workes: The flesh still lusteth against the spi∣rit: hate the old man with his deedes, put him off; put on the newe man Iesus Christ. Those things that proceede from the hart, are they which defile a man (saith our sauiour) as euill thoughts,Mat. 15.19. murthers, a∣dulteries, fornications, &c. hate the garment, that is, the outwarde conuersation, & defiled life of the flesh, in your selues, and in your brethren;Reu. 7.15. séeke to wash it, with all saints in the bloud of the lamb. This garment spotted of the flesh too many weare at this day: that is, follow the lusts of the flesh in all their dealings: the whole course of their life, their conuersation, as a garment, is stained with the lusts of the flesh: whatsoeuer the flesh desireth it hath. That which we will doe,Rom. 7.15. Col. 3 5. we doe; which ought not to bee done. The flesh should be made a seruant: The spirit should beare the rule. The flesh should be mortified by fasting, and praier, and holy exercises: The spirit should be strengthened with sacraments, and holy me∣ditations.Text. Verse 24. To him that is able to keepe you free from sinne.] Here is the con∣clusion
of the whole epistle, with a thanksgiuing:1. Cor. 1.4. Ephes. 1.3. 1. Pet. 1.3. the Apostle here∣in not following ye other Apostles, who alwaies vsed to giue thāks in the beginning: and they all following our sauiour Christ, who often made confession and gaue thankes to God his father,Mat. 26.30. Mat. 11.33. Luke 10.21. euen for his meate, for the faith and knowledge of his hearers: teaching thereby all christians to do the like. And here first he stirreth vp all christians to this thankefulnesse, by two notable reasons; because God alone can keepe vs free from sinne: and can make vs appeare before his glory with ioy. So Noe found grace in the eies of the Lord,Gen. 6.8. that he was not drowned with the old world:20.6. so God kept Abime∣lech that he should not sinne against him, and that he should not once touch Abrahams wife:21 19. so God opened the eies of Agar in the wilder∣nesse, and she saw a well of water, and she gaue her childe drinke: so when as Lot prolonged the time,19.16. and was loath to go out of Sodom (the Lord being mercifull to him) they brought him forth, and set him without the citie. If man trust in himselfe, he cannot chuse but be ashamed and confounded. Vnlesse God order our goings,Psal. 94.18. & hold them vp: we must needes fall downe flat, euen into the pit of de∣struction:Psal. 119.35. vnlesse he make vs walke in the waies of his comman∣dements, the best of vs shall go astray, shall walke by-waies:Psal. 80.18.119.25 v. 88. Psal. 143.11. vn∣lesse he quicken vs, as Dauid often praieth; how slacke and howe slow shall we be in doing his commandements? Therefore euery one must daily lift vp his heart to God, & call to him for grace: that he may auoide the snares of sathan, the waies of sinners, and that he may be able to do that which pleaseth the Lorde. We are not more iust then Noah, more zealous then Lot, more wise then Abi∣melech, more quicke sighted then Agar: God alone must keepe vs from sinning against him, wee must finde fauour in his sight, or else we shall be drowned with the vanities and pleasures of this wicked world. He must leade vs with his holy spirit, or else wee shall all be burned, with this fire of heresie, and impietie the Apo∣stle Iude here speaketh of. Vnlesse he open our eies, we shall not be able to sée any thing that is good for vs. But some will saie, If God be able to kéepe vs from sin, why then there be some that are pure, that neuer sinne. But that followeth not: For though God be able to doe it, yet he giueth that grace to none in this life, least he should be too proud: He will haue vs humble;Gen. 22.1. Iob. 1.20. Mat. 26.33. hee will haue all mouthes stopped; he will exercise our faith, whether we do beléeue his promise or no, of free remission of sinnes in his sonne Iesus
Christ: whether we being sinners, dare ioyfully vpon this his pro∣mise, euen venture our liues. For these and such other causes, God suffers many often times to fall, and to feele their owne infirmi∣ties, and frailties. Text. Verse 25.That is, to God onely wise, our sauiour, be glory and maiestie, and dominion and power, both now and for euer, Amen.] This place also prooueth that our sauiour is God, and he addeth two other cau∣ses, why we should giue him praise: because he is the wisedome of God, he hath declared God vnto vs, which was in the bosome of the father.Io. 1.18. Io. 15.15. Mat. 1.21. Ephes. 4.8. Psal. 34.19. 1. Cor. 15.57. 1. Io. 3.3. Hence forth he calleth vs, not seruants, but friendes: be∣cause all things, he hath heard of his father, hee hath made knowen vnto vs. He is our sauiour, which first saueth vs from our sins, which saueth vs from our spirituall enemies the deuill, and all his angelles, which saueth vs from all perils and dangers in this life, which saueth vs from death eternall, and from hell it selfe: which alone setteth vs in the sight of his glory, with ioy. And shal we not praise, and mag∣nifie this our gratious, and mercifull, and louing, and most migh∣tie God and sauiour? Let vs therefore yéeld to him, all maiestie, and magnificence: as doing things wonderfull, passing all mans reach and reason. Let vs giue him glorie and praise for these his wonderfull workes, let vs yeelde to him dominion, and empire, in this world ouer all Turkes, Tyrants and wicked christians: nay ouer all the deuils of hell,Psal. 135.6. who hath power to doe whatsoeuer plea∣seth him. To this our most wise, mighty, and louing sauiour Ie∣sus Christ, with God the father, and the holy Ghost; one God, immortall, inuisible, and onely wise: be all honour, and glorie, power, dominion, and maiestie: both now and for euer. Amen, Amen. FINIS.
